[Editorial note (2026-04-11): Two references to "Castle Daggerdale" in the Situation Report section (~Ches 28th 1481 DR) of this file have been corrected to "Castle Radiance." The original wiki text used "Castle Daggerdale" for Luminous Whitegate's title and in Tunbridge's speech about distance from Cormyr; both clearly refer to Castle Radiance. All other "Castle Daggerdale" references in this file are genuine. See Archive Search Report - Castle Daggerdale.md.]

The Daggerdale Chronicle –
14th and 15th Centuries Dale Reconning
DDC - Forword from an Itinerant Scholar
An account of the major political and religious happenings in and around Daggerdale from 1367 – 1482 DR, compiled by Grafton Fitzdecker, Independent Scholar.


Well Met, Reader:
This is the forward to the first edition of this book. I say ‘first edition’, because as I write this, I’ve heard that the Black Network is once again operating at full capacity in the Moonsea region, and just yesterday I spoke to a man that claimed to work for the Drurginz Trading company, here in Waterdeep. As you read on, you’ll learn that I am right to be surprised to hear this name, and you’ll guess, as I have, that this story is not yet concluded.

The edition that you are reading was compiled by commission from Candlekeep, last winter. There were much greater works of writing that I desired to access in the Keep, and their price for this access was a compilation of primary sources regarding beholder activity on the Sword Coast in the late 14th century DR. My handler at the Keep knew that I sometimes dealt with the deranged Waterdhavian elf, Steele, around whom many parts of this story are woven. Indeed, this very same character will appear in many of the primary sources you are about to enjoy.

Getting anything from Steele is usually a fuss, but on the particular occasion that I chose to darken his door, he was already in one of his legendary black moods. I was cautioned to give him space and time, but I pressed, and was rewarded. When I asked him what he knew about beholders, he told me “Apparently not enough”, and he veritably threw a box of papers, books and scrolls at me. Looking quickly at the mess about me, I could see that there were journals, maps, notes and other collateral relating to beholders, Zhents, Harpers, and a town by the name of Daggerdale, that I hadn’t heard of before that moment.

I motioned towards the mess inquisitively, as if to say, “may I?”, and he threw a dagger by my head, which stuck in the door behind me. “I’ll take that as an “of course, that’s why I threw it at you, now sod off” and thank you presently. I’ll bring it all back as soon as I’ve made copies.” At this point, Steele was brimming over.
“Don’t you dare, you little pig! Take it and get from my site forever!”
I gathered it hastily, and followed his instructions, though I have some burning questions that only he can answer. Those will have to wait, maybe for the next edition, eh?

The box was full of everything I needed to know about the topic at hand, and I wasn’t long in guessing why the Keep was so interested in it, and why Steele had it all together and ready to be flung at my person. The most recent notes were from 1481, and while centred mostly on distant Daggerdale, some

names and locations were circled in red with angry annotations in Silver Elven, no doubt Steele’s own hand. Linkages between the beholder and drow schemes in the Sword Coast in the 14th century were now being seen in Daggerdale in the 15th. I envy the Long-Lived races their ability to plan over decades and centuries, and admit that I find their machinations mind-boggling in their scope.

I have learned that events that seemed to start in the 1360’s are playing out new chapters currently on the other side of the continent, and that their persistence is the source of Steele’s rage. He has waged war on these forces for over 100 years, and he is no closer to victory.

How my research into these events turned from a commission to a passion is explained by one simple fact; that I have been in love with a woman named Sarah Estelmer for some 35 years. We studied together in Waterdeep as children, and I have loved her since grammar school. She never knew this, as for some reason she is the only soul on Toril for whom my loquaciousness falters, and our paths kept us apart for long tracts of time, with only brief intermissions. Sarah, always my academic superior, found herself in the Order of the Tome, while I have been a rogue scholar all my life.

Toward the bottom of the box of documents gracefully provided by Steele, is Sarah’s Report from 1481, entitled ‘The Shadow Lifted’, which I have reproduced here in its entirety. It was heartwarming to see that she too was a rogue in her own Order, and that she lived a full life with meaningful friendships, and even love. I in fact read her report before anything else, and this changed the nature of my investigation from beholders, drow, and Zhents on the Sword Coast in the 14th century, to the same and other matters in Daggerdale in the 15th. The latter is more interesting given our proximity to it, the value of the source documents from that era, and through my declared bias for the writings of an amazing woman.

While I expect that Candlekeep will be a little tilted at my deviation from their specification, I will boldly and presently claim that this is the best work I’ve ever put together. As you’ll read, the documents that I present below are not all from one box of papers from an insane elf. I have spent every waking moment of the last twelve months working on this publication, including a trip to Daggerdale to gather more information.

As far as I know, this is the most detailed and comprehensive account of the affairs mentioned in the title, and I suspect this publication will be a useful source of information and intelligence for those that need to get involved in the current resurgence of the Zhents and the Netherese on either side of Anuaroch (or Netheril…)

Finally, just a note on format; Below are dozens of primary sources that I have transcribed and put into a format suitable for a Gondsman’s Press. The original documents are stored at the Keep with my first printing, and it is my hope that the Keep will produce copies and circulate it far and wide. For now I shall confess, probably to the dismay of the Keep, that I indeed have made three copies of this work; one for Candlekeep, one for myself, and one for the amiable and helpful Administrator of the Whitecloaks in Daggerdale, without whom many holes would remain in the chronicle.

For most sources, I have given some notes on context (where I got it from, how reliable the source might be, and so on). I have given some commentary on the more interesting parts of the chronicle, even though I was advised not to.

If you are reading this out of pure academic interest, I hope you’ll enjoy every word at a leisurely pace. If, on the other hand, you are reading this to prepare for conflict in Daggerdale, know you this; I haven’t left anything in this account that might not save your life in some cave, castle, or forest in the Dales.
Forewarned is forearmed. At your service,
Grafton Fitzdecker 1st Alturiak, 1483 DR

DDC - Addendum to the Forward
Wherein your humble author shares a conversation at the Old Skull Inn, in Shadowdale with three venerable gentlemen.
GFD Notes:
I’ll grant you that this is an unusual sort of entry for a book like this, but I thought it captured perfectly the essence of the dales. This is a conversation I had directed at me in the taproom of the Old Skull Inn, which is on the main road in Shadowdale. The caravan I had hitched a ride with from Cormyr was stopping here for the night, before keeping on to Liberty Hill, and I had a chance to sit and write with a full mug of beer.

I couldn’t help but sit and listen to the locals. Their regional accent was so strong I found it hard to understand them, but when they started talking about Daggerdale, I was obliged to listen; these were local men with views I’d never heard before and were my first real impressions of what Daggerdale and the dales are really about. And they were happy to share a table, a mug, and a story with me.
Please enjoy, fair reader!
-GFD
“Just plain un-dales-like, I says” is what I must have heard a dozen times in the tap room at the Old Skull Inn after my caravan-master announced that we were on our way to Daggerdale. Sitting at a table with three local septuagenarians, I was given a colourful accounting of the history and character of Daggerdale.

“Those folk up there just aren’t right,” one old codger named Harald was remarking, when he was interrupted by one of his two cronies, Zeb.

“Never damned have been, what’s more! It’s all ‘Sun God keep you’ and ‘Sun God damn you’ just nows, but it weren’t long ago but half of ‘em worshipped the dog-humping shadow bitch herself! They’s just damned…damned…damned…I dunno…”

The third old man, Diff, chimed in, filling in for his stammering comrade “…extreme…” he said slowly and with a pointing finger and squinting eyes.

Zeb nodded assent and continued his line of thought. “Extreme. That’s what I was saying. Don’t know how to takes just a bits of this, and a bits of that. Always haves to jump in head damned first, whethers it’s damned good or damned evil, damned right or damned wrong. Where’s else could you finds the sodding Zhents dugs in for so many decades…”

“Or vampires! That’s what started it all, see” Harald exclaimed. “In my day, they called it Sorrow Dale, for all the misery that was clutching the place…” Harald was saying when Zeb cut him off.

“Oh dammit, Harald! They’s never damned called it damned Sorrow Dale or damned Misery Dale or goddamned Damned Dale, and nuthin’ else you says they dids, not in your damned day! She’s been Dagger damned dale the whole damned time. But yers right about the vampires. That was in my great, great, great grand daddy’s day, and he used to say the damned blood suckers sucked the, sucked the…sucked the…sucked the…I dunno…”

Diff squinted his eyes and wagged an accusing finger at Zeb, and slowly said “…soul…sucked the soul outa the valley herself.” He nodded slowly with a look of conviction as though he had announced something as indisputable as the time of day.

Harald nodded at his friend, and then turned to me. “When Diff’s right, Diff’s right. Never been the same since, and that was hundreds of years ago. They lived in uncertain times up there before…Uncertain Times. That’s why they called it ‘Dagger Dale’; because you used to have to keep a dagger in each boot, because you never knew which side you was going to get it from.”

Zeb interrupted Harald again, saying “They called it Dagger damned dale because of the magic pig- sticker theys used to kill the damned vampires, professor Harald. Anyhows, that ain’t neithers here nor goddamned theres now any goddamned way. They mays as well calls it ‘Sunny damned dale’ or ‘Amaunator’s Arse Farts Sunshine Dale’ for all the rantings and preachings they does up theres. They goes from vampires to damned Sun Gods, from Zhents to damned Harpers…they just seems to goes…from, well…well…well…”
“Extremes” Diff drawled out slowly.
“Diff’s right again, friend. You need a fill-up on that tankard?” Harald called for more beer for the table, but I could see that he and his two cronies were just pretending to sip at theirs. “Where was we? Oh yeah; here’s the thing about Daggerdale you have to get your head around. They never knew peace up there. Probably never will. When the rest of us was ploughing our fields and our wives in peace and comfort, the folk up in the Tesh Valley were still fighting with goblins and ogres and giants and that sort of thing, and when that wasn’t enough, they had evil wizards, evil Zhents, vampires, beholders, evil paladins, and anything else evil you can think of to chew on’em, from the inside-out half the time, and that hardened the lot of ‘em.” Diff and Zeb just looked down into the tankards they were clutching on the table, and kept listening while nodding in either assent or oncoming slumber.

“Yup. It hardened ‘em, I says” Harlad continued. “When the real Hard Times came, well, they should’a just moved on. No one would have said nuthin’, or talked ‘em down. But they stuck it out; through dead gods, armies of orcs and goblins, plagues, the Netherese, all of it. They stuck it out. Now they got

Amaunator up there, and things run like a gnomish clock, or so I’m told, but you’ll hear a lot of us say they aren’t like regular dales folk. But the truth is; they are the most dales-like among us. There’s nothin’ more makes a man of the dales than stickin’ it out.”

Moonsea Region - Circa 1367 DR

DDC – Chapter Three – Forword and Summary
Wherein the players and events of the 14th century that affected present-dale Daggerdale are neatly inventoried.

You’ll notice, fair reader, that I have omitted Chapters one and two from this chronicle. That is because I never wrote them, and the source materials are now difficult to find.

Chapter one would begin around 975 DR, with the vampiric infestation and the building of Castle Daggerdale. While there are enough wild and conflicting stories from this era to fill a book (indeed, I’ve seen just such a book), there are no source documents left, and none left to give firsthand accounts (though there might be somewhere deep in Cormanthor or Myth Drannor, but they are presently occupied).

Chapter two is much nearer our time. It would begin in the 1350’s with Randall Mourn, and probably end in 1371 with him hanging from the Bridge in Daggerfalls. This was the first Zhent occupation of

Daggerdale, and though short-lived, it created a draw for the Zhents to the area, much like the first ant arriving at a picnic.

Chapter three, which I have written (or collected and written) begins on the western shores of this continent, in the city of Waterdeep, more than 3000 miles away from Daggerdale. It begins here, because this was the first place I could find source materials relating to Zhents and beholders, who would sculpt the dale into what it is today.

The opening of the chapter is a collection of documents relating to some rogues (the Company of the Red Herring) who would ultimately evolve into the heroes that come to liberate Daggerdale in late 1372, though after many confusing iterations.

The Company of the Red Herring ran missions for a wizard named Thagdul, who worked either with, against, or for one or more beholders. The whole thing is quite confusing, but here are the salient actors in the play;

The Company of the Red Herring (CRH) – Adventurers and mischief-makers that get entangled with the beholders and Zhents, and unwittingly set off a chain of events that ultimately ends Zhent trading domination on either side of Anauroch.

The Company of the Eastern Storm – Made up of members of the CRH, Harpers, and other adventurers, this company sets out from Waterdeep in 1371, crosses Anauroch, and liberates Daggerdale. Their long and heroic tale is summarized as neatly as I can make it in DDC – 1372 – 2: The Daggerdale Expedition.

The Zhentarim – Two competing companies of Zhents in Waterdeep with ties to Zhent leaders in the Moonsea region. This organization grows from a troublesome and effective trading network to a military power, all while colluding with beholders much of the time, and drow some of the time.

Company Drurginz – Lead by the wizard Thagdul, who claimed that he and the company were all a front for the Harpers. This has never been proven or disproved to my satisfaction. This company and Thagdul seem to have been working with the beholder Xulla, who will come in and out of this chronicle many times.

Company Dalael – Based in Waterdeep with offices in Menzoberanzan, these are surface- dwelling drow that inculcated themselves into the nobility of Waterdeep and acted as a third- party in the struggle between the Zhents and the adventurers, ultimately contributing to the end of Zhentarim power in Waterdeep, which they would not share.

The most important theme to take away from Chapter Three, especially for readers mortal like myself, is that there are some schemes that take decades and centuries to hatch. We have not heard the last of Xulla, or the Dalael, maybe not even of Thagdul, though he was but a mortal man.

The rest you’ll have to read for yourself. Do pour yourself a warm cup of tea before you dive into DDC – 1372 – 2: The Daggerdale Expedition. Though this is one of the best parts of the chronicle, and the one for which I am most proud, I failed in my attempt to be brief.
-GFD

DDC – 1371 - 1: Dalael Correspondence – Mirtul 1371
A Note found in a drow safehouse by the Company of the Red Herring, Early Mirtul, 1371 DR.
Notes from GFD:
This was the piece of paper at the very top of the pile that Steele threw at me. Attached to it was a note in his hand saying “It really starts and ends with this”.

This note was originally recovered by the Waterdeep vigilantes that would come to be known as the Company of the Red Herring, lead by one Garth Shanks. It was found in a safehouse that belonged to the drow, which the mage Thagdul hired the dim-witted adventurers to raid. They subsequently got in over their heads…
Father Dalael, Quevin and Isilith;
Business on the surface is recovering. We are currently allied with a Zhent trading company called Company Ersgul (Coat of Arms inset); the Company is one of Fzoul’s major arms in the west, and falls directly under the control of one of his most (or perhaps least) trusted, and powerful allies: Xulla (mark inset, though I doubt you would forget it), whom you know.

The treachery of the Zhents is as abundant as we have heard. Xulla gives us bits of information, and frequently has us raiding holdings, which we took to belong to Ersgul.

Company Ersgul, as we have recently learned, is pitted against another, called Company Drurginz. I take this to be an arm of Manshoon, but I am uncertain. I have also inset their shield. I am suspicious that they may have connections to one known as Zantiid. Only by the grace of Vhaeraun was I able to learn Zantiid’s mark, and live to tell of it (but that is quite another story). Please send back any word of Zantiid’s politics, if you’ve any knowledge of them.

The family is good. Corrina is pregnant, and Arlos has become trusting of us again. Having just returned from a long vacation in Cormyr. I have amassed a great amount of information about this society, and I am sending it to you. Some tomes are aged (for human work) and will require our sages to
interpret. The language of the human race is such a malleable thing.
I must go now; this message will (I hope) be finding it’s way to you in the hands of a new (I am as equally surprised as you) Vhaeraunite. He is worthy of our trust. Upon receipt of this message, please consider sending more of our people. The climate is once again favourable, I assure you. Soon, our numbers will be needed again.
Vhaeraun shall remember, Quelar Dalael

DDC - 1371 - 2 : Remarks on the Company of the Red Herring
Winter, 1372. By Jalthor Murlyn, Captain of the Night Watch, Dockward
GFD Notes:
This seems to be a fairly good history of how a small group of ‘adventurers’ would get involved with, and ultimately lead the resistance against, a very complicated plot between beholders, Zhents, drow and other unsavoury characters.
-GFD
“The only knowledge I have of the Company of the Red Herring concerns the months between Greengrass and Harvestide of 1371. They did the City a couple of favours, but on the whole we’d have been better off without them.

“From what I understand, the company centred on a Dockward orphan that had more than a few run-ins with the Watch in my patrol days. Garth Shanks was always something of a character, as I recall, getting up to mischief with Szarah Mudge’s boy, Tomas, when he wasn’t cutting purses in the markets. He was always one to put on a show whenever the authorities had any questions. Eventually, he cleaned himself up enough to land a job at a respectable, if not strictly legitimate, shop as an errand boy. Do you know Serpentil’s Books and Folios? Jannaxil Serpentil sells maps and books, usually authentic, to a fairly large customer base, but most of his business is on the shady side, dealing intelligence and worse to the usual suspects. From what I understand, Serpentil was dealing fairly often in those days with Quevin Dalael, in his surface guise, of course.

“I imagine they were circumspect enough that Shanks never got beyond the usual suspicions that anyone of at least moderate intelligence would have dealing with Serpentil. One of Shanks’ first jobs for Serpentil was connected to this Dalael business – a ‘delivery’ to Castleward. The package turned out to be an incendiary device of some kind, and I hear the hit really got under the skin of one of the Zhent traders who were active in the city at that time. That was pretty much it for Garth’s association with Serpentil.

“The company came together following that business. Ildar Orsabbas was a fop who owned a Seaward trade outlet called Orsabbas’ Fine Imports. The idiot fancied himself a bit of a crime boss, calling himself the “Duke of Darkness” or something of the like. We were on to his operation, but he more often than not pointed us in the direction of more useful quarry. At any rate, he had a pet elf named Ellyth, an ambitious piece, if misguided in her choice of mentors. Her uncle was a good man, for an elf, a bladesinger named Gilthanas, but I hear he came to a bad end not too long after that.

“I understand that she was there on Greengrass eve, when Orsabbas met the rogue Teskul for

dinner. Orsabbas was selling Teskul some information on a shipment of swords enchanted by a Banite cult in Luskan. The shipment was moving out of the Helmfast warehouse in Dockward Greengrass night – the swords, in two crates packed with sugar cane, were going to move under the cover of the celebration. Teskul said he couldn’t do much with the information, but Ellyth was sharp enough to pick up on their conversation. Ellyth had heard a bit about the Helmfasts from one of her … colleagues – a bit named Ezrelda, and like the rookie she was, she came right out and offered to put together some

people for the job. That’s really where it all started. Ellyth got in touch with her uncle and her crazy cousin Esperel, Esperel got a hold of Garth, and Garth brought in Tomas.

“What Orsabbas didn’t know, and Ellyth didn’t find out until too late, was that it was Teskul’s boss that had arranged the shipment. They say Beshaba is just Tymora on a bad day.

“Teskul’s boss had arranged the shipment with Chuldan Helmfast, who managed the warehouse for his family. Helmfast’s is usually pretty well looked after, good light, guards on the roof, etc. Won’t keep out the mages, but it’s good enough to stop hoods like Garth and Esperel. The logs indicate that the cargo was to be loaded on to a privately-owned cog called The Misty.

“Tomas told me all this, or most of it, at least, shortly before his own death some months later. The five of them decided to ambush the shipment and make a switch during the commotion of the festival. It wasn’t hard for a couple of Dockward lads to pull together a wagon and team, and I’m not surprised they were able to make the switch without too much trouble. At least, no immediate trouble. This is all a prelude, remember, to the real show.

“Once they got back to Garth’s house, that’s when it all came apart, or together, depending on your perspective. They were so excited about the heist, that there wasn’t much more than a token attempt to keep their guard up. A man on the roof took out Esperel pretty quick, and the rest of them didn’t have much to say to their door being beat down by four thugs. Right behind them were Teskul and his boss, a Zhent named Thagdul who ran the Drurginz Trading Company. Drurginz was a semi-legit trading company with connections to the Moonsea region, but we know that they probably ran contraband through Skullport more often than not. Garth recognized him as someone who wasn’t too pleased at Serpentil’s stunt with the fire, and had a pretty good idea where this was going. It turned out that he’d had Teskul build up about as much of a dossier on this bunch as you could get.

“If you knew this bunch, you’d have expected a hopeless fight to break out. But Ellyth saw something in the doorway that pretty much took the fight out of them that day.

(From GFD: It was the purple-eyed beholder, Zantiid, I am led to believe, or an apparition of it.)

“Thagdul knew he had them over a barrel. It didn’t take much convincing to get Ellyth and Garth to agree to run a few ‘errands’ for Drurginz, doing some corporate sabotage on another Zhent organization in the city, Company Ersgul. Tomas and Esperel followed suit, but Gilthanas knew the scene and wouldn’t have any of it. No one ever proved that Gilthanas’ death had anything to do with the Zhents, but I’m a druid if they had nothing to do with it.”
DDC - 1372 - 1: Decisions at Phaulkonmere
30 Tarsakh, 1372 DR, Agamemnon's Journal: Summary of a meeting at Phaulkonmere Villa in Waterdeep, wherein it is decided how to address the problem of the Zhents, the drow and the beholders.
Notes from GFD:
This might be one of the most interesting records in the collection. These pages were transcribed by Steele himself, as the journal was not present. He notes that the original journal was ‘procured through great tragedy and misunderstanding’. I’d love

to ask him about that, and if he knows what happened to Agamemnon, but that will have to wait.

For the benefit of your understanding, fair reader, know that Agamemnon was a wizard of some accomplishment who was a known Harper, and perhaps the last in Waterdeep in the 14th century.
We hope for his safe return…
-GFD


30 Tarsakh, 1372
We met, the lot of us, at Phaulkonmere to discuss the Zhent and Drow threat to the City and to points beyond. Many were there because they had been involved in this mess for so long. Others were there through a sense of duty to their fellow man. Some were there because they were seeking such things as adventure, fame and fortune. Some were there for even more selfish reasons. And some were there for the simple reason of pursuing vengeance, and with good cause.

Present at Phaulkonmere that day were the following (and I have pre-emptively clumped them into the companies they would form, though they were a chaotic rabble at the start of the meeting);
Neverwinter Team:
· Maevri of Rashemen - Witch
· Oberon – Ancient warrior awoken from stasis (must spend some time with him)
· Rufus Larrigan – Principled were-creature
· Oliver Windemchester – ‘Master of Human Nature’ by his own claims – a bard?
· Beljuril of Azuth – Priest of Azuth and very capable wizard
Daggerdale Team:
· Boregar the Wanderer – a ranger or fighter of great ability
· Maturin Horgath – Paladin of Ilmater from the distant East (GFD Note; ‘St. Maturin’ in the 15th C.)
· Hannibal Felthian
· Mourn “Raven”Raventree – Noble warrior of Waterdeep
· Sparrow – Arcane assassin? (GFD Note: Ultimately ends the mage Yarkul)
· Corrina – (GFD Note: Not the same as the Dalael bride, but we’ll hear of her later)
Waterdeep Team:
· Rychel Voordan – Master of the rooftops

· Zechary Mudge – Dockward tough
· Garth Shanks – Ringleader of the CRH, principled but undisciplined (or else a master of misdirection)
· Esperel – Insane elf, very reckless and unreliable
· Jafar – Unhinged wizard, not sure what side he’s on…
· Brandel – Eleven archer of incredible strength
Also present were myself, and the last Phaulkon (who’s family estate we were meeting in, though now owned by some legal trickery by the Company of the Red Herring), Jeryth Phaulkon.

Thagdul was conspicuously absent from this meeting, but Jafar insisted that he represented Thagdul. This did nothing if not make worse the CRH member’s opinion of this wayward mage.

(GFD Note: Thagdul MUST have been in Daggerdale at the time, given everything his faction of Zhents accomplished there.)

Events current and past were discussed. From the East, Boregar brought a report most grim. The Zhents had taken over Daggerfalls once again, and Randall Mourn himself had been hung from the new bridge over the Tesh River. Yarkul had been put in place as ruler of Daggerfalls and Daggerdale, and his rule was enforced by an elite mercenary company known as The Fist. Further, churches to Bane and Iyachtu Xvim had been built, and the town appeared to be taken for good.

Worse yet, the Zhents had hundreds of slaves toiling in a number of mines. It was suspected that Hobb (an ally of the CRH who was kidnapped earlier in the year) was imprisoned in one of these slave

camps. Outposts had been built in Anauroch, and Zhent caravans were coming and going through the Great Sand Sea with little difficulty, and the town of Daggerfalls was growing rich off the trade through its gates, as it is the gateway to Anauroch from the East.

All trade through the more traditional routes (such as through the gap at Tilverton and then through Cormyr) had ceased because of a couple reasons. Tilverton had been overrun by goblinoid hordes again, and a Zhent banner was flying from the city’s walls. Cormyr was involved in a costly war with the Sembians over a border-mountain that Mithral had been found in. The resurrection of Bane had much to do with the problems in the East, but the Zhents seemed also to have played the hand that was dealt them in a most cunning manner there.

In summary, almost all trade between the Western Heartlands, The North, Amn, Tethyr and Calimshan was coming through the desert upon Zhent cargo trains, or paying huge fees to use their roads and buy safe passage. The Zhents were growing wealthy, and most of this wealth seemed to be pouring into Daggerfalls, where extensive fortifications were being constructed. Clearly, an expedition would have to be sent east to set things straight. Yarkul, at least, would die. Or so was the pledge of Sparrow.

In the North, a second objective was set. Malkor, too, would have to be brought down and the roads made safe once again. The work of the Road Mage was not complete, and Beljuril and Rufus had made a pledge that they would honor. Our organization was in great peril, and its survival rested upon the deeds of these heroes.

Finally, the City of Splendours itself became the last objective. It was clear that the Zhents had too much influence in this city, and indeed, much of their wealth and power structure was now located here. With the Company Dalael as another huge problem to be fixed, perhaps the group should have assigned a more capable task force to this objective. Be that as it may, here are the stories of these three teams…

Daggerdale Map - Circa 1364

DDC – 1372 – 2: The Daggerdale Expedition
A collection of notes and narrative by Luminous Whitegate, Submitted to the Yellow Abbey in 1439.
GFD Notes:
On both sides of Netheril/Anauraoch, you will find books, hear songs, and meet children named after the heroes that set out from Waterdeep in 1372 to liberate Daggerfalls. This account was put together by Lunimous Whitegate himself, though he likely had help from a number of clerks at the Abbey. Still, at the same time as this was being submitted, he was building Morningstar Cathedral up at Castle Radiance, and fighting off incursions of orcs and Netherese spies.

Fortunately, as he wrote this, there were still many people alive who remembered what had happened 60 years earlier, and he was better friends with a few dwarves in Town than he would admit to (even when I spoke to him on my visit to the Castle). I

expect that much of this narrative between primary sources is from Dalak Quickaxes, who still runs a public house over 100 years after these events (which were the inciting incident for him to set up a business and retire from adventuring in the first place).

Luminous tells the rest better than I do, so I will leave it at that, and bid you happy reading!
-GFD
Departure
The most reliable part of the story as I understand it really starts at the end of Mirtul, 1372, as the Daggerdale Expedition (DE) approaches Loudwater, nearing the mountains that separate the Western Heartlands from what was the vast desert, Anauroch. Much happened between the gates of Waterdeep and the long inland-journey they made, but that part of the story I am not familiar with.

Though others would join later on, the DE at this point was composed of the following members;
• Boregar the Wanderer – a ranger or fighter of great ability
• Maturin Horgath – Paladin of Ilmater from the distant East (GFD Note; ‘St. Maturin’ in the 15th C.)
• Mourn “Raven”Raventree – Noble warrior of Waterdeep
• Sparrow – Arcane assassin? (GFD Note: Ultimately ends the mage Yarkul)
• Corrina – (GFD Note: Not the same as the Dalael bride, but we’ll hear of her later)

• Dalak Quickaxes – Dwarven battlerage, now Proprietor of the public house in town

Loudwater was the last civilized place on the East Road at this point in the journey, and the DE paused in this solemn town to re-supply. All stayed in Loudwater for a time, except Boregar who argued that there was no time to waste. And so, he lived up to his name and left early, to wander the East Road.

It is important to note that the DE had already suffered loss; Mourn Raventree was killed by assassins on the road before Loudwater, but was thankfully replaced by the famous swordsman, Dorian of Sembia.

Why Dorian fell in with the DE is lost to history, but the impact he had on our community is not.

The rest of the DE left a couple days afterward, and upon their travel along the East Road, they received magical word from Beljuril that the Neverwinter Company had been victorious. The grim news about the death of the Harper Initiate Rufus is taken hard by Boregar, who was starting to suspect some greater plot, and fears that someone has infiltrated his order, or sold them out.

The DE comes to Dekanter, and finds that the town is under quite a bit of construction, and that they make no efforts to hide their allegiance; banners of the Zhentarim and of Cyric fly freely, and there is clearly much slavery here. The DE was loathe to leave this abomination behind, but a great task had been set before them, and so they pressed on, the desert just a day away.

Heading into Anauroch, the DE is disheartened to find that they have traveled less than twenty miles after about four days, and soon after that they learn that they have traveled in a circle for a long time.

Sand storms called ‘Azirla Dahab’ plague their passage, and it seems as if though the desert was not going to let them pass.
Meeting Grandfather
On the 16th of Kythorn, the DE, and Maturin especially, had an encounter with fate. It was on this day that they encountered Grandfather, a great werelion, and his consorts on a rocky heel jutting out of the hot golden sands. Grandfather demanded tribute in flesh for passage, but none was offered.

Grandfather and his consorts attacked, and in a long battle with the creatures, Maturin, Boregar, Dorian and Sparrow were all wounded by the great werelion. Maturin, especially, took wounds numerous and grievous enough that there was little doubt that he had been infected. Dorian was spared his death by Tymora alone, as Grandfather’s great maw found his neck, and flung his limp body into the sands before ripping at the guts of the dangerous battlerager, effectively ending his career. In the end, they managed to repel the creatures, but their wounds were severe. Here are the recorded thoughts of Maturin the Grey from the next day;


St. Maturin’s Journal, 17 Kythorn 1372

It is less than two months since we left Waterdeep, yet it seems that years have been stripped from my life. Our party has been five days in the desert, and we have covered less than twenty miles.

The desert wind whips my robes about me, the sand stings my eyes and open wounds. Sharp pains shoot through my skull. My vision blurs. The bite of the Lion-Creature, the harsh and blinding light of the desert sun, and my own internal turmoil are almost more than I can bear.
I endure.
We are stopped for a rest on the path leading us towards salvation or damnation. The first Zhent- tainted oasis lies over a day’s travel ahead. We will find no respite. What we might have paid for will be denied us- my money is gone. Our horses are gone.
I glance around.
Dorian is crouched on his haunches beside me, coughing silently and clutching his ruined throat. I watch him spit blood onto the sand. The moisture evaporates immediately, leaving a faint discoloration on the pale sands.
The heat presses down.
He writes with a shaky hand on a crumpled page of vellum torn from his depleted journal. Precious inks stain his hands. He hands me the note.
‘We must continue’.
Sparrow helps Corrina into the saddle. She lurches in the saddle. Her face is sullen. She glances at me, and blame, bitterness and anger spew from her eyes. Her cheeks are sunken. Her hair is lank. She fears for her unborn child.

Boregar pushes ahead. He was withdrawn into himself. Since Raven’s death he has been distant and driven. I cannot catch his eye. His boots crunch the sand.
I follow.
Warburden marches beside me. Even this most noble creature seems defeated. He tolerates Dalak with no complaint. He carries our supplies. He carries our armour. He carries the folly of my pride.
The party carries the marks of my sin.
O Lord Ilmater! It was Your Will that I saw the evil in the noble-looking Lion. It was Your Will that I fight It. But the Creature did not act in evil! Tribute for safe passage. It did not seek war, but peace. It is peace that I long for, and it is peace that You denied me!

I remember fighting in the Bloodstone armies against the brigand forces of the Lich-King of Damara. I remember the blood, the anger, the hatred, the pain and the sorrow. I vowed to stop the wars. I vowed to heal, to struggle to save lives, not take them. I vowed to ease suffering wherever it existed in the Realms.

But yesterday, my Lord, You showed me Evil. Yesterday, my Lord, You asked for Blood. Why did it sue for peace, O Lord? Why did it seek to spare us? I feel the blood course through my veins. Lycanthropy. I touch my tongue to my teeth. Are they sharper? My skin itches. Tomorrow night is the full moon. Is this Your Will?
I feel the eyes of the party on me. They fear me.
I fear myself.
A gust of wind. Warburden rears up. Dalak pitches to the ground. I reach out a hand to restraint the mount, then reach down to help my comrade. His wounds have opened. I tend to them carefully, reassuring him. He grunts stoically, but I see the worry in his eyes. I know that my dread writhes equally within him.

Ignorance and suspicion eat at our bellies. Tomorrow night we’ll know. Tomorrow night we’ll be tested. For now we continue.
For now we endure.
lmater, why have You forsaken me?


This was the beginning of the great Story of St. Maturin, though he had no way of knowing it at the time. His suffering had only just begun.
Infection
The next night, the DE arrived at the first Zhent oasis-outpost, Vaerthyl. Before they would leave this outpost, Dorian, Sparrow, Maturin and Boregar turn into were-lions and ripped the place and everyone

in it apart. The battle-rager also helped in the destruction, but in the end, he was met by Maturin in his lion-man form, who ripped Dalak apart, nearly killing him.

The next day dawned with little hope for the heroes. The whirlwind of bloodshed, violence and destruction was but a foggy memory. The four new lycanthropes found themselves each waking up alone and naked in an unfamiliar part of the desert. Most managed to find their way back to the oasis, and there they found the horrific scene of slaughter. Men were ripped to shreds and many had clearly been feasted upon. This caused the four infected members of the party to become sick to their stomachs. Zhents and slaves alike had all been slaughtered. Horses had been butchered, walls clawed through. The entire place was in absolute ruin. Corrina had gone missing, and never again was she heard from. Her story ends in obscurity here.
Now they were five.
A great pyre was made to burn all the corpses, and great piles of weapons and such were made. Dalak was found, and tended to by Maturin all day, but things did not look good for the battle-rager. Though the remainder of the company looked for their missing comrade, at length they all solemnly admitted that it was time to move on. The road continued, and so did their quest. They left behind a companion that day, and many of the items they treasured and needed for the journey. But Maturin left behind everything. Ilmater turned His back on Maturin that day, and the Paladin began his long lonesome trial.

The remaining four members would have perished if not for a fortuitous meeting with a benign tribe of Neshaba.

(GFD Notes: There are still some of these tribes roaming the planes and the fringe-bits of desert that remain. It might be possible that this group is still out there somewhere, avoiding the Netherese.)

These desert nomads were quick to help the DE, despite what all had heard about the people of this land. It was not until much later that it became clear why. This particular band bore the symbol of the Green Eye of Muir’Quaggoth, and they must have known about the infection in the veins of the DE.

After days of wandering the road, they came to the second oasis-outpost, Olomaa. They decided not to tackle this one head on, but in their attempt to circumvent the place, they were intercepted by the 14th company of Fist mercenaries. They managed to destroy this company nearly to the man, but they learned that these twenty men were of elite training, and quick thinking.
The Wanderer and the Quests
Days later, as they trekked through the sands, the DE encountered another ‘golden death’ storm. This was the worst one they would endure, and it was bad enough to sunder the company. Dorian was blown away hopelessly in the storm, and the DE lost almost all of the valuable gear they had managed to retain after the slaughter in Vaerthyl. When the storm finally subsided, Dorian and Sparrow were long gone, and no tracks or trails were there to be followed. The desert had seemingly just swallowed the men up mercilessly.

Three days later, and two nights before the full moon would rise again, a boon came from the desert, and hope was put into the hearts of all, but especially in the heart of the Forsaken Paladin. A wanderer came from the desert. A man who seemed a beggar came over the dunes, and he helped along the

weakened Dorian, who he had found the day before. Dorian had been staring at the sun and hallucinating, drawing his final breaths. The wanderer followed the birds of carrion and rescued him.

This man, Shildevan the Wanderer, was a holy man of Ilmater. He was on a holy pilgrimage to harsh lands everywhere, and the hand of Ilmater guided him to the DE. He managed to bring all but Sparrow back together again.
Now they were four.
Shildevan had favour enough with Ilmater that he could cure the horrible lycanthropic sickness in the veins of the infected men, but all had to agree to a quest to receive this blessing.

Dorian was to eliminate the threat posed by the Beholders, and that he could not accept any pay for this mission. Though the clever Sembian agreed to not accept a single ‘copper piece’ for the entire quest, he did not realize the scope of his challenge. Indeed, his was the only quest that would bring him back to the streets of Waterdeep over a year later, to equally dire struggles.

Boregar was commanded to be true to his friends, but to return and set right all the wrong he had left behind. This seemed like a great task given all the evil they had turned their cheeks on during the journey so far.

Maturin was commanded to free the slaves of Dagger Dale, and then to return to the desert to slay the Chosen of Muir’Quaggoth, Grandfather.

So it was that these three men were cured of their infection, and were set upon the greatest quests of their lives.


Delivery into the Dales
Back on the road, the DE began to make solid headway after their fortuitous encounter with the holy wanderer. They came to Addas Babar, and secretly traded with some slaves for food and water. A small fight ensued, and Boregar was taken down by the mage Farim, the only survivor of the Vaerthyl massacre. Though he was later rescued by his companions, the Gond Pistol artefact that Boregar had wielded was not recovered.

Days later the DE once again encounter the Nashaba, and this time their headman Kabina assigns a guide to them, so that they may go through the desert quicker. After many more days of travel and many more pounds had come off the frames of the travelers, the Desert’s Mouth Mountains came into view in the East, and the hearts of the travelers leapt.

It should be said that all the obstacles, challenges, misery and atrophy of the desert have not been detailed in this brief summary. The journey was one of constant loss and doubt, and in recorded history it was not known that four lonesome travelers could make such a remarkable journey and live to tell about it, until these four came out alive.

While traveling in the bad lands between the desert and the mountains, the four encounter the ogre- mage Yin Xu. They find they are unable to hurt the creature before he is able to escape using his gaseous form, but he is also outmatched.

After crossing the mountains, the four head down into the fertile valley that is the border region between Dagger Dale and Shadow Dale. The hearts of these men were renewed, though their bodies were just beginning to recover from their journey. They traveled off the roads, as they were weakened and had insufficient tools for making war, and knew that the Fist would be close by.

They encountered a group of Zhent scouts as they neared Shadow Dale, but they were rescued by a group of elves of the Region, who Boregar was familiar with. The elves then escorted the DE to Shadow Dale, where they arrived on the 4th of Eleint.

Even the Boregar was noticeably thin when the four turned up at the Old Skull Inn. The others had the look of skeletons, and all were haggard, filthy, and wretched. After they were cleaned up, and donned some new clothing, they weren’t long fitting in at the taproom. Crowds flocked around them (despite their want for some peace) and asked many questions of the men who had come from the desert to liberate the slaves of Dagger Dale.

One of the guests at the inn that night was the noble fop, William Cormaeril. This man had come from Cormyr, and claimed that he was the rightful heir to rule Dagger Dale with the death of Randal Mourn. He had a small retinue that included a half dozen Purple Dragons, and he boasted that he would liberate Dagger Dale from the treacherous Zhents, but he was not taken seriously by anyone who heard him.
Also traveling with him is his wife, Medea Rowan, and their two sons.
GFD Notes: Medea left the dale in early 1373 with her sons, to return to her ancestral home in Cormyr. A year later, she sent a letter to her husband, William, explaining that their sons both died in a horrible fire. Cormaeril fell into a deep depression and was killed in the field a few months later on a regular patrol. Though I have not seen the reports, he is said to have fought poorly, seeming to welcome death, and reunification with his sons, who were the last of his line. I have been outside his small mausoleum, and can confirm that he died Flamerule 20th, 1374. With that, the Cormaeril line ended, as well as their claims to Daggerdale. This is all fairly common lore in the dale.

What is uncommon lore, as I discovered in an obscure watch-report in the Abbey, is that his mausoleum was broken into in 1425, but the thieves were stopped by the watch. In the report, they mention that a magistrate gathered up the things the thieves stole and carried them off, rather than re-interring them. I have indeed seen a box in the Historic Wing labelled ‘Wm. Cormaeril’, but I was not granted access to it…
-GFD
That night peace would not come easily. The half-elf assassin Dragon entered the inn and made an attempt on Dorian’s life, but was not successful. She managed to escape before any harm could befall her. Though she scorched and skewered Dorian, her most grievous wound was upon his heart. The fool was beginning to fall for her.
First Battle of Ananathar’s Dell – Eleint 5
The next morning, the epic scale of the events in the Dales was made greater yet again. The order of the Broken Blade, including 8 knights of Tempus and their retinue, rode into Shadow Dale with full pomp and ceremony. They, too, announce that they will be heading to Dagger Dale to put an end to the

villainy there, and that they will not wait a day. Their leader Sir Durnbold implores Cormaeril to ride with them and take his rightful seat after a valiant battle, but his cowardice was great, and the Broken Blade rode out that very morning without him.

As the Paladins of Tempus went west out of town, all took it as a good sign. But then, the heavens gave ill portent. A green and black vortex was seen in the sky, and it inspires panic in the village. As the sun was coming up that morning and the vortex was swirling, the Church of Lathander began its bifurcation. A fragment of the church lead by Rewel Thunderstorm, the second-in-command of the church in Shadow Dale walks out on High Dawnlord Cassimar’s sermon. Thunderstorm insists that the vortex is a sign, and that they should have sent all available Lathanderites with Sir Durnbold to help in their noble quest.

By a reckoning put together by an Oghman in Waterdeep much later, (GFD Note: Kennyth Thames) this was the morning that the slaves in the Dagger Hills Mine uncovered the beholder tablets, and the vortex was likely the manifestation of some god associated with the beholders.

That night, good news and bad both come to the DE in the inn. Sparrow has emerged from the desert! He explains that he was also helped by the nomads of the desert, and that magic sustained him. He brings ill news though. That day he passed by the site of an ambush, and reports that the Order of the Broken Blade have all been slain in ambush less than 20 miles from Shadow Dale. As this news spreads, so does the bifurcation of the local church of Lathander.

The next morning, all surviving DE members (now they are five again!) are together and recuperated. They plan to re-supply today, and to begin their toil. That morning, though, more trumpets are heard, and Shadow Dale once again seems to be the stage for a play of the Gods. The holy trinity of Tyr, Torm and Ilmater march their brightest lances and blades into Shadow Dale that morning. The following orders were present;
• Order of the Golden Lion (Torm), led by Sir Gethard Soulbright
• Order of the Lambent Rose (Ilmater), led by Sir Lexinauth and Father Eisley of St.Collin’s Abbey. Both of these men refused to speak with Maturin.
• Knights of Justice (Tyr), led by Sir Wildermot Silverlance
One of the men in the tent-train of the OLR was Revered Brother Turin, who was an old friend of Maturin’s. The two had served in the army together in Damara, fighting the Lich King of Vaasa. Turin was glad to see his old friend, despite what politics where at work.

Word that day comes to Boregar from the local wood elves that Yarkul was spotted at the Dagger Hills mine the day before, perhaps accompanied by a beholder. They took something large and heavy from the mine and marched away. Sparrow insists that the trail least cold lies in that direction, but there were many questions about which task to start first. There were 3 slave mines to free, and the town itself to liberate. The choices were many, and there were many political considerations now as well, with knights of three orders in town.

The Second Battle at Anathar’s Dell – Eleint 7
The night of Eleint the 6th, a great conference was held in the Twisted Tower. Lord Amcathra hosted a meeting with the DE, the knights of the order, and the two leaders of the bifurcated church of Lathander. There were many discussions as to what was the best course of action. As well, Sir Soulbright sued for some troops from Amcathra, but he could spare none. The only Shadow Dalesmen that would accompany the war party would be a select few priests of Lathander from the Thunderstorm faction of the church of Lathander.

Early on the morning of the 7th, a war host rode out of Shadowdale the likes of which had not been seen in a score of years. The three orders, accompanied by the DE set out. They had a retinue of priests of Ilmater and Lathander in tow, as well as a few Shadowdale men who decided to follow with what arms they could muster. Cassamar and Amcathra met them on the west edge of town, wished them luck and apologized that they could offer no further aid.

Twenty miles and most of the day later, the war host came to Anathar’s Dell. There, they found the small walled farm village burnt to the ground, and the bodies of the slain Knights of the Broken Blade strewn about, defiled and rotting. They were put upon a pyre and given rites by the many holy men there. Their impetuousness was also cursed at that time. The Broken Blade had marched with the Trinity for many days, but would not abide the pace of the Ilmater tent-train, and thus found their enemies two days too soon.

While the smoke billowed into the sky, an enemy host gathered on either side of the dell. To the north, the Knights of the Black Gauntlet gathered. This is the militant order of the church of Bane, and had just recently been assembled after the resurrection of Bane. To the south, the more formidable Brothers of the Black Fist, led by Baron Drake assembled. This militant arm of the church of Iyachtu Xvim had been growing for years at this point, and their main headquarters and training ground was located in Dagger Falls at Brotherhood tower.

A brutal battle was joined, as the forces of good clashed with the forces of evil. Paladins of many gods struggled against each other, and in the end it is difficult to say who won or lost. The Knights of the Black Gauntlet were utterly destroyed, but the Brothers of the Black Fist were merely repelled. Baron Drake slew several paladins of all three orders himself however, before he thought it prudent to lead his forces from the field. In the end, the DE and the surviving members of the war host of the Trinity held the field, but at great cost. And Baron Drake was far from defeated. He laughed as his demon-steed bore him from the field.

The battle rager Dalak was nearly killed that day as well. The Baron delivered a blow that re-eviscerated the battle rager, and though it did not kill him, it put an end to his fighting days. He spent the rest of this story convalescing in Shadowdale.

(GFD Notes: I’ve met Dalak many times, and discussed much. He won’t talk to strangers about this time, though. Don’t ask.)

Anathar’s Dell is often referred to as Paladin’s Grave these days, for the 21 Paladins that were buried there.

It is important to note that years later, a great cenotaph was erected there. However, as the Spellplague hastened (and still hastens) the growth of Cormanthor, the cenotaph and the knights were moved to my grandfather’s farm before I was born.-LW

It is late into the night before the war host marches again, back to Shadowdale, in acceptance of defeat and setback.
Preparations for War – Eleint 8-10
The next day was a day of many activities. A council is assembled again. When the survivors of Anathar’s Dell describe what happened to Lord Amcathra, he voices his concern over the absence of the militant order of the Church of Cyric, which is also strong in Dagger Falls. Cassamar and Thunderstorm get into a heated argument over signs from Lathander, and the right and wrong course of action, and Thunderstorm goes so far as to say that Cyric was not at the battle because he was at work in the heart of Cassamar, who should have sent troops to the battle.

The Boregar set out that day to get word from his allies in the woods and surrounding country side. He visited the significant other in his life, Silve Silverhand. This Harper and daughter of the famed Storm Silverhand was a long-time lover of Boregar. The two had a lasting but intermittent relationship. The two lived harsh lives that kept them both on the road and apart, doing deeds they received little thanks for. This day, they met as lovers and as colleagues. Silve had long ago planted a man in Dagger Falls and had been receiving correspondence from him for some time. She received the following bloodstained letter, which she wished for Amcathra to see;

Lord Amcathra:
This is all I have learned about the military in Dagger falls:
Yarkul is the head of everything, military included.
There are two branches of the military: the Garrison and the Fist The Garrison
Led by Commander (formerly Constable) Tren Noemfor (IV epaulets).
There are 10 companies of 20 men, plus a captain (III) and 2 sergeants (II) each.

• 1st Garrison is led by Captain Denethor, Randal Morn’s captor. They are always at the Tower.

• 2nd Garrison, led by Captain Innisworth. It is stationed at the First mine (Rainhill - LW).

• 3rd Garrison is stationed at the Second mine (Chillholm). It is led by Captain Aegis, rumoured to be a half-ogre. Both sergeants are his sons. (This is now known as Whitegate Mine, after my grandfather liberated and exploited it - LW)

• 4th Garrison is led by Captain Braehl. It is stationed at the Third mine in the Dagger Hills (Tyrant’s Mine – LW). This company is exclusively made up of crazy Cyricists.
• 5th through 8th Garrisons are stationed in town.
• 9th Garrison is a cavalry company. It patrols the East Road. It is led by Captain Vargul, an aged veteran of this area’s wars.
• 10th Garrison is also a cavalry company. It patrols the South Road.


The Fist
25 Companies, mostly of 20 men each.
• 1st Company is led by Commander Harrington (IV), also the Commander of the Fist Mercenary Company itself. It is stationed at the Tower.

• 2nd Company Garlunk’s Roughriders, Mostly half-orcs led by the Villain of Scardale. It patrols the East Road.

• 3rd Company Blacktooth’s Hussars, highly seasoned riders, mostly half-orcs. This company patrols the South Road.

• 4th Company Sandalwood’s Roughriders, Sandalwood is known as the Murderer of Mirabar. He is a nasty half-elf with infallible aim.

• 5th Company Gumbottom’s Guard, a unit comprised of 10 hill giants. They are stationed at the gates to the Eastern Bailey

• 6th Company Klangedon’s Hammers, A terror squad of ogres dispatched for specific duties

• 7th Company Gadbout’s Fangs, Captain Gadbout is known to have killed 2 sheriffs in the Dales. Another ‘specialist’ squad, mostly of orcs.

• 8th Company Dunvegan’s Corsairs, all the finest archers in the Fist are in this company, stationed in the tower.
• 9th Company (Cyricists) stationed at the third mine
• 10th Company (former Red Plumes), Stationed at the first mine.
• 11th Company (former Purple Dragons) stationed at the second mine
• 12th Company, led by Yin-Xu. A group of ogre scouts (?!) led by the relentless Yin-Xu. This company is known to have done a great deal of damage to The Circle, and is hunting the Wanderer
• 13th to 20th Companies Stationed in Anauroch
   • 21st to 25th Companies in training at the Citadel of the Raven Other Considerations:

The Naug-Adar (GFD Note: Naug-Adar are Zhent Mages) are Yarkul’s mage-lackeys. They command companies of the Fist and Garrison and are individually responsible for assigning ‘priests’ to their company. I believe there are at least ten of them.

Brothers of the Black Fist; this is the militant wing of the Church of Iyachtu Xvim. It is led by the enigmatic Baron Drake, and I believe they are outside the chain of command in Dagger Falls.

Daggerfalls has never seen so many terrifying soldiers in all its days. They are matched by the new fortifications built by an army of slaves, all of it the fruit of the Zhent trade route through the desert.
I will follow up when I can…



I have transcribed this note in its entirety, mostly because I’m a military man myself and I admire the detail of this report. But also to illustrate the power that had come to Daggerdale at the behest of the Zhents, and their determination to keep it.

Another note was also delivered from the spy in Dagger Falls some days later that said the following;


Eleint 9, 1372 DR Friends,
The word in Dagger Falls is that the Elves of Cormanthor have marched upon the mine in the Dagger Hills and razed it to the ground.

It is said that Captain Braehl and the entire 4th Garrison are slain, and that the elves subsequently marched all the slaves into a pit and burnt them alive.

This seems unlikely to me (the elf-portion of this story, at any rate), but by all accounts the Dagger Hills mine is closed.
Please confirm what you can.
Also, today there was open fighting in the streets between the local Xvimites – the residents of the Brotherhood Tower (a knightly order of Xvimites) – and a bunch of Cyricists.

Before the 6th Fist Company broke them up (their knees and arms included), I did hear one of the priests of Cyric yell “Your silly order is but a thumb on Cyric’s Hand.” This priest subsequently lost his head, and the knight completed his rebuttal by saying “Your treacherous god has not had all of us killed.”

I suppose this is related to the battle of Anathar’s Dell, but I am unsure. It is exceedingly tense here right now.

The Tyrant’s Mine – Eleint 10-12
Boregar took the note and delved into the woods to meet with his elven connection. He is given a magical elven cloak as a gift, and learns about Yin Xu, the ogre mage that they fought in the desert. It seems that Yin Xu is now stationed on the border region between the two dales, but Boregar suspects that Yin Xu has been tasked with getting rid of the DE.

On this day, however, William Cormaeril sets out on his expedition. He boldly claims that he will have Dagger Falls liberated in but a few days. The council is re-ordered, and Amcathra expresses his frustration with the events unfolding here. He implores the two factions of the church of Lathander to reunite, but they will not. He is frustrated that each side will not agree to march together upon Daggerfalls and that if the forces of good continue to attack in bits and pieces, then that is how they shall end up. The council then decides that more reasonable goals have to be pursued. Thus, they set the 3rd mine as their first objective. Sparrow had a visionary dream on the night of the vortex that he reveals at this time. He believes that Mystra was guiding him to the 3rd mine to pick up the trail least cold.

The DE sets out for the 3rd mine (in the Dagger Hills, where the tablets were found). Today we know this as the Tyrant’s Mine, but I’m not sure when that started, or by whom.

On Eleint 11, they arrive at the mine and find it pretty much abandoned. Doing some exploration, they find a pile of bones in a pit, but the night is getting long. That night, Maturin receives a visitation from ‘Torm’ in his dreams. A great pillar of skulls is building into the sky, and the death will only stop if he delves into the pit to find his answerers. ‘Torm’ tells Maturin to follow the Tablets at all costs. This puts him at a crossroads however, as following the tablets would put him further from his quest and would leave Dagger Dale in the same condition it is in now.

The DE spends the early morning the next day exploring the great pit, and finds beneath the bones a pair of great doors carved with beholder writing. Sparrow uses divinations and sees visions of 20 men

(probably followers of Cyric) lead into the pit, where they fight 4 beholder-like monsters. He also has a vision of two huge tablets being taken from the mine. Any further divination beyond the doors is impossible, and they are completely impervious to magic, possibly made of Starmetal. They find they are unable to open them in any manner, and quickly decide it is time to free some slaves.
Exodus from Chillholm – Eleint 13-21
A couple of nights later, the DE is close to the Chillholm mine. That night, Sparrow sneaks into the barracks and cleanly assassinates the mage running the operation. Sparrow overhears that the Fist will be leaving in the morning, but that the Garrison Captain there is upset about that, with all the orc sightings of late.

Early the next morning, 11th Company of Fist ride out of the mine, and shortly after, the DE strikes. In the drawn-out battle, the Garrison there is slain almost to the man, and 6 score of slaves are rescued. That night, the exodus to Shadowdale begins.

The next day while the exodus marches overland to Shadowdale, Boregar and Dorian make a guerilla attack against the First at Rain Hill. They light off a powder keg in the barracks and destroy almost an entire company of Fist before making their escape.

The exodus back to Shadowdale was not eventless. Maturin had his hands full tending to the failing health of the liberated men, and despite his best care, many could not survive the dangerous travel home.

On the night of the 19th, the 2nd, 3rd and 4th companies of Fist caught up with the exodus at Liberty Hill (it wasn’t called that yet, of course), and though losses were great for both sides, the Fist did flee the field of battle, and the liberation of those slaves was complete. Of course, my grand father was one of those at the battle, and his account of it can be found elsewhere.
(GFD Notes: c.f. DDC – 1398 – 1: Life of the White Saint)
Toward the end of the Exodus, the group is accompanied by a large retinue of elves, to ensure their safe delivery to Shadowdale. Boregar was informed that the Rain Hill mine had been recently abandoned on Yarkul’s orders.

On the 21st of Eleint the exodus was complete, and over 100 men and women who were slaves in the mine were delivered to Shadow Dale. The remainder of the Lambent Order of the Rose set up many medicine tents and worked around the clock to heal those from the mine.

On this day, it was also discovered that there were spies in Shadowdale who were quickly hanged.

Messages begin to go back and forth, and Dorian himself gets involved in this. Though none of the DE besides Dorian knew about this letter, it would later resurface…


Dragon my love,

I think our little show at the Old Skull went off well. However, you should have sealed the deal before you let me go.

Your searing black eyes have left me absolutely mesmerized. I fear that having had the beautiful honour of meeting my match (and better) has left me reconsidering my allegiances.

I cannot in good conscience bring myself to do harm to one as gorgeous as yourself. No, alas, my heart is yours. My insides ‘burn’ with desire to see your radiant countenance, but just one more time.

My dear, sweet, beautiful Dragon, it is for my love of you that I betray my side in this terrible war to bring you this one piece of news:

Thagdul knows about the doors in the mine, and its contents. As I write this, he plots and positions to overthrow you and your father for control of Daggerdale.

If you do not trust me, remember that my companions and I are well-connected with Thagdul and his Waterdeep agents.
Protect yourself and your interests, my darling.


With deepest love,


Dorian of Shadowdale



Although no one considered this at the time, it seems as though Dorian’s loyalties were contested. This is a terrible portent for what was in store for my family many decades later.

The next day, a mage from Daggerdale came to deliver this message to Amacathra and the people of Shadowdale;


I, Yarkul, Lord of Daggerdale and ruler of Dagger Falls,
Do fully and whole heartedly offer a treaty of non-aggression with the people of Daggerdale.

For my part of this Treaty, I declare I will not hinder the travel of any citizen of Daggerdale, nor any other person or their property, traveling along the Trade Way, nor will I keep patrols on the Trade Way, nor will I keep patrols on the Trade Way beyond a distance of 10 mi. south of the Daggerdale Valley Border.

I will also free any citizen enslaved in my Dale and allow them to go or stay as it suits them, and make what reparations, in coin, that I can to return them to their former mode of life.

On the part of Shadowdale, it’s Lord and agents, we simply ask that it’s aggression towards Daggerdale cease.

I will hold up my end until such time as I get a rejection from the Lord of Daggerdale, or until aggressive action is taken against Daggerdale by the above mentioned parties.

I hope that we can make some arrangement to meet and discuss these affairs and begin to heal the wounds that my careless leadership has caused.

I hope, in the long run, to develop a mutually beneficial relationship between our two Dales, in which citizens will travel and trade freely.

These terms I offer truly and whole heartedly, along with an apology for the damage that my leadership caused in its budding year.
Please send a written reply with my man. Yours in Peace,
Yarkul
Eleint 23, 1372 DR.



This letter and the wizard bearing it caused a tremendous uproar in the council. Heated argument over how to proceed followed, but the end the DE swore to travel to Daggerfalls, and to meet with Yarkul to hold him to account.
Exodus from Daggerfalls & Arcane Assassins – Eleint 24-26
The DE leaves for Dagger Falls with this mage, named Grimspite that day. Arriving in Daggerfalls the next day, Boregar is surprised to see the place. It barely resembles the Daggerfalls he saw the year before. A great wall has been constructed of solid stone all the way around, and a beautiful, fortified bridge has been built across the Tesh. From the bridge, many bodies hang, including the corpse of Randal Mourn, which has a slight necromantic dweomer upon it.

Inside the new Eastern Bailey, there are hundreds of slaves gathered. They look frightened and malnourished, but they are not being abused. The DE decides to take the slaves out of town right away, rather than confronting Yarkul as a group, and Maturin begins the exodus of these people.

Sparrow stays behind in Dagger Falls, and that night he gets into a spell duel with Yarkul after sneaking into the Tower, and kills him. This thankfully is the end of Yarkul’s part in the story. However, the next night Sparrow returns to investigate the Tower to see how the power vacuum is filling in, and is set upon by another wizard and an assassin/Zhent spy named Venosar. He is magically bested by Thagdul (who if any knew was present in the dale, had not revealed it), and his had is cut off by Venosar.

Despite being at the mercy of Thagdul and his assassin, Sparrow finds himself waking up in a medicine tent in Shadowdale. To this day, none know how he went from falling into unconsciousness at the Tower, to waking in the Shadowdale, but his sanctity with Mystra likely has something to do with it (and his escape from Anauroch a month earlier, as you will recall). He had a dream vision from Mystra that

he is to establish a church in Daggerfalls, and in the dream, he still has his hand. Waking up, he finds that his hand is gone, but that a spell-fire blue spectre of it appears when he works the Weave.

It takes two days to get the freed slaves back to Shadowdale. They are added to the charge of the overworked priests and retinue of Ilmater, and Maturin stays up all the night to help in treating them.

Boregar finds that a note from his man in Daggerfalls has reached him, a little late;


Eleint 21, 1372 DR Friends,
Good tidings! The bulk of the Fist has left Daggerdale. I confess that I did not personally see them leave, but I did see the remainder of the 2nd and 4th Companies ride in two nights ago, and the 3rd Company did not go on patrol as usual.

It is morning, and I can find no evidence of any of the Fist Companies normally present, except the 5th and the 9th. The 9th is here still, in either disguise or in decommission, as they do not wear the Fist uniforms.

Also, the 2nd Garrison marched in with all the slaves from the mine last night. The slaves are being held in the Eastern Bailey, and are being treated in an uncharacteristically kind manner.
Congratulations on whatever it is you have done. I remain on active duty.

This day is a busy one. First of all, Dragon sneaks into town to meet with Dorian. She explains to him that the Xvimites are quite pissed off at Sparrow, and that an attempt is going to be made on his life soon. She explains that a demon, the former concubine of Yarkul, currently lives in Brotherhood Tower, and will be coming for him some day soon. The two exchange their first kiss, and she departs.

Dorian rushes to locate Sparrow, who he learns was brought in late last night to the medicine tents by unknown parties. Going to his tent, he learns that a child delivered a message to the priest as soon as he woke up, and that he met with a beautiful woman outside. Sparrow and the woman departed. He goes immediately to The Old Skull Inn, and there meets with Gaebril Tremalkin for the first time. Many people in the tavern saw Sparrow go upstairs with the beautiful woman, and Dorian rushes up the stairs and starts knocking doors down. Gaebril follows, and soon they find a succubus over the prostrate form of Sparrow on a bed. The two repel the demon, who flies away out the same broken skylight that Dragon herself escaped from days ago. Sparrow comes to, recovering from the effects of powerful enchantments. He seems to be intact, but his path now seems clear, and all are ready to depart for Daggerfalls.

It cannot be overlooked that Gaebril Tremalkin appears in the story at this time; great forces of good have poured into the dales; many knightly orders fought and perished, and the differences in the zeniths of joy (hundreds of slaves being liberated) and nadirs of misery (knights being slain by evil counterparts in the scores) made exactly the fertile breeding ground for the introduction of the cult of Shar that would plague us for so many years afterward.

Although there are no records to support my theory, I suspect it was around this time that Gaebril began preaching his obscene faith to the masses in the tents, and his transformation in history into the Black Saint began.


Brotherhood Tower and the Company of the Eastern Storm – Eleint 27
That night, in the Old Skull, the DE is joined by Garrick who has just come in from the south road after a long and brutal trek. He has with him the ranger Eiron, a gamekeeper for a powerful Waterdeep family that has interests here in the Dales. Garrick has come to help his friend Boregar, and also brings in the Dark Paladin, Gaebril who he has been friends with for years.

That very night, the DE sets out for Daggerfalls, with fire in their veins and their wills fortified to their task. Not long out of Shadowdale, an elven runner delivers a message for Boregar that reads as follows;


Eleint 25, 1372 DR
Things are changing here very quickly now, and it is difficult to keep track of it all.

I was personally looking on yesterday when you and your friends marched those hundreds of slaves out of the Eastern Bailey and south to freedom. My heart leapt for the first time since I started this assignment, and later I wept, that our hard work has finally brought about some good.

Well, there is more, though good or bad I cannot say. It is difficult these days, and with this type of enemy…

First of all, early this morning, William Cormaeril addressed the town, declaring the rule of the tyrant Yarkul to be at an end, and declaring himself the rightful ruler, by birth, of this town. He announced that Yarkul had been killed by a Harper assassin. I suppose this isn’t true, but whoever did that job has my nomination for certain.

At any rate, the garrison all donned new tabards of yellow, with a coat of arms of four fields: one a purple dragon, one the Daggerdale coat, one with the Cormaeril sigil, and the fourth quarter a tacky rising sun. The twenty or so men that surround Cormaeril wear purple tabards of the same style.

Someone had to be expecting this to happen, as even the cleverest invoker would have had a difficult time conjuring up a couple hundred bright yellow tabards in one day.

I heard a commoner in the tavern this evening remark that “at least the Zhents didn’t make such a show of lording it up over the people.”

I have a source that sits on the council in the Tower who filled me in on some of the political changes that William is going to instigate:

1) No religious oppression and no tolerance of religious quarrels. The town will be paying to build a temple to Lathander as soon as a capable priest is found.

2) Absolutely zero slavery. Slave ownership and trade is punishable by hanging, or at the end of a sword…

3) Establish a trade route to Cormyr. What they plan to do about Tilverton, I do not know.

4) An alliance between the Dales is also desired by William, as WELL as with the town of Yûlash. I don’t know how that can be done right now.


That is all I know about the political changes that Cormaeril wants to make. A couple of other events here are worth mentioning as well.

Today at about noon, a bunch of the Garrison dressed in yellow tabards marched into the temple of Bane and slaughtered the clergy to the last.

This came about after a man in the town council accused the Banite church of retaining its slaves. I don’t know who it was that made this accusation, but it is an interesting play; certainly all the Churches in town and likely the Tower itself still have slaves in them. Nothing would be done about this if not for the publicizing of this fact by a power-elite member.

At any rate, 24 more slaves became free men and women today, and the Church of Bane in Dagger Falls is no more.

Related to this, my informant on the Council tells me that he was told in confidence by William himself that he (William) is worried about the three demons living in Brotherhood Tower (the Xvimite knights’ building). He knows he lacks the strength to overcome the Baron and his remaining men, and this keeps the voice of Hatemaster Dragkul a very powerful one on the council. Certainly, we shall not see the people who are enslaved in that horrible place freed anytime soon and no accusations have been made against the Xvimites.
I feel this is something we shall have to deal with ourselves.
The Fist may not be out of the picture yet. Riders came in this morning from the north road, reporting that they had been ambushed by a group of ogres and hill giants while trying to reach Addas Babar. From the report, ten men were cut down in seconds, and only two managed to escape. From what I have been told of the tactics used in this encounter, it sounds like elements of the 5th and 12th Companies are watching the road to ensure that no one will be able to either follow the ‘Beholder Stones’, trade west of Dagger Falls, or both!

Things appear to be getting better, but our war is far from over. That is all for now.



This correspondence stokes the fires burning deep within the core of these heroes, and they press on through the night. A cold autumn wind and lightning storm chased them to Daggerfalls, but many of the people of that town still claim to this day that it was the Liberators of Daggerfalls, our heroes, that brought the storm with them.

The day dawned overcast and grim. Many of the locals claim that they woke up that morning to great crashes of thunder and lightning.
