They claim that they knew something was going to happen that day, and almost all good citizens report that they felt very anxious as the sky went from deep black to grey. Here is the report of one man, nameless now, in history, who was witness to the events of that day;


From my second floor apartments, I have windows facing south, east and north, and saw everything that day.

I couldn’t sleep well the night before. A great storm was in the south, and it was drawing nearer all night. It must have woken me about four hours before sunrise, and I was compelled to just watch it roll in. No rain came with the storm, but this was a cleansing storm like this joyless town had not seen in decades.

As it drew nearer, it became more intense. I suppose it was the anger of the Liberators that drew the lightning and thunder. For as they drew to the gates, it seemed like the gates of hell were about to be kicked in, and a maelstrom about to unleash itself. I was nervous as hell just then. Another crash was heard, and I can’t say that it was thunder or the crashing of the gates at the Eastern Bailey, but the Liberators Storm blew right down the street. I ran from window to window. I ran to my eastern window to watch the gates, but a gust of wind blew me nearly back into my room, and the lightning struck again. There was thunder on the street, and I don’t know now if it was thunder from the clouds, or from the hooves of all the great horses that charged down that newly cobbled street, or both, but the Storm raced by my north window, and I could see the Heart of the Storm. Those men, the Liberators, flying right up to the Tower, and I knew the Gates of Hell had been kicked in, and the Maelstrom was upon us. I was scared, and I noticed shutters across the street being slammed shut. The few people on the street, citizen, soldier, man and woman, all fled and hid from the Maelstrom of the Liberators.

I know not what transpired up at the Tower, but the Liberators soon came back into my field of view, north up the street, knocking at the doors of Brotherhood Tower. The Maelstrom was about to reach a crescendo, and I confess that I hid myself at that time. A violence unimaginable broke loose up the street, and all I could do, all any one could do, was just stay in their homes and pray to all the gods that were watching.

Well, our prayers were heard. By the end of that day, the Maelstrom was over, and Baron Drake and the cult of Iyachtu Xvim was no more.



That morning, the DE went to the Tower, to talk with Cormaeril. He was loathe to grant them council, but at length he heard them. They announced that they would attack Brotherhood tower, killing the Baron and the three demons that dwelt inside. They sued for assistance from Cormaeril, but the coward offered none.

(Unfortunately, the DE had fallen for the canary trap that had been laid by Cormaeril; knowing that there was a spy at the council, he had secretly told all those he suspected that there were demons at

Brotherhood Tower. To each suspect he gave a different number, and when the heroes claimed to know of ‘three’ demons, the spy was revealed, though our heroes didn’t know it yet…)
Alone, the heroes marched to Brotherhood Tower.
The battle that ensued there that day was of legendary scale. The heroic details are many, and are outside the scope of such a cursory review of the history of the dale. However, the outcome can merrily be reported.

Baron Drake was slain. The final blow was delivered by the excommunicated paladin of Ilmater, but it was the efforts of Gaebril, and more importantly, Dorian of Sembia, Greatest Swordsman in the Realms, that it was possible for Maturin to finish the Baron off. The clergy of that church were slain to the man, as was the entire Brothers of the Black Fist order. The influence of Iyachtu Xvim had been completely cleansed from Daggerfalls.

Early on the morning of the 28th of Eleint, two young men ride into Shadowdale from Dagger Falls, insisting that they speak to a master Balak (Dalak’s brother, who was rescued from Chillholme earlier in the month.) “We bear missives from Lord Horgath!” Taking a brief respite from his hearth, Balak receives a pair of letters and a sack of coins from one of the envoys before they head into the town with more letters. Here is the first letter from St. Maturin;


Master Balak,
Please read the enclosed letter to your brother Dalak, and ask young Timfast if he has been keeping my friend to the diet I prescribed. His ill temper notwithstanding, it is of paramount importance that Dalak be confined to oats and whey until he has a chance to recover from his recent injury. Remember – he is to be strictly (and I am deadly serious) forbidden alcohol – especially his gutshaker. Remind Brother Turan that your brother is to be given double (triple when necessary) dosages of Calishite laudanum should he become irritable. I have enclosed fifty Sembian crowns to cover the expenses that he will no doubt run up with the Order of the Lambent Rose, if he has not done so already.

Additionally, I must apologize on the matter of my armour. Present circumstances prevent me from returning to Shadowdale for the foreseeable future, and I have recently come into a bounty of plate armour here in Dagger Falls. You may sell my armour at your convenience, and I trust that your profit will cover the cost of the repairs.

You may also wish to inform Lord Amcathra of the events described in my letter to Dalak.


What doesn’t kill you…. Brother Grey


St. Maturin’s Letter to Dalak Quickaxes, Eleint 29

Dear Dalak,
It is nearly over, my friend. I trust that your health has improved under Brother Turan’s conscientious care and Timfast’s cookery. I don’t need to tell you… on second thought; I’ll remind you that the wounds you suffered at Freedom Hill were grievous indeed. Your life is still in the balance. This time next year we may be able to share an ale together, but only if you follow Brother Turan’s medications and keep your head. I intend to see you hale and healthy when my work is done.

I wish to tell you that Baron Drake, the daemon we fought at Anathar’s Dell, is dead, and the Church of Iyachtu Xvim in Dagger Falls is broken. If I get ahead of myself, it is to spare you the suspense, which is not beneficial to you in your condition. I will tell all in turn.

Following our return to Dagger Falls with the refugees from Yarkul’s regime, one of the refugees told Lord Mourngrym about the destruction of the Church of Bane in Dagger Falls by the forces of William Cormaeril.

At the same council meeting where the refugee’s story was heard, we learned that the Zhents in Dagger Falls had come into possession of a primer for Harper Code and a list of the names and descriptions of known Harpers. The Harper agents Garrick Shining and the druid Aerin had set out only a week after us, coming southeast through the Goblin Marches rather than through Anauroch with their news. They also brought the unhappy news that only a handful of Harper agents remained in the Western Realms.

Boregar, too, brought news. A Harper agent in Dagger Falls indicated to us through a secret missive that the city was still rife with corruption and fear. While Cormaeril pressed negligently on with reforms and grand plans to ally the new Dagger Falls with Cormyr and Yûlash (Thagdul’s new stomping round), daemons walked among the citizens, and the murderous cultists of the Godson brazenly flouted the new laws, kidnapping unwary citizens and keeping them as slaves.

With the mysterious slabs making their way ever deeper into the desert, Sparrow sought the advice of the Lady Mystra, and divined that we would have no hope of catching them before they reached Addis Babar, the largest of the Zhents’ Anauroch outposts. Dorian and I disagreed on the best course of action, but with the council of Boregar, a man named Gaebril Tremalkin – a holy warrior of a strange faith – and Garrick Shining, we decided to cleanse Dagger Falls once and for all.

Following the council, we were to get some rest before heading north. I had barely caught my first wink of sleep in 48 hours when Dorian burst into my tent to tell me that Sparrow was both in grave danger, and was missing. I know not how the warning came, but Sparrow was nowhere to be found. A hurried search was organized, and with a presence of mind that still surprises me, I tracked Sparrow to the Old Skull Inn, where patrolling guards had seen him head in the company of a beautiful woman.

En masse, our party charged into the inn and up the stairwell only to find ourselves confronting an obviously ensorcelled member of Shadowdale’s emergency militia. Our friend Dorian, hardly the most level-headed of men these days, failed immediately and spectacularly in his attempts at negotiation and began to scuffle with the man. I ran downstairs with Boregar to enlist the aid of any spellcasters who

considered themselves decent enough to come to our aid and I am surprised and sorry to say that only one soul in the bar saw his duty clearly. By the time we had reclimbed the stairs, Gaebril and Dorian had forced their way through the door that Sparrow and the woman were sequestered behind. I came to the doorway just in time to see her figure sprout wings, let out an inhuman screech, and launch upwards, smashing through the skylight.

While Garrick fired an arrow up at the quickly diminishing beast, I bade the spellcaster dispel whatever magicks may have lain upon Sparrow. But even as his eyes cleared, I could see that his movements were growing sluggish. I suspected that the foul thing had poisoned him in some way. When I asked him, he indicated that it was so. I quickly jammed my index finger down his throat to induce vomiting, and, satisfied that he was safe, helped him down to the bar. By now, the inn had emptied to watch whatever succubus or harpy had been preying on our friend fly quickly north, towards Dagger Falls.
Our course was clearer than ever.
At noon, we set out for Dagger Falls, arriving the following morning. Sparrow was afraid that he would be recognized at the gate, but whatever forces had issued the capital interdiction against his return had evidently not passed the order on. (Happily, Sparrow’s spellcasting ability has not diminished with the loss of his hand – whenever he attempts to cast a spell, a phantasmal hand of blue light appears to work the somatics – truly a sign of his sanctity, at least in Mystra’s eyes.) Passing through the gate relatively unmolested, we journeyed to a pub outside the north gate where we were to meet a contact of Boregar’s. Why we must always seek out the houses of sin, I know not. Would it be too much to ask to meet a contact in a house of worship once in a while? I must admit that certain among us were not very circumspect about our inquiries, which may have had the dire consequences that I will write of soon.

Investigating the town, we confirmed that though Yarkul had fallen, the evil grip of the Zhent churches still held sway. Boregar, as the official ambassador of Shadowdale, sought an audience with Lord Cormaeril. Though he could not command the sacrifice of his guardsmen, and would not allow any volunteers, he indicated that, would we take up arms with the Xvimites, his forces would not intervene. I will tell you that I did not like this petty little man. Not only did he force his own cowardice on his men, who could not have refused duty’s clarion call to rid the Dales of the Godson’s evil taint, but he played us against the Xvimites without committing himself to either hand, seeking, no doubt, to ingratiate himself with whichever force proved victorious. A Cormyrean by birth, he seems every inch the bastard son of a Sembian and a Zhent.

With Cormaeril’s pusillanimous blessing, we waited while Sparrow did reconnaissance on the Xvmiite temple. It was locked solid, without windows, having only metal doors, and being completely encapsulated with both stone and metal, it seemed impregnable. Before long, Xvimite priests appeared as from nowhere and began to work their accursed spells against us. We had clearly been expected, and enemies came from every street and alley to face us on all sides. Immediately, Dorian and Boregar charged, while Garrick, Gaebril and I put our backs to one another and began to face off against the companies of armsmen that came at us from either direction. With his battery of spells, Sparrrow ran an impressively judicious guerrilla campaign as support.

For over an hour we fought, with darkness, paralysis and the curse of the Godson laying on us like a foul haze. But we would not tire, and our courage did not flag. Just when we thought the infidels might

break, a gong sounded, and the remains of the force let out a hoarse cheer as the terrible Baron Drake strode from the opening doors of the temple, flanked by a coterie of experienced looking men.
Without hesitation, Sparrow threw a fireball into their midst.
Horribly burned, all but the Baron retreated into the dark fastness of the temple, shutting the doors in front of them, with the Baron facing us down. Though Garrick, Gaebril and I were still engaged with the warriors, Dorian rose to the challenge of fighting Drake, his confident swagger unchecked by the cambion’s foul presence. My memories of the battle are hazy, but I know that Garrick broke from our circle to attack the Baron and was cut down, though whether by the Baron or a craven armsman I know not. Sparrow barely managed to bandage his wounds in time to save his life. Were he not with me now, I should have said he died.

Soon, Gaebril too broke from the fight and confronted the cambion with Dorian. I could see nothing from where I stood, all being concealed by the foul thing’s darkness, but when the light returned, Gaebril had fallen and Dorian danced with the daemon alone.
By now, we fought on the strength of our potions alone.
For what seemed an eternity, I was facing off against three trained warriors, Boregar with another two and Dorian seemed at an impasse with Drake. Then, in a critical instant, the Baron lunged at Dorian and overcorrected. Dorian’s returning blow nearly cleaved off the daemon’s arm. Seeing our chance, I broke from the circle and took a few short steps towards the prostrate thing to bring down Raven’s Tooth on its black and battered head, cleaving the foul skull in twain. (Though I meant to offense, Dorian has been quite curt with me since the decapitation. I get the sense that I robbed him of ‘the glory’ of the moment, in what would have been his finest hour. I cannot honestly comprehend how someone’s code of honour would see necessary bloodshed as glory, and not as a hideous last resort. But then, I suppose you are hardly a sympathetic audience for my point of view).

With a look of shock on its face, the daemon’s body collapsed. Immediately, its armour and weapon began to bubble and sublimate into a foul mist. The remaining Xvimites broke, hard. But I do not think they escaped. While we began to take stock of the situation, Boregar brought Drake’s head to Cormaeril, who seemed overawed. People began to float back into the streets to marvel at what we had done, and the guard quickly organized to finish the job and force open the gates of the temple. At length it was done.

Never have I been involved in so fierce or lengthy a battle, and never again do I want to see so much bloodshed. I have a new appreciation for the stalwartness of your kind, my friend, and a new sadness in knowing what sort of life you live. May Ilmater let my blessing upon you be heard. We managed to rescue the men who had been enslaved in the bowels of the temple, and through no small degree of argument with that bastard Cormaeril, I was able to commandeer some supplies and care for their upkeep, at Dagger Falls’ expense.

Unfortunately, early in the afternoon, we discovered the fresh corpse of Boregar’s contact. Evidently, he had been murdered while the battle raged. Dagger Falls is still without true peace, and I fear it will never be.

As for our current situation, I will be as informative as I can. Dorian has left us, and I do not know if he will return. His plans for the future have varied erratically over the last week. I hope to see him again, but will leave it to Tymora to see that our paths cross again. Gaebril and I, and perhaps Boregar, are heading into the desert in pursuit of the slabs, and I intend to hunt Grandfather to fulfill my pledge to Ilmater. Garrick’s plans are uncertain, though I expect he will accompany us. As for Sparrow, he has decided to reconsecrate the Xvimite cultists’ den and build a temple to Mystra and Lathander in partnership with Cormaeril. I pray that they are successful.

We have accomplished so much in the last months, and yet so much more is before us. Of the four of us who crossed the desert together, I am comforted that you, at least, have achieved peace, though at great cost. I wish you and Balak all the best and bid you take care. Boregar and Dorian have much to deal with, and I cannot escape the feeling that our destinies are still linked with Dagger Falls and Anauroch. For myself, doubt plagues me like a shadow, stronger now that the path seems clear. I had another vision from Torm yesterve, urging me again into the desert, away from Dagger Falls. There is yet to be a reckoning.
Ilmater guides us all,


Maturin.



This correspondence to the retired battle-rager is probably the best account of the final conflict between Drake and his Xvmites and the DE.

Dorian was frustrated with the lengthy decision making process, and rode off to pursue the tablets without any help. Not far up the north road, he encountered two Entropists who had just killed a Zhent wizard. Who these Entropists were, and what their role was is lost to history, but undoubtedly concerns the Starmetal in the area that is renders the Weave inert. They convinced Dorian that his best path would be with his comrades and his senses were returned.

It is worth mentioning at this time that Dorian had somehow been deeded Castle Daggerdale by William Cormaeril, after Brotherhood Tower had been thrown down. He considered this his new ‘hereditary home’, and rode hard that night, and spent the night in the ruined castle. Dragon had been following him the whole time, and the two shared their first night together in those ruins. The next day, they departed. Dragon was determined to return to the west by way of the south road, and Dorian was going to return with this friends to Daggerfalls.
This history of the Castle is a matter for another time.


The Temple of Cyric – Eleint 30
Though a vision from ‘Torm’ had been given to Maturin, the DE could not be convinced to leave Dagger Falls. They hotly debated the issue of leaving, to pursue the stones, but many were unhappy with the

situation in Daggerfalls still. An assassin had killed Boregar’s man, meaning that there was still a treacherous puppet master somewhere in the council of that politically-metamorphing town. Finally, it was decided that they would stay and clean up this town for good, or ill, and allow the tablets to escape into the desert.

A council was called in the Tower. All major players in the Dale were present, and many things were discussed. The nature of the council was changed to include Sparrow and Rewel Thunderstorm, and plans were made to turn Brotherhood tower into a joint place of worship for Lathander and Mystra. Further, Dorian, now Lord of Castle Daggerdale and a small barony that surrounded it, had also landed himself title and a position on the council.

Tempers eventually ran hot at the council, as Cormaeril would not give in to any requests by the DE or other good parties at that council, and finally Gaebril and Sparrow had seen enough. The two began a brief but effective inquisition at that very council table, and an invisible man was discovered behind Cormaeril. He was subsequently attacked and chased, and through the remarkable, some would say miraculous, efforts of the Harper Garrick, the spy was captured and interrogated. This man turned out to be a Zhent spy named Venosar. Much was revealed by the interrogation and examination of the journal of this rogue-mage spy. The following details were uncovered;
• Yarkul was everyone’s puppet
• Venosar had been a mediary between Thagdul and Cormaeril for months
• Thagdul was an ally, and Yarkul was his vassal
• Thagdul has been active in Yulash for at least 3 months.
• Cyric was influencing the Lathanderites directly by deceiving Dawnlord Cassamar

• Amaretta (the succubus) – conjured by someone, Yarkul may have had some power over her, but her presence pre-dated Yarkul

• Venosar was ‘our man on the council’. He was a feared assassin, sent to replace Yarkul. He charmed Cormaeril in the first place, and arranged the removal of the Banites and Xvimites
• Cyric does not appear to like the idea of the tablets going west.
The number of demons reported to be in Brotherhood Tower was told to all the members of the council, in confidence, though each member was told a different number. This is how Boregar’s man was discovered and subsequently executed.

Another important find in the bed chamber of Venosar was the fated longsword of Morgan Lathkule. This blade had found it’s way here, all the way from Waterdeep, with Yarkul, who had kept it as a token of his defeat over Raven. The blade was taken by Dorian, but ownership of this legendary weapon did not end there; it would be wielded by Maturin months later, but let me not spoil the surprise just yet. Allow me to say only this; that blade, though delivered by evil hands, was sent by the Good Fates, as you’ll soon read.

With this information, the path the DE would take became clear to all except Dorian. They would rid the town of the Cyricists when they were healed.

All the healing resources of the Tower were mustered, and after the DE had rested for about ten hours, they attacked the fortified church of Cyric in Daggerfalls.

This was another battle of epic proportions. The DE, accompanied by the now clear-thinking Cormaeril and his elite hearth guard, staged a three-pronged attack upon the vile lair of these villains. During the attack, it was learned that Morgul the Vigilant Talon (high priest or Cyric in Daggerfalls) had been amassing an undead army. The ranks of many species of undead bolstered the ranks of priests and warriors of the Baneson servants, and the battle was difficult. In the end, though, the Church of Cyric was also completely destroyed, and the Heroes were praised with great praise.
Departure - Harvestide
By the time things cooled off in Daggerfalls, Harvestide was upon the Dales. Winter was coming, and the DE were overdue to leave. All signs indicated that the Tablets were weeks ahead of the DE, but they planned on catching them anyway.

Daggerfalls had become a place of peace again in those days. Rewel Thunderstorm, though having made peace with Cassamar, still begat the church of Lathander in Daggerfalls. Sparrow stayed in this town too, to do his goddess’ bidding, and opened his temple in conjunction with the new Morning Lord’s Temple. The three evil faiths were not heard from or seen in Daggerfalls for many years to come, and peace was upon the place.

But Daggerfalls is doomed to have some turmoil. In the wake of the Black Saint (though he wasn’t called that yet), a cult of Shar blossomed in this town. An oratory of Gaebril, given in the Eastern Bailey convinced many to join this faith, to help them enjoy the new lives they had, and to forget the evils of the past.

An oratory given by Maturin that very day also spawned an intense, but briefly lived following of Ilmater. Until the height of the Spellplague and the God Deaths, the faiths of Lathander and Shar were the most influential in the Dale and in the town itself. The temple to Mystra was also a very busy place, and it is well known that this attraction brought many practitioners of magic, and their money, to the town every year.


The Road West
Though the first Harvestide celebrations in over 20 years were being held in Daggerfalls, the DE stayed only until after breakfast of the 2nd of Marpenoth. They took to the road, traveling as light and as fast as they could. They intended to catch the Beholder Tablets, but hey would not do so this winter.

Less than half a day out of Daggerfalls, the DE was ambushed by the 5th Co. of Fist, Gumbottom’s Guard. This company of ten hill giants was lead by Yin Xu at this point, and his leadership nearly proved effective enough to turn back the DE. Several were hurt badly, but they still managed to defeat enough of the giants to route them. Clearly, the road was still being watched by the forces of the Beholders, and the journey would not be easy.

A few days after that, the DE was nearly exterminated. They encountered beholder-kin upon the road. A large, tree-like beholder attempted to have the DE turn back by using magical suggestions, but this proved ineffective. A battle broke out, and other beholderkin joined the battle to protect the overseer

tree-beholder that tried to end the encounter peacefully. The DE was overcome by these foes, and if not for the intervention of the Entropists, all would have been lost.

These two men, now introduced as Amon and Zuth, of Chessenta, explain that they were pursing the Tablets west, but realized they were not suited to travel in the desert. They turned back, hoping to find a way West through the dangerous lands to the south. The two men had a long discussion with the DE. They explained that two beholders that the DE knew of, Zantiid and Xulla were simply ‘second rank’ beholders. They knew of the staves, but little about them. The two men seemed most determined to get to the Tablets, but did not state their purpose entirely.


Addas Babar
The DE was soon in the desert again. Just as the badlands begin to give way to sands and dunes, one finds the citadel of Addas Babar, perched high upon an island of rock overlooking the first oasis on the long road through the desert.

The DE decided they would not circumnavigate the outposts on this return-journey. Boregar was on a quest to put to rights all those wrongs he had left behind, and the DE would have been without him if they would not fight his battle with him.

The DE made short work of this fortress, and left it a grave of Zhents and a ruin.


Bhaerlith
Bhaerlith was a difficult conquest, given the heavily fortified and geographical nature of the place. At length, however, the DE were victorious, and the fortress was liberated. Of the bounty found in this fortress, the Gond Pistola was recovered and returned to Boregar. Many other powerful tools of war were also recovered.

The many slaves that were there stayed on. Many were devout followers of Ilmater, and though Maturin had clearly been excommunicated, they took it as a sign that they too should isolate themselves and endure the lonesome desert.

To this day, Bhaerlith is an abbey dedicated to Ilmater. The wandering priest Shildevan came to the abbey not long after the DE had departed, and assumed leadership of the flock.


Olomaa
Travel through the desert was made somewhat easier this time around, though Boregar worried that they would not make it out before winter. He explained that even the native nomads of this land brave the underdark during winter, rather than face the harshness of Anauroch’s cold season. They DE was making good time, though, as they were more effectively supplied after each fortress they sacked. It was the plundered resources of these forts, plus the hard-gained-wisdom from their first crossing that made their return-crossing possible.

At Olomaa, they found that they did not get there in time to sack the place. The fortress was in ruins, and not a soul could be found upon initial arrival. Boregar investigates further, and finds that a lone priest of Cyric is living there. This man, Ful’Zan, explains that a beholder and the Fist came through and killed everyone. This settlement had been the desert bastion of Cyric, but the temple is now in ruins, and the sole survivor of the place has resorted, not with much loathe, to eating the flesh of the dead flock of Cyricists there.

When Maturin shows up, Ful’Zan shrieks and hisses, and says “You didn’t leave when you were told! Now you can’t catch it!” Apparently, this crazed priest knew something of Maturin, and although the Boregar attempted to subdue the man, and he makes off into the desert. His trail could not be followed.

The DE stays on here for a day to burn bodies and desecrate the remains of the Temple. They ponder the visions from ‘Torm’ that were visited upon Maturin back in Daggerfalls, and conclude that Cyric was posing as Torm again (the ‘Fool Knight’ being his favourite god to impersonate) to motivate the DE to follow the Tablets, and leave the church of Cyric in Daggerfalls alone.

That Maturin didn’t follow the advice of Cyric in the guise of Torm is to his credit, as well as the credit of his friends and advisors, who saw their duty clearly. Cyric had been taken completely off the board with the cleansing of Olomaa.


Maturin and the Lion
Many weeks later, the DE arrives back at Vaerthyl. As Boregar had feared, winter had come and the DE where trapped. They prepare the ruined keep there for their occupation throughout the winter.

The winter is cruel in Anauroch, to say the least. The remaining five men of the DE train hard all winter, but on New Year’s Eve, the time of reckoning for Maturin and Grandfather is nigh.

Late that night, as the full moon broke through the relentless clouds and snows, and the eye of Muir’Quaggoth was seen by the Grey Knight in its radiance. A great roar is heard off in the desert somewhere, and the DE do what they can to equip Maturin for the fight. Not long after, Grandfather lets out a roar just outside the doors. Maturin takes the floor, braced for battle, while the other 4 wait at the stairs. They know that this can be a fight between Grandfather and Maturin, alone.

Grandfather crashes open the door and stands on the threshold while Maturin calls out the beast;
Grandfather!
In the name of Ilmater, I call you out and command you to lie down before me. I command you to repent your wrongs and forsake your evil god.

I accuse you, scion of Muir-Quaggoth, of carnage immeasurable. Your legacy of pain and suffering lies heavily upon Faerun.
I am here to cleanse it. In the name of Ilmater;

In the name of those who have suffered; In the name of all that is holy and good; Repent and prepare to be destroyed.

Grandfather growled low and strode into the room. The two god-fated combatants stared at each other for a moment, and then the Lion sprung! From the outset, things looked horrible for Maturin. He was knocked over and pinned right away, the giant lycanthrope poised above his prone form. The Lion bit deep into the knight, and tore and tore. All the while, however, Maturin was pulling the beast onto silver-plated spikes upon his breast plate, and making what attacks were allowed him with the Lathkule blade; this blade having been forged and enchanted in Waterdeep for the eradication of lycanthropes. The blade was thrust up through the beast’s belly, and it gave a great roar before delivering one final bite to the knight. It tore deep into his neck, and then both combatants ceased their struggle.

Maturin was hardly perceptible from beneath the giant beast, and neither were moving. When his companions came to his side however, and hefted the heavy monster off him, they found him still breathing. Though he was covered in blood, both from himself and the Lion, they could make out the shape of a gray tear under the Knights right eye. The knight breathed, and his companions helped him to his knees. Maturin stayed kneeling for what seemed like an eternity. His breathing caused him to heave, and he steadied himself with the bloodied blade that had slain the huge Lion that lay at his side.

He looked up, and the grey tear sparkled for just a moment, and Maturin nodded wearily. At that moment, a scraping was heard at the wind-assaulted door. Warburden had returned, and stepped in to nuzzle his masters bloodied head. With what strength he had, the weary knight raised one bloodied gauntlet to stroke the beasts great face in silence, while his companions, silent as well, looked on.
Dorian was heard to whisper “Ilmater be praised”.
This final portion of the Daggerdale Expedition is most eloquently told through the words of the Grey Knight, found in his memoirs years after these events;




Ilmater's boon 'neath the green-eyed moon Did tame the were-lion's wroth;
The desert trails had their secret tales For the sons of Muir-Quagoth;
But a Damaran knight is an outlandish sight, To rise from Anauroch's haze
And a night of fear in the Rogue Dragon Year Was Grandfather's end of days.




The Story Ends and Continues
Much more could be said of what happened to those heroes after the death of Grandfather, and their return to Waterdeep. But with regards to the role they played in Daggerdale, this chapter of the story is concluded. In the spring of 1373 they continued on to Waterdeep, hunting beholders, Zhents and Drow with their other companions whose company they parted in Phaulkonmere two years earlier.

I wish I knew what happened to the tablets, to the wizard Thagdul, to the other Zhents and the drow, but I do not. The world shortly after was thrown into the chaos of the Spellplague, and only during my lifetime have we seen a reconnection between the Dales and the Western Heartlands (despite the efforts of Returned Netheril).

I do know that Dorian returned to the Castle, and I think he’s still there in some evil form or another.

I know also that the Black Saint returned in secret in the early 1400’s; his presence was whispered of enough to be more than a rumour, but he is dead now, though ironically not forgotten.

Maturin too is dead. I am told that the remains of his body are at the abbey at Bhaerlith, which remains free of Netherese influence despite its proximity.

Unfortunately, Sparrrow Flame-Handed, who served as the high priest of Mystra for decades even after her death, also vanished in the tumultuous years of the Spellplague, though his body is not accounted for. He was last seen with my father on the plains of Netheril, facing off against abominable agents of that evil empire. Wielding what magic he could, he held off a company of monsters while my father and his soldiers retreated from an impossible battle. I in fact owe my life to Sparrow, as this was years before my birth.

The Daggerdale Expedition and its allies was made up of other mortal men whose names I cannot find in this age, though evidence of their passing remains. Of the Harpers, Boregar, Garrick & Aerin, there is no further mention I have found (and I have searched), but there are many young boys named Boregar in this Dale and Shadowdale today, and Harper’s Court outside what was Brotherhood Tower, is named for them.

I will return to an accounting of some of these loose ends someday when my duties are either lessened or shared. But for now, I remain,
Luminous Whitegate,
Lord of Castle Radiance and High Commander of the Order of the Lambent Shield
DDC – 1373 - 2: Notes on the Ocular Alliance in Dagger Falls 1372
Report by Mnestheus Melshimber with files from Jeryth Phaulkon Submitted 10 Mirtul, 1373 to Twilight Hall in Berdusk
Notes from GFD:
I have actually seen two copies of this report. This is a translation of the original, which was in Steele’s box, and is now in Candlekeep. The other I found in the New Twilight Hall, but I’ve nearly said too much.

I’ve included it in its entirety, because it seems to set the stage for the handover of Daggerdale from the clutches of the evil Triumvirate, and it maps out relationships that are still important to understand.
-GFD
Following the resurrection of Bane in the autumn of 1371, the constellation of powers and allegiances of many churches, governments and organisations underwent a not unexpected period of adjustment. Not least did this affect the Black Network of Zhentil Keep. By 1371, the Zhentarim had become enmeshed in the machinations of a powerful group of beholders, here referred to as the Ocular Alliance. This marriage of convenience has had far-reaching effects on both the Black Network and the inter-regional trade in Western Faerun. While the aims of the Ocular Alliance are as yet unknown, they have been extensively speculated upon elsewhere by this author, and it is not the purpose of this report to do so. Rather, the following pages will detail the role played by the various organisations involved in the conspiracy, and the schism of 1372 that led to the current enmity between the Church of Cyric and the Ocular Alliance. These notes have been compiled with the assistance of Lady Jeryth Phaulkon, who knew many of the eyewitnesses personally, and without whose knowledge and dedication to our cause we would have remained ignorant of the following facts.


In the days after Greengrass of last year, a small gathering of our order in the western city of Waterdeep initiated three missions that would lead to the unmasking of the Ocular Alliance and severely hinder its aims. The existence of the Alliance, long suspected by many, had until then been unsubstantiated, owing to the recent difficulties experienced in the North and East (see the accompanying Notes Concerning the

Unstrung Harp, also by this author). The Church of Cyric was to play a central role in the expedition undertaken by those who became known as the Company of the Eastern Storm

The Church of Cyric played a key role in the maintenance of the Ocular Alliance's domination of Dagger Falls, playing a primarily defensive role, (at least after the consolidation of power in the spring and summer of 1372). The primary objective was the paralysis of any organized opposition by the other Dales. This was played out in Shadowdale through the agency of High Dawnlord Cassamar, the priest of Lathander that unwittingly played into the hands of the Ocular Alliance by advocating non-interference in the affairs of Shadowdale's neighbours to the north.

When the concentration of interests opposing the Alliance reached a critical mass with the arrival of the knights of the Holy Triad, a new approach became necessary. Lord Maturin Horgath, at the time a paladin out of favour with his patron deity, was the ideal candidate for the Dark Sun to use in order to advance His interests. Through the guise of Torm the True, Cyric arranged an ambush for the forces of good at Anathar's Dell, where they were pitted against the unholy orders of Bane and Iyachtu Xvim.

Cyric's cunning in the arrangement of this ambush, however, would prove to be his undoing. The decision not to support the Knights of the Black Gauntlet and the Brothers of the Black Fist in their clash against the Holy Triad was taken by the other members of the Alliance as an outright betrayal, and Cyric's role was quickly written out of whatever plan was being pursued by the Masters of the Alliance. That is, if there indeed remained a role to be played.

Prior to the slaughter at Anathar's Dell, it seemed that Cyric's role in the Alliance was one of trust and importance, as key strategic points were exclusively manned by the unholy orders of the Dark Sun. The 4th Garrison of Dagger Falls oversaw the excavation of the mine in the Dagger Hills, where the "Beholder Tablets" were unearthed. Secondly, the desert citadel of Olomaa, along the Zhentarim- controlled trade route across Anauroch, was a strong Cyricisit enclave. One of the two Cyricist Fist companies was stationed there. Indeed, the role of the Cyricists in the fabric of the Fist mercenary company has yet to be understood. Their involvement certainly predated the alliance between the Fist (which we understand to be a military arm of Manshoon) and the interests of the Oculars.

However, such rumination is of exclusively historical interest in light of the events that followed the second battle of Anathar's Dell. On the 7th of Eleint, 1372, the forces of good and evil clashed in Cyric's well-orchestrated ambush. The knights of the Triad were sorely diminished before the Brothers of the Black Fist (paladins of Bane) were driven away. The Knights of the Black Gauntlet (paladins of Iyactu Xvim) were destroyed utterly, but the Ebon Spur (paladins of Cyric) were nowhere to be seen. This cowardice of leaving the dangerous work to his allies would prove to be Cyric's downfall, it seems.

The next day, the mysterious Beholder Tablets were unearthed from the mine in the Dagger Hills, and, to the best of our knowledge, the entire Cyricist garrison was marched to its death in the mines, which were sealed thereafter. It is unknown whether these soldiers were a willing sacrifice by Cyric, believing that He still held a position of trust within the Alliance, or whether their usefulness had simply expired, along with Cyric's, and this was the first open move by the Masters of the Alliance against their former ally.

Martial wisdom advocates keeping one's enemies closer than one's friends. Cyric's seeming position of trust in the Alliance revealed itself to be just such a short leash, keeping the devious deity's agents under

the watchful eyes of the Oculars. A short-lived outbreak of violence in Dagger Falls the day after the tablets were excavated revealed that the theological arms of the Alliance were becoming unstable. A squabble between Banites and Cyricists required the intervention of the Fist soldiers at the behest of Yarkul.

Reports from an agent who played a key role in the liberation of Dagger Falls and shattering the Alliance's stranglehold on trade across Anauroch indicate that it was at about this time that Cyric began to move against the Alliance, through his influence over Lord Horgath. Appearing once again in the guise of Torm, Cyric urged Maturin to follow the Tablets, and prevent whatever was guiding them west from making its journey. This vision occurred on Eleint 10, a scarce two days after the excavation of the tablets.

The fact that the Church of Cyric remained a powerful force in Dagger Falls at that time indicates that hostility between the former allies was not yet in the open, but it is likely that both the Masters of the Alliance and Cyric Himself understood that they were now at odds. When the Tablets arrived in Dagger Falls and the Fist were recalled from their various patrols, the balance of power rested on the edge of a knife, ready to topple at the slightest breath.

It is interesting that Yarkul, the Zhentarim mage who played such a key role in the Alliance, was cut from its ranks at almost the same time as the Cyricists. More interesting still when one considers that Yarkul was an ardent follower of the Church of Xvim, and consort to a demon of Xvim, a succubus named Amaretta. Yarkul had been instrumental at securing a role for 'The New Darkness' in the ranks of the Alliance in 1371 when he made contact with them in Waterdeep, and had brought them to the east after completing whatever role he had played there.

For all intents and purposes, the Alliance was through with the Dalelands - and the Churches - when the Beholder Tablets were unearthed. It seems that the usefulness of both Xvim and Cyric were limited to that purpose. Perhaps the Masters of the Alliance were punishing their vassals - Yarkul and the Xvimites for their failure in Waterdeep, and the Cyricists for their ambition - or perhaps they were simply tired of having to manage the politics of competition within their ranks. In any event, these internecine worries were left behind in Dagger Falls when the Tablets moved west. Yarkul and the soldiers formerly of the 9th Fist Company were all that remained when the Alliance turned its many eyes to the west.

Yarkul's subsequent efforts at peacemaking only resulted in his (long overdue) assassination, and the establishment of a new government under the hereditary rule claimed by Lord William Cormaeril of Cormyr. The relative strengths of the Churches of Xvim and Cyric can be seen in the rapid elimination of the Church of Bane after Cormaeril took hold of the reins of power. There is, however, a sizable caveat to this statement. Cormaeril, as was later revealed, was acting as an unwitting pawn for yet another Zhentarim mage, one Venosar, allegedly sent by his superiors in the Zhentarim to replace Yarkul (prior, it must be noted, to Yarkul's death). Cormaeril's short-lived policy of establishing trade links with Yûlash - another Zhentarim-controlled town, indicates that Venosar was likely an agent of Thagdul, the mage who controlled that polity for most of 1372. Little is known of this man, save for his involvement the previous year in Waterdeep, and that he was allegedly responsible for the installation of Yarkul in Dagger Falls. (It should be noted that it is the working hypothesis of this author that Thagdul is, or was, the spokesperson for Zhentarim interests within the Ocular Alliance. See my previous reports on Zhentarim trade monopolies on the Sword Coast in 1370-71.)

With the elimination of the Church of Bane, the replacement of Yarkul (friend to Xvim) with Cormaeril (puppet of Venosar), a delicate balance of power remained in Dagger Falls. Hatemaster Dragkul and Morgul the Vigilant Talon waited each for the opportunity to seize control and oust the other. It was the arrival of the company that would become known as the Eastern Storm that brought things to a head.

Cyric's policy of pitting one enemy against another did not waver, for all that he hoped the heroes would follow the Tablets. If the heroes would not head west, then they could be put to work in Dagger Falls.

Venosar revealed his Cyricist sympathies as Cormaeril sanctioned the extermination of the Xvimites. Unfortunately, the heroes unwittingly put Venosar onto the scent of one of our own agents within the Dagger Falls establishment, but his own undoing came shortly and surely thereafter.

Having secured the Church of Cyric as the sole remaining interest in Dagger Falls, the Dark Sun attempted one last time to put Lord Horgath back on the trail of the Tablets. For whatever reason, the knight stayed on for the events that exposed Venosar's dealings and led to the final purge of the Church of Cyric from the town.

A footnote to this report concerns the men who had belonged to the 9th Company of Fist. They disappeared from Dagger Falls with the downfall of the temple, and were not seen again until Marpenoth that year, when the Eastern Storm came upon their corpses on the trail of the Tablets. It seems likely that Cyric, having failed to spur his pawn the paladin in time, finally used his own resources and sent his soldiers to stop the Tablets. They must have followed the trail of the rest of the Fist into Anauroch, somehow slipping past the guards that had been left to thwart such pursuit, only to be slain when they finally caught their quarry.

A report from the Eastern Storm indicates that the desert citadel of Olomaa was scourged by the caravan accompanying the Tablets. It seems that there is now no doubt that Cyric and the Ocular Alliance are open enemies.

It is the hope of this author that the intelligence and analysis herein will prove in some way towards the elimination of the threat posed by the Ocular Alliance. While the fact remains that our true enemy is, as has always been the case, the Black Network, the Ocular Alliance has proved a powerful tool for their efforts against us. Nowhere is this more evident than in the murderous success of Venosar in the Dales and the insane mage Malkor in Neverwinter and the North. The dissolution of this Alliance can only be to our advantage as an organisation.

One other note bears mentioning. While our sources indicate that the Eastern Storm have recognized Cyric's treachery and that Lord Horgath has once more achieved a state of incorruptiblity, Cyric's role in the affair of the Ocular Alliance may yet be unfinished. The connection between the mage Thagdul and the Church of Cyric, while poorly documented, may be stronger than is yet known. With Venosar's death and the elimination of his soldiers and Church in Dagger Falls, Cyric may now look to Thagdul to advance His interests. It is the recommendation of this report that resources be allocated to the investigation of this mysterious person, and while such an investigation may be impractical given the strain on personnel recently, it is nevertheless of utmost importance. Thagdul's role in this affair must be deciphered if our knowledge of Cyric's modus operandi is to be of any constructive use in the fight against the Alliance.

Finally, it must be admitted that an alternative hypothesis to the events of Eleint 1372 exists - that the Xvimites and the Cyricists, both key players in the Ocular Alliance, were betrayed not by their unseen

masters, but in fact by an as yet unknown force external to the Alliance itself. However, the evidence on the matter indicates otherwise. Whatever, or whoever, such an external force could be is entirely unknown.
Mnestheus Melshimber, Mirtul 1373

DDC – Chapter Four – Forword and Summary
Wherein the prosperous dale is set upon by a formidable foe (Netheril), with many heroes answering the call to arms.

Although the primary enemy of Daggerdale has been the Netherese since their return to Faerun at the start of the Spellplague, and especially in the decades that followed as they secured their previous territories (the desert Anauroch, which has been transforming into the green plains of Netheril for some time), this chapter is about the villains they worked with to attack the dale from within.

This story is mostly about the religious struggle between competing faiths in the area. Amaunator has been the dominant faith, since being adopted by the Whitegate Family decades ago and has the most administrative and military control over the dale.

Chauntea is the other major faith of the region, often called ‘The Old Religion’, as Chauntea predates the Spellplague by more than a thousand years (and as you will learn in the unwoven threads of Chapter 7, may be an even older Netherese god). As a mainly agricultural settlement, it is not surprising to find such a large following of Chauntea.

Shar is another matter altogether, and if you, faithful reader, have read Chapter Three, you will know that
the seeds of this faith were sewn in the 14th century, when one of



Netherese Ruin Revealed by Retreat of Anauroch

the Eastern Storm (Gaebril Tremalkin) openly proselytized on behalf of Shar, and created many followers, and indeed, a blood line that becomes the Dark Garden in this story.

This chapter begins with the rise to power of the Whitegates, who came by all they have honestly. They rebuilt the dale with faith and sword and asked nothing in return. However, this story is dominated by the decimation of their family and holdings by the Dark Garden, and we find their story in it’s denouement by the close of this chapter, though the threat posed by the Dark Garden is ended.
Here are the players in this act;
The Whitegate Family – Started by Ardelusk Whitegate, who was at the Battle of Liberty Hill (c.f. DDC – 1373 – 2: The Daggerdale Expedition), this family were staunch worshipers of Amaunator, and spread this faith throughout the dale.

The White Cloaks – a company of adventurers with letters patent to carry out operations in the dale. Started by a group which also included Lumina Whitegate. These men and women are heroes in the dale and beyond.

The Dark Garden – a circle of black druids who follow Shar, the head of their circle a woman named Belladonna, who is a grand-child (or possibly child) of the Black Saint, Gaebril Tremalkin

The Yellow Abbey – this is the seminary in Daggerfalls for the clerics of Amuanator. The Historic Wing is a part of the Abbey that contains the more secret tomes and forbidden knowledge that

has accumulated throughout the centuries in the dale, and was the home (prison?) of Brother Phineas Hoetmer, whose connection to the Dark Garden affair was as inextricable as it was inexplicable.

Sunblades – This is the militant order of the dale, and is largely considered a branch of the church of Amaunator, though that was formally changed at the Governors’ Assembly in ’82. There are Sunblades in every settlement in Daggerdale, and many heroes come from the ranks of this disciplined order.

There are others that played a role, and you’ll read of them in the pages to come, and I hope, enjoy this story and the bitter-sweet conclusion of the chapter. But I’m in peril of spoiling the ending and will leave it at that.
-GFD


DDC - 1398 - 1: Life of the White Saint
A Record of the Life of Ardelusk Whitegate (1340?-1399) and the rebuilding of Dagger Dale During the Tumultuous Years of Arcane Plague - Original Biographical Notes by
Senezear Dale.
Notes from GFD:
This is an easy document to find. In the libraries of most established houses in the dale, you’ll find a book about the Whitegates. About 1/2 of it are from sessions that Ardelusk Whitegate held with Senezear Dale around 1387. What you will read if you find a copy are the compiled and edited notes from Shefton Dale, Senezear’s son. I spoke to Shefton Dale up at Tesh Valley Farm when I met with the Tethyamar League. Mr. Dale insisted that the account was completely as his father had written it, but did confess that a portion of it seemed to have been missing, after the entry on Paladin’s Grave.
Such is the nature of collecting old paper…
This bit of the book is worth reading as it mentions the woman Arabelle Needle, who would sew a great deal of suffering many decades later…

But, enjoy the story and perspective of this humble hero before you make yourself mad with the benefit of the reader’s hindsight…
-GFD
Liberty Hill
I came to this place for the first time on the 19th of Eleint, 1372. Maturin and his men were leading myself and scores of other freed slaves on an overland march that had taken us many days. We had been harried by the enemy every step of the way; Yarkul was enraged over the loss of what was then called ‘Chillholme Mine’; I think he suspected that the mine was worth more than just star-borne-tablets of some obscure monster goddess.

Anyway, we spent all night arraying defences on that hill; Boregar had been scouting around us, and he came back in a hurry saying that several companies of Fist were only a few hours away. We set up what spears we could in the ground at the top of that hill, and armed and trained every able-bodied person. I was showing a few of the younger men how to swing a hammer to break a man’s knees when Dorian came up to me, smiled, and knocked my clumsy hammer from my hands with the flick of his wrist and the flash of his blade.

“A hammer is no tool for a true warrior” he said to us. He had a small boy with him, Cederick Blackmane was his name, and I came to know him well in the decades that followed. Cederick had an armload of swords that the Liberators had taken from some of the 3rd Garrison at the mine, and it was all he could do to not stumble over the weight of them. Dorian grabbed the swords and put them in our hands, and spent the rest of the dark hours showing us a few basic strokes.

When the daylight came, I was never so thankful. All that long night, with the worry of the enemy closing in around us, and the fear of not living up to Lord Dorian’s training, I as terrified. I’ve never been that afraid before or since. It was the worst night of my life. When the day came, I was never so thankful.

Before the day came, as the sky was turning grey in the east, the Fist came upon us. We were completely encircled by them; 2nd - Garlunk’s Roughriders, 3rd - Blacktooth’s Hussars, 4th - Sandalwood’s Roughriders. The Murderer of Mirabar himself was there, as were the terrible halforcs Garlunk and Blacktooth. There were dozens of heavy horse, a platoon of murderous archers, and a score of heavy foot that slammed into us.

I will not recount this battle stroke-for-stroke. Others have already done that to such a degree that my account is of small contribution, and perhaps even small contradiction. What I will offer is that the enemy broke with the first rays of the sun, which only a few have mentioned, and then only to say that the halforcs didn’t want to fight with the sun in their eyes; the 2nd Fist had ridden into us from the West, and atop their great warhorses, they indeed would have seen the sun first; I recall it glinting off the brutal blade of one such monster.

No, this battle is a legend already. I only wish to state that this is the place where I first felt like a freed man; I had been taken from my shackles at Chillholme, and I had marched as a refugee for days behind Maturin and the others. But atop Liberty Hill, I fought.
I fought with a sword, and I drove off my enemies. I was then a Free Man.
The Farm
Many years later, I returned to this site. I knew it had become a site of some small pilgrimage; there was a cenotaph there, and many small gravestones had been placed randomly around it. No one knew where anyone was really buried, except the Fist. They lay under three huge piles of stones, which I always assumed had been put there by the elves of Cormanthor, but to be honest, to this day I’m not sure who buried those dead villains beneath so much stone.

None of that mattered. It was 1374 and I had already had my Vision, and much of what I accomplished had already been done. But this was my greatest accomplishment; castles and towers and knights and all that were fine achievements, but on the site of that place where I first swung a sword, I also hoed my first row. I built a farm there, and raised a family, and Amaunator provided all the sun we needed to

gather surplus crops all the years I have lived so far. I was already rich in gold from ‘Chillholme’, but now I was rich in crops and children, and that is a gift far greater than any vein of any metal.

Both of my sons were born there, and there they learned to swing a blade. There, they learned to swing the sickle as well.

One day, a small group of people had come from town; they were peddlers in some sort of

collective. They were selling needles and cloth and that sort of thing, and they went around to many of the farms to do just that. Their leader was a fine-looking woman whom I recognized immediately. I had first seen her on the other side of Anuaroch at some terrible mountain-fortress where the Zhents were unpacking us from our crated journey from the Sword Coast. She had been a seamstress in Neverwinter, I recall.

Her name as I had known it was Arabella Needle, but she now called herself Arabella Liberty, and the small child that clung to her skirts was likewise called Liberty. She asked me what name I had given this farm, and to be honest, I hadn’t thought of it. ‘Ardelusk’s Acres’ I said in half-hearted response. I think I may have even asked, rather than suggested the title.
She shook her head. “Liberty Hill”.
The woman was not being coy or putting on airs. She had fought with us in ’72 on this very site as well. She too had won her freedom here, and she was right about the name.
The Paladins’ Grave
I did something in 1395 that I later came to regret, though it seemed like the right thing to do at the time.

Cormanthor had begun to grow unchecked, the times being what they were (and still are as I sit here and tell you this). Many times in the years since my liberation, I visited a place only 20 miles away from my farm, called Anathar’s Dell. This place goes by more names than the paladins buried there, but I always called it ‘Paladins’ Grave’. The story of the two battles there in 1372, before my liberation mind you, are still told with as much colour and detail as though they happened yesterday, though I cannot now think of a soul besides the Proprietor of Quick Axes (a place I don’t frequent), who was actually there.

Anyway, I always thought of this place as a sort of precursor site to my own revered Liberty Hill. There were a score of paladins of the four Orders that dominated that time buried there, and their stories are more or less well documented. What is unknown is that the great cenotaph there, constructed by a repentant Dawn Lord Cassius, had been toppled by the oaks of Cormanthor, and many of the graves were being overrun by the forest.

I moved that cenotaph and those men to my own farm, and they lay there today. I was roundly criticized for disturbing these graves, but I would not sit by and watch them become lost to us by way of a relentless forest.

I can recite the names of all those knights by memory, as they appear on that stone. In fact, if I close my eyes, I am standing in the bedroom in the tower on the farm, and looking to the west, I can see the last bit of sun coming through the mountains and reflecting off that ever-polished stone.

I need to change something I said; I don’t regret bringing those men to my farm. Their deeds will never die so long as my line keeps clear that hill, and I am happy to have my children and their children harvest crops under the silent watch of that cenotaph.


DDC - 1455 - 1: The Wedding of Lanya (Forester) and Perspicuus Whitegate
Kythorn 1, 1455 DR Compiled from notes written by Decker Blackmane many years after the incident.
GFD Notes:
I found this in the Yellow Abbey. In its native form, this is a sheaf of papers in a small box, and I am not sure I was meant to find it. I could not find it again several days after I did, and I expect it was moved to the Historic Wing.

Decker Blackmane wrote this note in 1471, along with nearly 100 pages of other memories he had from the 1450’s and 60’s. Most of them revolved around the constant struggle to keep back the oaks of Cormanthor, and dealing with growing numbers of orcs in the mountains to the west of him. This is the only account of the wedding I found, which is surprising given the number of people there, and the long shadow it cast on the dale. The deaths of so many Whitegates and Foresters that day ensured that the events of 1481 would spell the end of these lines.

But again, I get ahead of myself; the people of the dales do not share the patrilineal sense of generation that is so often observed elsewhere. In fact, the enemies of the dale seem to have thrived on a matrilineal and matriarchal system that survives generation after generation.

I am ashamed to say that I didn’t get the chance to talk to Decker. He is still alive, and the head of his farm. A few months in the dale was not enough to get around to every loose end…
-GFD
“It was a fine day in the summer; the first of Kythorn, and no one had the slightest idea that such a lovely day would end in the partial extermination of a family, much less The Family.

We were all at Liberty Hill Farm, and had been for a tenday; this was a wedding that was finally going to see the Forester family joined with the Whitegates, and hopefully put an end to the petty squabbles they had inflicted on us for a generation. I think there must have been nearly 150 people from afield in attendance, on top of the couple-hundred at the farm, and there was no difficulty feeding them; the Whitegates were as prosperous as ever. The noble scions, Loedegan and Madigan were as capable as farmers as they were warriors.

Old Ardelusk always liked to have these types of ceremonies at the end of the day, rather than the beginning. He said it was better to show your resolve when the day is worn than to be optimistic in a bright morning sun. There were tremendous theological differences between this and the upper clergy, or so I’m told; I didn’t give a turnip for the carrying on of those zealots then or now. And anyway, Lanya was from a good Chauntean family (the main problem in the first place) and they always loved an evening service.

The other thing that Ardelusk, may he ride with honour in the world-hereafter, always insisted upon, was a service beneath the Paladin’s Cenotaph. He used to make a show of reciting the names of the men who died so that he could be free, and Loedegan had taken up the same reverence. In fact, I think he moved the times of these major services to the afternoon just so they could be held beneath the Cenotaph, which is on the west side of the farm.

Now, the Sun Blades weren’t what they are now, and I’ll save my commentary on that for another time. It was still mostly militia doing the job of protecting the people, and that’s the way it should have been. Who knows how things would have turned out…

Anyway, the “Bright Spears”, as they would come to be known in later years, the 7th Company of Sun Blades, were the first company ever stationed in a fortress farm, and Liberty Hill was the first to have them. No surprise, really. These men patrolled the edge of the forest all day long. They were accompanied by many a knight; the Order was already strong then, and there were 2 Rides in attendance, and there would have been more if it wasn’t for trouble in the Wastelands in those days.

During the day, a couple of small skirmishes were fought; it seemed to us then that a small band of listless orcs had wandered into the area at exactly the wrong time, for the sake of both parties; we slew many orcs that day, but there isn’t a bride to be found that wants orc-slaying on her wedding day (more’s the pity, really).

I guess in hind-sight we could all say “Why didn’t Loedegan call the whole thing off? Or Magigan or Argent? They were all there and the news of the skirmishes escaped nobody, even though all the soldiers came back in one piece, most jubilant at the victories they had won. We didn’t know what was coming, or how devious a trap the little band of orcs had been the bait for.

So as the sun was going down, its last rays cascading through the mountains and making the Cenotaph light up with many reflecting colours, all the men-at-arms were fully armoured and arrayed. In fact, to make sure that nothing would interrupt the wedding of his favourite niece, Loedegan was out in the fields riding with a group of knights. They were the first to die.

From the bushes, a group of screaming orcs flew into the field, and we thought they were charging into battle. Loedegan and his men thought the same, and rode them down quickly. However, they were not charging, but routing; on their heels were a score of armoured nightmares on spectral steeds, and these crashed into our knights mercilessly, and hacked them from their mounts. I recall seeing the brilliant helm of Loedegan, which has not been recovered to this day, fall to the ground, and only later learned that his head was still in it.

Enraged at the massacre of his men, and at the affront for an attack during the wedding of his grand daughter, Madigan too rode out. He rounded up most of the nearby men, mindfully leaving a couple of

platoons of militia and a couple of knights to protect the rest of the people, who were now mostly retreating into the safety of the farm walls.

The reserves of our men were only halfway across the hay fields when more soldiers, some spectral, some clearly (as discovered later) bodily undead, emerged from the forest; there was a division of archers that light up the gloaming darkness with a hail of pale-lighted arrows that fell among the reserves. Madigan survived the hail, though ¾ of his men did not. To his credit, he never looked back, and stayed focused on the engagement before him; a desperate combat of mounted nightmares and doomed men.

It was at this point that the clergy realized what was happening, and despite orders from Madigan to the contrary, many of them also rode out to face the undead, bringing their divine light to bear on this evil foe. The battle in the field was desperate and bitter, but the arrival of Argent and his clerics destroyed many of the lesser monsters, and drove off the rest. However, that had been the plan all along.

At that very moment, in the midst of what people remained at the wedding tent and tables, which was many a concerned Whitegate and Forester alike, a new enemy struck. Appearing as though from an evening mist, just as the last rays of light vanished, the Greatest Swordsman in the Realms appeared. I swear on my mother’s apple-pie recipe, it was him; we’ve all seen pictures of Dorian, and I was close enough to see the black veins on his undead face, and the cold malevolent eyes of the monster. He looked about for the greatest opponents first, and this as well supports my assertion (and many have argued against me) that it was Dorian there; he behaved just like the hero of legend, and began dispatching the Knights of the Order that stayed to protect us; he made a sport of them, showing them their weaknesses in each stroke, and toying with them like a wolf in a rabbit cage. Occasionally, he would take a back-handed sweep of his blade which would behead or disembowel an unfortunate victim. Thus, Solis and Ardelusk II died, and many a brave Forester and many a brave militiaman.

When he was very nearly done dicing up those that stood against his lone fury, he set his focus on the battle out in the field. I have always assumed that those were his minions out there, though I have some suspicion that those in the field played for the opposite team during their naturally-appointed years. However, he looked out and called for Loedegan and Madigan, challenging them. His minions had done their work a little too well, though; the brother Knights were both dead. Only Argent then lived to answer the call (Luminous was at the Castle, attending matters there with all due protocol), and he came riding back, leaving the desperate struggle in the field behind him.

As Argent drew nearer the undead monster of Dorian, the thing affected a look of concern. The sun again shone behind the charging cleric, through some trick of the gloaming twilight sky or some divine wrath I know not, and it blinded the monster. It drove him back, and he stumbled into the Cenotaph, and there isn’t a soul who was standing on that wall that day looking at that spectacle who will ever put it out of their heads, though we have been asked to do exactly that. The monster began to weep blood, and he threw down his sword and began to beat upon the Paladin’s Cenotaph like a petulant child, and his howling and shrieks of unearthly torment drove most of us from the wall.

Dorian collapsed at the base of that cenotaph, and Argent rode right over him, and dismounted expertly despite his bulky plate armour. He began to glow with Divine Wrath, and again, none could stand the wall for the spectacle before us. When I again looked, Argent stood there alone. Dorian, if such it truly was, had vanished just as he had come, and his blade with him.

With the route of the terrible leader of this undead cadre, the battle in the field wrapped up; many of the undead likewise vanished, and others crumbled to dust, leaving only a handful of confused but thankful warriors standing alive in amidst untold carnage, just as light again left the valley, and all was dark.

Now, I alone confronted Argent about this later. “That was Dorian of Sembian, the same hero that decorates a hundred hearths in this dale, or I’m as blind as a bat, cleric!” I insisted.

“Perhaps it was. It is a sour matter if that is the truth, though in the end I drove him back, and I have a way to keep him bottled up that will cost us dearly…I mustn’t tarry, in fact.” Argent was clearly somewhere else in his head. This is understandable; his father and uncle and too many other relations to mention had just been slaughtered before his eyes, and though the battle was over, he had some secret mission to see to immediately, and he scarcely took note of me when I asked him what we were to do.
“Clean up this mess” he replied flatly. “
“Bring in the dead, and destroy the remains of our foes. I must leave immediately. I leave Perspicuus in charge of matters here, and would apologize if there was time. There is not.” He rode off, but I made a parting shot;

“I thought you Sun worshipers didn’t keep secrets, Cleric!” He stopped his horse and wheeled about on me, and his look suggested he might ride me down like the monster he had driven off. “Just this once, Blackmane, we’ll keep this quiet. Whisper not a word of this to anyone; this dale does not need its heroes made villains, and you don’t need me as an enemy.”

I kept mum about this, of course. It pained me to do so. Over time, the few whispered rumours that Dorian of Sembian, Greatest Swordsman in the Realms, had returned from the grave to destroy the Whitegate family, slowly faded out. I helped them to vanish as though spectral wisps in a gloomy night, insisting that the monster was not Dorian.

I have always hated Argent for this dishonesty, but it might have been for the best. After all, this dale doesn’t need its heroes made villains, and I don’t need Argent as an enemy.
DDC – 1479 – 1: Report from Alystair Dretch to Cpt. Whitegate
Wherein he describes the discovery of the Dark Garden, and the coven-leader named Lotus
GFD Notes:
In this report, the Avenger Alystair Dretch reports on a mission he ran with Tuugan Swift, wherein they foiled the creation of a powerful cult of Shar at Dwimmerholme farm (if only that was the end of trouble for that poor farm…)

This report as well as DDC – 1480 – 1 were both graciously provided by Administrator Reks.

We hear of how expertly Alystair manages to gather intelligence and sends it up the proper channels quickly. He is wrong about a couple of details (such as the nexus of the Dark Garden, which turned out to be Liberty Hill, and the fact that Lotus was a Kenku; she was rather a shape-shifting dark druid that favoured the form of a raven as all 3 members of the coven did), but for the most part, he seems to have the entire thing figured out in Marpenoth. It’s hard to say why it took another eight months and hundreds of lives to root out the other two covens.

Although they didn’t know it yet, their foe’s name in this was the black druid Lotus, who would be killed nearly a year later at Liberty Hill. They had foiled her for now.
-GFD
6 Marpenoth, 1479 DR.


Captain Whitegate;
Tuugan and I have recently uncovered a most devious plot unfolding within the region. Its roots are tied to our dreams, the Dark Garden is flowering.

Tuugan and I began our investigation here in Dagger Falls a few days prior to the Harvestide festival.
*Note: I have secured a room for 1 year at Quick Axes for Whitecloak member use.
We investigated a shady dealing involving a caravan master of the Moon Sea Collective named Tzunam, his Mercenary troupe leader named Yarlick Mean, and a woman named Lotus, and the Dwimmerholme farm. The investigation was aided in small way by Magistrate Invictus and would end with Tuugan and I departing for Dwimmerholme farm the next day.

Dwimmerholme was besieged by foul works. Wolves acting unnaturally, acres of land being burnt, and a succession of Orcish raids were most prevalent.

With the aid of Magistrate Hoetmer, and a Netherese Prayer Book in his keeping, we were able to root out and stop a Ritual called the Ritual of Founding from occurring. This ritual would be used to create a new Sect of Shar at Dwiommerholme. The dream was also accurate in its foretelling.
Ritual of Founding

Three scarifices are required
The first is followed by a boon
The second is preceded by a boon (sacrifice greater than first) The third sacrifice comes before the boon (greatest sacrifice)

The three sacrifices are timed to be one moon apart.

A high-ranking individual in the Cult of Shar must be present at the sacrifices. A Relic must be present at the third sacrifice

The most important supplicants time the final sacrifice with the new moon, as well as other celestial events.

Although Tuugan and I managed to prevent the Ritual at Dwimmerholme, during the second Sacrfice, I fear a greater evil was carried out that same night (Harvestide) in Dagger Falls.

I believe the ceremony of the third sacrifice was completed, a new Sect of the Cult being established in Dagger Falls.

My reasoning is thus; Harvestide is a great celestial event, and the most prevalent event this time of year. It would fit that the third sacrifice be carried out that night. However, the ceremony Tuugan and I interrupted was only the second. It fits that a more important Supplicant was established elsewhere, and by the dream the Dark Garden center is Dagger Falls.

It is also my belief that the Artefact being utilized is The Black Hand of Saint Gaebril. Since it must be present at the third sacrifice, no two Sects can be established the same night.

Although late in this report, I must now speak of the woman named Lotus. She was the high-ranking Sharan at the ceremony Tuugan and I interrupted.

She is I believe a Kenku, and possibly a shape shifter as well, I know she can take the form of a Raven as I have borne witness to it. She commanded a group of Krinth, which Tuugan and I dispatched.

She is commonly seen as woman of height approximately 5’4”, she has short black hair and birdlike features.
Two more women are in league with her.
One is tall and stunning, with dark hair and very light skin.
The other is less well kept, with shoulder length curly dark hair. It is said she smells of the woods.

I believe these three to be the ring leaders, and high priestesses of Shar. Lotus was at the Dwimmerholme ceremony, someone else had to preside over the Dagger falls ceremony.

I need not say that we must make every effort to see these women brought to justice. As a last note, I fear I have more bad news.

During the time of the supplication of Roger Dunland in Dwimmerholme, all messages to and from Dagger Falls failed to reach their destinations.

I hope this report finds you well, I will send another after Tuugan and I reach Dagger Falls. Yours in Faith,
Alystair

DDC – 1480 – 1: Report from Report from Alystair Dretch to Cpt. Whitegate
Greengrass, 1480 DR Captain Whitegate,
It would seem the situation with the Dark Garden is growing beyond Tuugan and I.
This report is not detailed, as we have just begun to receive reports and rumors of attacks at many farms in the region. Tesh Valley, Charity Hills, Liberty Hill, Mystral's Grove, Lost Stead, Gribbons and Crossed Blades have all sent reports of attacks. The perpetrators are mostly of Orcish origin, but there have been rumors of Lycanthropes as well. It is my suspicion that the Dark Garden holds the ultimate leadership, but that is as I said, only a suspicion. I believe it may be time for the Whitecloaks to increase their presence here in Dagger Falls, there are simply too many leads for Tuugan and I to follow on our own.

We depart shortly for Crossed Blades. The roads are soon to be full of merchants, travellers and most pointedly Pilgrims on their way to pay their respects to our Saint. As Aegus Peregrinus, I must ensure the roads are safe to travel. Thus we may not tarry here to continue to gather intelligence.
Yours in Faith, Alystair
DDC – 1480 – 2: A Discussion with Administrator Reks about The Dark Garden
Wherein your humble chronicler records verbatim, and for your benefit dear reader, the memories of Administrator Reks with regards to the woman known as Deadnettle, part of the Coven of the Dark Garden.
GFD Notes:
This is the conversation recorded exactly as it played out, that Reks and I had about the Dark Garden, Deadnettle, and some other affairs around the same time.
