After Banitt gave his moving speech after the Battle, and was invested by Bishop Whitegate, a flood of immigration came almost immediately to the farm. On the day he took the mantle of Magistrate, Banitt presided over a village of 225 souls, most of whom were orphans. As I write this now, the population of Liberty Hill Farm is nearly 2000! Banitt, long known as the ‘Pilgrim’, declared that he was directed by Amaunator to come to come to Daggerdale, and to fight her enemies. He was given the Blade of the White Saint to battle the Dark Garden, and he was meant to stay in the ruined village of Liberty Hill to bring a new light to the darkness that had taken it. His version of this story is much more eloquent and compelling.

There was a tremendous amount of work to do to clean up the village, much less start rebuilding. But before a tenday passed after the battle, the pilgrims started showing up; first, migrants from nearly every farm in the dale arrived. Later, farmers and workers from the surrounding dales came. And before the snows came, and in the spring and summer after they left, pilgrims from distant lands arrived. They all came on pilgrimage to see the Blade, and to get a blessing from the Pilgrim Magistrate

of Liberty Hill. Many stayed. I would guess that several thousand pilgrims have come through Liberty Hill since that time, and as I have mentioned, enough have stayed on that the place is the third-most populated area in the region, behind the towns of Dagger Falls and Charity.

The cathedral at Liberty Hill is now very richly adorned; it has received gifts and donations from every corner of Faerun. However, the centre piece to the place is the relic that Banitt is now the life-long steward of; the Blade of the White Saint. This sword simply lays on an altar in the nave of the Cathedral, where anyone can simply walk up and touch it, or even pick it up. Indeed, Magistrate Harbaugh is often there to thrust it into the hands of the pilgrims that have come to see it. He assures me that the blade is quite safe and secure, and I am obliged to trust in him, though I can’t for the life of me divine what protections he has in place, beyond good will and the forbearance of travellers.

The Tower of Liberty Hill, and the Table of the Sun that sits atop it, were given to the village as a public property by Lumina Whitegate. She told me once that she could not bear to live in the place without her brother, sister, cousins and all the children running around. It is just as well; the Tower has been turned into a public house, with a significant number of rooms that can be rented by pilgrims, for whatever they can pay (or not). The upper level has been used to accommodate Magistrate Invictus, and the dozens of Sun Blades that have been added to the defence of the village. These Sun Blades are from the new 10th Company, “Shadow Sentinels”, and are specially trained to deal with very dangerous and cunning enemies.

So today, Liberty Hill Farm is a bustling and prosperous place. The fields are all under plow, the village is bursting at the seams with new people and buildings, and the concourse-market, a type of open-air affair that is generally frowned upon in the dale, looks like a part of our own Waterdeep bazaar dropped down into the middle of this wilderness; there are colours, sounds and smells from distant parts of the continent that give this village a truly worldly feel.

The prosperity of Liberty Hill is marked with some sorrow, though, which is felt by all. This was the hearth of the Whitegate family; the ancestral patriarch of the family founded this place, and his own account (c.f. ‘Life of the White Saint’, Shefton Dale, 1477) of the matter is moving. Today, the only Whitegate living here (for ‘here’ is where I write this very document) is my dear friend Lumina, and she has stepped back from any sort of governance or privilege. She owns a small cottage at the corner of the village, and though she has a public life, being an ambassador to new guests and pilgrims, her presence here is the very symbol of power-waning.

As sad as this fact of life is, it is just that; times change, and there can be no doubt that the net change at Liberty Hill is profoundly good. It is so good in fact, that when I have concluded my duties in the Order, I will return to Liberty Hill to spend the rest of my days there, and finally to be buried in the yard on the west-facing hill of that happy place.
The Kingdom of Tethyamar
I would probably not be writing this as I am, if not for Tethyamar. As I have mentioned, and has been recorded in greater works, the Tethyamar League won the day at the Siege of Lastsun, and effectively ended the war, for now, with Netheril. Netheril took such terrible losses that they could not continue any sort of aggression. Unfortunately, they have never sent a delegation to discuss a truce, so we can only assume that there is more hostility on the horizon, when they have the means to carry it out.

I will add presently that I find it strange that Prince Melagaunt does not offer terms of any sort; the

Netherese princes responsible for other polities have taken a civilized, if devious, approach to politics. Melagaunt seems determined to wipe Daggerdale off the map, whatever the cost.

At any rate, he will have a difficult time of it, now. The East Gate of Tethyamar was discovered in the Gorimdun Mine by the White Cloaks, and this discovery brought life to the movement to unearth this ancient dwarven city. The dwarves showed up in the nick of time at Lastsun, and though they suffered dearly for their ally-saving intervention, they have continued to trickle into the dale ever

since. Monthly, more dwarves are added to the population of the dale; at first, they settled up at the Castle as preparations were made to descend into Gorimdun. Before the snows set in, several hundred dwarves descended with what looked like a year’s supplies.

All winter long, reports came back from Tethyamar. They had indeed found the eastern reaches of the Upper Halls of Tethyamar, and had indeed secured them. However, as one engineer explained it to me, it was like they had just found and secured the first inn outside the gates of Waterdeep; there was an impossibly larger city awaiting them. However, it was held against them. The depths of Tethyamar had become a thriving environment of deep-things and undead, and they would have to fight chambre-by- chambre for any further gains.

In the dead of winter of 1481, the Tethyamar League officially changed its name to the Emissaries of the Kingdom of Tethyamar. They still hold a tower in the Castle, and have likewise set up an embassy in the Town as well. This spring, they began construction of a grand fort attached to the outer bailey of Tesh Valley Farm, and as I am told, there is a field full of tents surrounding the place. They are calling this small fort ‘Stationer’s Hall’, and it is to be used as a sort of supply-post for the expedition, and also as a trading post with the dalesmen. It has rekindled the blighted economy of Tesh Valley Farm (see my earlier report on this matter), and brought a good deal of excitement to the region.

Presently, there is a dispute in the ‘Kingdom’. The heirs of the Kingdom have been meticulously traced for the several hundred years of their exile from the city; in fact, they have always made claims of finding the place and resettling it. This has been the stuff of dwarven legend and fancy, until last

year. Now the claimants to the throne have come forth. As it turns out, the commonly acknowledged and rightful heir to the throne was one Ghellin Thordbardson of Clan Iron House (Iron House was the founding and ruling family for the entire duration of dwarven occupation of the city.) Ghellin died a decade ago, and left behind twin sons. These two, Tasster and Tezster are not on good terms; with the discovery that they would indeed have a kingdom to rule or to split, they have already done the latter. This has divided Tethyamar before it has even been retaken.

I know that Gambledin has done everything in his power to reconcile the brothers, as have many other dwarven political personalities, but the two remain inextricably at odds, and a layer of complication has been added to resettling of Tethyamar.
Peace and Prosperity in the Dale
After the Seige of Fort Lastsun was ended, and the forces of Netheril were in full retreat, peace and joy came immediately to the dale. By then, the threat of the Dark Garden was completely eliminated; the roads and farms were as safe as they had been for decades. The war had left a robust military apparatus in place, and when the direct threat from Netheril ended, this apparatus was used to clean house, so-to-speak. The mountains around the Castle and the forests around the farms were scoured mercilessly until the snows came that year. Many of these small campaigns forged heroes and stories to

bolster the already-growing collection from the War with Netheril, and the Saints’ Battle. By the time the first snows came, which wasn’t until Hammer of 1481, there wasn’t so much as a single band of frightened orcs left to trouble the sleep of the happy farmers.

The dale had come through dark times, but their emergence from this time was a glorious thing. The faith of the people in the Old God and the New God was feverish and well-rewarded. The summer of 1480 lasted until after the Autumnal Equinox, and the final harvests weren’t made until the end of Uktar. I can still taste the apples that came off the trees when there should have been snow a foot deep; they were as sweet and rich as any I’ve ever had, and are the perfect symbol for prosperity in this previously war-torn region.

Of course, it is quite common for there to be a perceived level of wealth and gain after a war; with so many dead, the resources left are split between fewer and thus seem greater. But I could point to precisely-kept ledgers of the Gate Clerks that will show a marked increase in all manner of trade that fall and the spring after. This is partially explained by the influx of migration to Liberty Hill and the dwarves of Tethyamar, but there can be little doubt that Faith has played a significant role here. Despite the rift that the Dark Garden tried to cause between the Old faith and the New, they were joined together by even stronger bonds during that peace which followed.

The apple tree that was planted by Chauntea in the dale, was bathed in the sunlight of Amaunator, and the ripest fruit imaginable was the product. This allegory has been illustrated in many recently-crafted songs and poems (some by my friend, Troia Trustar), and in the many weddings in the spring of 1481. As I have watched the doings of the young people of Liberty Hill this spring, there have been a dozen weddings, and most have been inter-denominational. It is an encouraging sign, indeed.

The plans of Netheril and the Dark Garden failed, and Daggerdale is enjoying a level of prosperity unseen since Ardelusk’s days.
The Black Hand of Gaebril Tremalkin
Zenith Lord Whitegate made a decision about the Black Hand that surprised all. As I write this, the Black Hand is on display in the Cathedral of Dagger Falls, in the southern transept. It sits atop a slab of the purest alabaster, and is not under glass, irons or locks. It sits so that any might go up and touch it, if they dare. I will back up just a bit, though.

At the conclusion of the Saints’ Battle, and the investiture of Magistrate Harbaugh, that same new magistrate pleaded to keep the relic of the Black Saint beside that of the White, in the cathedral of Liberty Hill. Bishop Whitegate declared that the threat of someone causing mischief with the Black Hand was something different from the threat of someone causing mischief with the White Blade, should Banitt’s ‘security measures’ prove insufficient. So, the Black Hand was taken away that day.

Weeks later, the Black Hand was revealed in its new resting place in the Cathedral in Dagger Falls. The Zenith Lord agreed partially with Banitt; it would be better to put it on display, and keep no secrets. He decided on keeping it in town rather than at the farm, siding with his Bishop in this regard.
The Zenith Lord made this proclamation with the revealing of the Black Hand;
       “Let any who would consider the path offered by Shar come to the Cathedral of Dagger Falls, and there look upon the relic of the one they would call ‘Black Saint’. Let them stand before the vileness

of this thing, and account for themselves the wages of Shar’s service; foulness, corruption of the flesh and the soul, and, ultimately, death at the hands of the Just! Let them, our enemies, come; I will admit them unmolested into our own cathedral to shake hands with their saint, and if they so choose to keep their dark path, they will be released, again unmolested, until we find them again. And if they choose to turn away, we will welcome them into the fold then and there! And let us ourselves not shy from this relic; look long at it every time you grace the cathedral, and consider the ruin that Shar has inflicted on our home. Look, and remember!”
Companions
I should now disclose a lapse in my duties. I wrote to Canoness Majarra in early Kythorn, 1480, asking for an extension of my deployment in Daggerdale, and it was granted in good faith. I had much work to do, wrapping up loose ends and looking at intelligence coming from the front. However, one of the main reasons that I asked for the extension was to be with Magistrate Hoetmer, with whom it is now well known, I was romantically involved. Phin and I spent long hours pouring over the vast amount of documentation that daily came to us in the Historic Wing of the Yellow Abbey. With the defeat of the Dark Garden, the lines of communication were again reliable and prolific in their generation of reports.

However, Phin’s health started to fail the very night he woke up from his Aetherial Sleep, watching over the reconnaissance of the Farm on Mirtul 26. It was the longest of duration and, he claimed, “most profound” journey he’d ever made in the Aether. To comment on what he did, saw, and how it affected him in the Aether would be pure speculation at this point. Phin never told me, and he kept few notes. I do think he had a terrible time in his dreams, though. His ability to help others inside his journeys came at a cost, and I believe that the effort he put into warning the White Cloaks about the trap that had been laid for them was the final stroke.

As we worked daily on our intelligences, Phin became gradually more exhausted. On the 29th of Flamerule, just days before the trial of Belladonna, and the conclusion of his travails, he went to sleep and never woke up. If he knew he was going to pass, he never made mention or in any way prepared for it. The very day that he passed, he spent an hour looking over and editing some notes that he made about his theories concerning his connection to Banitt, Iolus, and the others. He never did figure it out, as far as I know. I am sure it is the last thing he was thinking about as he passed.

I was not the last to see him, though. In his final sleep in this mortal realm, he again projected into the Aether, and had a long conversation with Banitt and Iolus, visiting both men in a shared dream. Both of their accounts of this dream are identical. Phin gathered them on a mountain top that Iolus said was familiar to him. He said he was “glad to be at liberty, even if only in his sleep”. Iolus became upset, mostly at himself at this point; He had sworn to get Phin out of the Yellow Abbey, as he thought he was a prisoner there, of a certain variety. Phin did often complain about not being able to wander outside the Abbey at liberty, further suggesting that Lumina and Iolus were right in their assumptions that the old Magistrate was a prisoner. He just knew too much that the Church could not have leaving the Historic Wing, much less the Yellow Abbey.

At any rate, Phin thanked the two men for their friendship and service to the Dale, and commended them on their faith in Amaunator. They discussed what few unresolved issues there were from the Dark Garden affair, and at length, Phin said to his companions “I see the Sun, it is time to go.” I believe he passed at that very moment, and is now in the Yellow Fields with his Lord.

After the trial and sentencing of Belladonna, I had occasion to travel to Liberty Hill Farm. I wished to see the villainess herself, and wanted to oversee the preparations for her incarceration. At this time, the clean-up of the village was complete, and there was already much rebuilding and many pilgrims and immigrants to the village. It was an encouraging sight, to say the least. Most encouraging of all was my welcoming; Troia and Lumina themselves were at the gates, wishing welcome all those that entered. I knew these women from a few meetings before the war, and they immediately warmed to me, and drew me close.

I planned on staying at Liberty Hill for a tenday, to see things through. I ended up staying the winter, and after putting my affairs at the Yellow Abbey in order in the spring, returned to spend my last 2 months in the dale. I write this very report as I sit at the humble kitchen-table of my friend, Lumina.

During the months of rebuilding and immigration to the village, Troia, Lumina and I acted as a greeting committee. We would see all new visitors to lodgings and food, show them about, bring them to the cathedral, take care of their children, and so on. We met a dozen new people every day, and helped make arrangements for hundreds of them to move permanently to Liberty Hill. All day, every day, we worked at this task, though it was never a travail of any sort; the three of us were so full of enthusiasm for this job, that we were thankful every new day for the chance to do our part.

And every night, we three stayed together; many nights we would go to the Tower, and entertain the newcomers, or just stroll at leisure. Many nights, though, Lumina was clouded in shadow, and we spent those long nights fighting for her soul. Every new day found her as bright as her name, but I am sure that without our companionship, especially that of Troia, who is a peerless counsellor, Lumina’s soul would have been lost. Every morning, after her matins, she would mount the stairs of the Tower, and would talk with Belladonna on her prison. Many days she returned from this duty with a shadow just behind her eyes, and these nights, after our day’s work was done, we would, as I have said, fight for her soul.

As I write this, Lumina is mostly recovered; she has very few bad nights now, and I think the routine of facing Belladonna every day, at exactly the same time (12 minutes after sunrise), is now therapeutic for her, despite the fact that Belladonna just stares back in silent hatred. Lumina has given up most of her worldly possessions, and only keeps a small cottage, in which I shared a room with Troia this past

year. She constantly refuses gifts from the people of the village, usually redirecting them to the most needy families, few as they are. I think our battle for Lumina’s soul is won; it has healed along with Liberty Hill. But there is, like Liberty Hill, one dark spot to be found in the place that has been carefully caged and must be vigilantly watched over until the end.

Of Troia, I will say that a lovelier woman was never born. She is beautiful from the inside, all the way through; she has a soul of pure kindness and she is every bit a credit to Sune. She spreads joy as Lumina spreads light, and I spread learning. The three of us were just the thing for Liberty Hill, to be sure. But Troia had an effect on the people that could not have been hoped for; the weary pilgrims that braved the perils of peregrination and arrived here were met with this profound beauty at the gate, and she

took them by the hand, everyone, kissing their hands no matter how road- stained. She sang them through the village; she made many songs to help people to remember land marks, history,

people, recipes for pastries, and a hundred other topics. She always cleaned up the children that came, washing them, brushing their hair, giving them new clothes, and so on. I think there wasn’t a soul who entered our gates that wasn’t left feeling as beautiful as Trioa herself.

But Troia has one secret that she keeps, from most, if not from us. She spent the

three nights of the full moon every month wandering the dark forest around the fields of the farm. She would be gone all night, and come back just before dawn, to the amazement and puzzlement of all. Her nocturnal wanderings were well rumoured at, and known by all. None besides her closest friends,

Phinneas Hoetmer - Painting by Sara Estelmer, circa 1481

however, knew that she spent three nights a month with her friend, Braxus. Further,

none save the sharpest rangers even knew of the benign werewolf’s sentry of the farm (or perhaps just of Troia.) She didn’t openly discuss the matter, and it would take the most insistent prising on the part of Lumina to make her even confess to the matter. Troia always insisted that her friendship with Braxus was plutonic and I believe her. Her walks have come to an end, though. She returned early on the first night of her walk in Ches, and wore a complicated expression of grief and joy.


Farewell to Daggerdale
As I write this, it is the 15th of Ches, 1481.
I have concluded all of my affairs at the Yellow Abbey, and given thanks and regards to the clergy there. I have offered them hospitality on the Order if they find themselves in our Fair City, and they have likewise insisted that I return as soon and often as I wish. Bishop Whitegate has been a generous

host these last two years, and expressed sincere regret that my time in the dales had concluded. After I took care of my (numerous) final correspondences, archiving, and farewells, I made for Liberty Hill for one last tenday of the springtime Sun on the farm.

I was glad to see that Troia there; her duties with the White Cloaks have kept her away since the weather became warmer, but as promised, she returned for the Spring Equinox, and we have spent much of the day wreathed in all manner of Chauntean decorations; I think I will be days pulling leaves

and such from my hair. The air is so warm, moist and rich that it is more like drinking an intoxicating wine than breathing. In fact, I’ve had a bit of both (shame on me, I know). My companions and I spent all day in the sun, watching young women chase young men in Chauntean courtship games, while the adult citizens drink and sing, and the smaller children race about, naked most of them, like little forest sprites. Truly a day of fresh beginnings, springtime every bliss-filled moment.

It seems odd to be leaving on such an evening; when so much is just beginning at the place I now call home, the place I must hasten from. But duty finds me packed and ready to leave again, and I will not record my parting salutations to my friends and my home. My pen will remain forever hopeful of fond returns.
S. Estelmer
DDC – 1480 - 11: Report from Alystair Dretch to Captain Warburton about the Dark Garden at Foot Hills Farm
13 Kythorn, 1480 DR
GFD Notes:
Here we learn of the foul-tasting denouement to the story of the Dark Garden. This story at least is concluded, if others are not. Report graciously provided by Administrator Reks after quite a bit of drinking one night (it might have been two).
-GFD
Situation Report:
To: Captain Iolas Warburton of the Whitecloaks Subject: The Re-taking of Foot Hills Farm: Kythorn 13th Captain Iolas,
A well-earned title indeed.
As you are likely all too aware, the suspected 3rd infestation of Sharan Cults upon the Dales was indeed at Foot Hills Farm. The investigations of Ms. Estelmer confirmed this suspicion.

On the morn of the 10th of Kythorn Magistrate Invictus and I led a small company (some 300 men) away from Dagger Falls to Foot Hills farm to rectify this situation. I must note here that I am indeed impressed by the faith in Amaunator the men of the Dales represent. Many of the 300 were in fact still recovering from wounds taken at the cleansing of Liberty Hill. Of note are the Dalehearth Companies, having already won much renown at Liberty Hill. They refused the rest they were offered and I do not believe we could have stopped them from joining this company had we tried. Proud men, those.

Upon our approach to the farm mid-day on the 11th, Tuugan and I pushed ahead to gather some intel on the fortifications and the enemy we would face. The lands surrounding the farm showed no evidence that a battle against the undead would once again be waged. In fact, we found very little, until Tuugan

came to me and led me to a desecrated shrine of Chauntea. There had indeed been a Ritual of Founding performed at the shrine.

With this last assurance that our suspicions were correct Tuugan and I approached the farm itself. To our surprise, we did not find the resistance we were expecting. It seems that General Thunderstorm had gathered a host of SunBlades, 2nd Company ‘Mountaineers’. With these 100 or so soldiers he had himself, that very morning, stormed the walls and taken the town. Some 80 to 100 cultists put up a mild resistance but proved no match for the Tormite and his host.

It took more argument than it pleases me to admit for Tuugan and I to gain entry to the farm itself. Thunderstorm himself met us at the gates and initially refused us entry. Being a man of war, not one of faith, my status meant little to him. However, upon hearing that Invictus would arrive shortly with a host of some 300 men, Thunderstorm agreed it would be better to have Tuugan and I alone enter the

town. Our reporting to Invictus that everything was well would, in his estimation, satisfy the Magistrate and prevent any further, and unwarranted carnage in the farm. A stubborn fool the Tormite, but it seems in the end a man of some semblance of thought none the less.

There was a clean-up underway, the bodies of many dead cultists and Sun Blades (from both sides it would seem) were being removed from the streets. Some of the dead being prepared for honourable burial, the others being piled to be thrown upon a pyre.

Some dozen cultists, having surrendered (it seems without the Dark Garden and the Black Hand of Tremaklin behind them their ‘devotion’ was far from what we faced at Liberty Hill), were being held in the town center. My questioning of them was short lived.

It seems that Invictus grew tired of waiting for Tuugan and I to return, perhaps he suspected us dead, and had brought his army to the gates of the town. He was met there by Thunderstorm, who denied him entry.

As an aside here, the scene that was playing out between these two, as I arrived back at the gates, was nothing short of ludicrous. Two very strong-willed men, both unwilling to respect the others authority, stood before their troops and literally screamed at one another. Like two spoiled children bickering over a spoonful of honey.

Truly, Thunderstorm in his position is not required to follow any command of Invictus’.

The General of the Sun Blades makes no oath to the Magistrates. However, considering the recent events, and the victory over the Dark Garden, one would think even a General would consent that it was a victory for Amaunator, not the men of the Dales.

I surmise that Invictus felt the same. He accused Thunderstorm of being a traitor and of harbouring the enemy. This, of course, only goaded Thunderstorm all the more. The two armies, behind their respective leaders, began to form up, loosening blades in sheaths and presenting their shields for battle.

The argument between the two men became even more heated, and their discourse turned more insulting. Neither man it seemed was actually thinking at all anymore.

Perhaps the most surprising event of the day was the sudden appearance of Troia between the two men. When she arrived, I know not; I had thought that she had stayed behind at Liberty Hills to assist the clean-up.

Nonetheless, there she was, standing firm, like a small piece of iron between the Hammer of Amaunator and the Anvil of Torm. She reached out to each man, and spoke softly to them.

I would love to know what it was she said, as both men immediately began to calm. However, I was not given the opportunity to listen. The closest that any came to shedding blood that day were Tuugan and his brother Alaric. I suppose Thunderstorm must have made some admonishment of Chauntea in his anger. The creak of the massive bow Tuugan carries alerted me to the fact that he had the weapon at full draw, and aimed at the head of Thunderstorm. Tuugan’s brother had immediately followed suit, but his bow was aimed at Tuugan.

Only as the two leaders began to visibly calm at the words of Troia, did the brothers release the tension from their draws. In truth, the entire matter is a bit of blur to me. At one moment bloodshed was a certainty, in the next, the entire situation was de-escalated by Troia, the two leaders clasping each other by the wrist and apologies being made.

Iolas, my feeling is that on that day, the poison of paranoia and hatred that the minions of Shar so willing spread infected all present at the gates.

We may have ended the immediate threat of the Dark Garden, but the real threat that is the Poison of Shar is still upon us.
Let us remain vigilant.
Yours in Faith,
Alystair, Aegis Pelegrinus.

1 The Children of Laurel Thunderstorm and Castle Dunvegan all kept their mother’s maiden name.

DDC – Chapter Five – Foreword and Summary
Wherein the lost city of Tethyamar is discovered and attempts to reclaim it begin, with difficulty.

With the threat of the Dark Garden eliminated, and the full-scale war on the front with Netheril temporarily abated, focus now turns to the gates of Tethyamar, and the opportunity to secure a powerful ally for the dale.

Tethyamar was old before the dale was young, though it was abandoned for nearly 300 years before this chronicle began, its legend was never dim. Adventurers and others have searched for it for centuries, but it was the wizard Thagdul that found it in the 1300’s, and the White Cloaks that unveiled this discovery a hundred years later.

This chapter is brief, and far from over. Tethyamar is vast, and the reclamation of it has only just begun. I am sure there will be another chronicle about this effort began soon, and in fact, my friend up at the Castle has already offered to write it, when his venerable order sees fit to relinquish him. But let me get to the synopsis here (it’s brief).

The Eastern Gate of Tethyamar (on the Dale side of the mountains) is opened by the White Cloaks in 1480, during their conflict with Deadnettle and the Dark Garden. Already a political presence at the Castle, the Tethyamar League is alerted to the find, and sends word to the 13 clans spread across northern Faerun, and they begin the migration home.

Tethyamar is found inhabited by various hosts of evil subterranean creatures, and worse yet, word of a possible Western Gate (on the Netheril side of the mountains) becomes the focus of scouting and military activities with Netheril. Daggerdale desires to have the dwarves retake Tethyamar, and the Western Gate, so they too will threaten Netheril. Netheril wants quite the opposite, as one could imagine.
The actors in this part of the story include;
The White Cloaks – who are now expanded to two teams, and struggle to meet all of their obligations. Allied with prince Tezster Gellinson, they delve deep into Tethyamar, and uncover the Caulderwell, a vitally important asset for the success of the resettlement.

The Redjacks – a rival company based in Castle Radiance, run by Hastle Redwater, a man of barely-tolerable character but capable with regards to running a mercenary company. The Redjacks ally themselves with prince Tasster, and take a brute-force approach to taking the Upper Halls, with measured success.

The Kingdom of Tethyamar – the first organization in the dale representing the kingdom was the Tethyamar league, established by Tezster nearly 20 years ago, and lead by the capable dwarf known as Gambledin, this organization was recast after the discovery of the East Gate as the Emissaries of the Kingdom of Tethyamar, again with Gambledin at its head. The Kingdom itself is currently overseen by the Council of Silver, which is made up of the most senior member of each clan outside Iron House, from which the princes Tasster and Tezster originate. As such, I’m not sure we could call it a ‘Kingdom’ in the traditional sense yet, but I am certain that will change in the near future.

Again, the final pages of this chapter are far from written. It may be hundreds of years after I’m gone before the events they describe even happen. But I think I’ve given an overview of the strategic importance of the dwarven kingdom and its relationship to the dale and her enemies.
-GFD
DDC – 1480 – 13: The Kingdom of Tethyamar
A note written by Luminous Whitegate at the request of your humble chronicler.
GFD Notes:
While visiting the Castle shortly before my departure, I had the pleasure of discussing many things with Lord Luminous Whitegate. He provided me two evenings at either end of a full week’s stay in his fortress, and I am sincerely grateful for his time; he is the busiest person I’ve ever met, and he is not young.

On the first evening, I asked him about Tethyamar, and he replied “I’m quite fond of the dwarves, as you can imagine. Let me search my papers for something I wrote a couple of years ago on the matter. My pen is a better caretaker of memories than my mind at this point.” I’m not so sure of that, but I played along. The man is sharp as a judge, even at his age.

At any rate, he provided me with a copy of a note he’d made in the early spring of ’80, which I submit below to your benefit, my dear reader.
-GFD
I would probably not be writing this as I am, if not for Tethyamar. As I have mentioned, and has been recorded in greater works, the Tethyamar League won the day at the Siege of Lastsun, and effectively ended the war, for now, with Netheril. Netheril took such terrible losses that they could not continue any sort of aggression. Unfortunately, they have never sent a delegation to discuss a truce, so we can only assume that there is more hostility on the horizon, when they have the means to carry it out.

I will add presently that I find it strange that Prince Melagaunt does not sue for terms of any sort; the Netherese princes responsible for other polities have taken a civilized, if devious, approach to politics. Melagaunt seems determined to wipe Daggerdale off the map, whatever the cost.

At any rate, he will have a difficult time of it, now. The East Gate of Tethyamar was discovered in the Gorimdun Mine by the White Cloaks, and this discovery brought life into the movement to reclaim this ancient dwarven city. The dwarves showed up in the nick of time at Lastsun, and though they suffered dearly for their ally-saving intervention, they have continued to trickle into the dale ever since. Monthly, more dwarves are added to the population of the dale; at first, they settled here at the Castle as preparations were made to descend into Gorimdun. Before the snows set in, several hundred dwarves descended with a year’s supplies.

All winter long, reports came back from Tethyamar. They had indeed found the eastern reaches of the Upper Halls of Tethyamar, and had indeed secured them. However, as one engineer explained it to me, it was like they had just found and secured the first inn outside the gates of Waterdeep; there was an

impossibly larger city awaiting, and it was held against them. The depths of Tethyamar had become a thriving environment of deep-things and undead, and they would have to fight chamber-by-chamber for any further gains.

In the dead of winter of 1481, the Tethyamar League officially changed its name to the Emissaries of the Kingdom of Tethyamar. They still hold a tower in the Castle and have likewise set up an embassy in the Town as well. This spring, they began construction of a grand fort attached to the outer bailey of Tesh Valley Farm, and as I am told, there is a field full of tents surrounding the place. They are calling this small fort ‘Stationer’s Hall’, and it is to be used as a sort of supply-post for the expedition, and also as a trading post with the dalesmen. It has rekindled the blighted economy of Tesh Valley Farm and brought a good deal of excitement to those fine people.

Presently, there is a dispute in the Kingdom. The heirs of the Kingdom have been meticulously traced for the several hundred years of their exile from the city; in fact, they have always made claims of finding the place and resettling it. This has been the stuff of dwarven legend and fancy, until last year. Now the claimants to the throne have come forth. As it turns out, the commonly acknowledged and rightful heir to the throne was Ghellin Thordbardson of Clan Iron House (the founding and ruling family for the entire duration of dwarven occupation of the city). Ghellin died a decade ago, and left behind twin sons. These two, Tasster and Tezster are not on good terms; with the discovery that they would indeed have a kingdom to share or to split, they have already done the latter. This has divided Tethyamar before it has even been retaken.

I know that Gambledin has done everything in his power to reconcile the brothers, as have many other dwarven political personalities, but the two remain inextricably at odds, and a layer of complication has been added to the resettling of Tethyamar.

As we are forever in their debt for their sacrifice at Lastsun, and our deliverance, we have pledged ourselves to aid in any way we can, ad infinitum, to the rebuilding of Tethyamar, and I eagerly await my chance to visit Thorbardson’s Hall and declare it in the very halls of this legendary city.
DDC – 1481 – 1: Briefing Note on the Kingdom of Tethyamar
From a book of records at Candlekeep Emmissaries in Castle Radiance
GFD Notes:
The monks working up at the Castle for Candlekeep are wonderful people, and I’m under no compulsion to tell you that. They of course anticipated my arrival, and did everything they could to facilitate my work, including providing this and other documents. It is interesting to note that the bulk of their research and archives here are focused on Netheril, and they have largely ignored the people and events that are quite literally in their back yard. I guess that’s why I was sent to collect as much as I could.

I should say that I spent many long evenings with Br. Darred and the others, sharing news from the Sword Coast, and learning everything they knew about Daggerdale. While most of their time here has been spent in the Castle (perched on the edge of

Netheril, and dozens of miles through rugged mountains before you find any other civilization), I have no doubt about the quality of the material presented below.
-GFD
Report Penned by Br. Darred
Committed to the Archive this 11 Eleint, 1482 DR.
The rediscovery of Tethyamar by the White Cloaks and the impact this had on the politics of the region can be found in S. Estelmer’s report, The Shadow Lifted, Part 4. I will herein add to her observations and continue the accounting.

With the migration of dwarves into the region, including claimants to the throne of Tethyamar, the Tethyamar League was renamed the Emissaries of the Kingdome of Tethyamar, and Gambledin was appointed Ambassador to the Dales by the Council of Silver. With this, Tethyamar became an official political entity in the region again, albeit one that was fighting for its existence with its enemies, and among its own ranks.

As of early spring, 1481 DR, Tethyamar itself is a battleground. Only the Upper East Halls have been recaptured, and depending on what maps one goes by, this is only 2-5% of the entire city.
Political Relationship with Daggerdale
There can be little doubt that the people and leaders of Daggerdale are grateful for the presence of, and military help provided by the dwarves of Tethyamar. The Embassy is on excellent terms with the administration of the Castle and the Dale at large, and has a permanent seat in Loedegan’s Hall, where they report daily on the happenings in the deep.

Officially, the government of Daggerdale and the Church recognizes the authority of the Council of Silver, and their appointed ambassador, Gambledin.

Addendum by GFD: After the Governors’ Assembly in 1482, The Council of Silver was recognized as a voting member of the High Assembly, with Gambledin currently filling that seat at Governors’ Hall in Daggerfalls.
Tethyamar in the Dale
It is important to note that Tethyamar has a significant presence in the dale, and that this presence is expanding every day. Since Discovery in 1480, the population of dwarves in the region (in the Castle, the Town, the mines and the City of Tethyamar itself) went from about 30 to nearly 1000.

About 200 of all dwarves in the Dale live outside of Tesh Valley Farm, in the new settlement called Provisioners’ Hall. This camp and building project is a significant trading post (for goods and information) between the men and the dwarves of the Dale. The population of dwarves and humans here are exceptionally cooperative with each other and have a mutually prosperous arrangement.

About 700 of the dwarves in the Dale are in the deep, involved in the recovery of the city of Tethyamar.

The remaining dwarves, about 100 or so, are found mostly in Town, with an additional 5 at the Castle. They are traders and artisans who support the efforts of their struggling kingdom through their

professions. This group of skilled dwarves is helping to forge a solid financial relationship between Tethyamar and the Dales, as well as offering the most significant cultural exchange in the Dale since the Zhent occupations of the 14th century.
Brief and Recent History of Tethyamar
For the origins of the mines and history before 1364 DR, much greater works exist that I will not reproduce here. My account will begin with the Zhent Occupation of the dale in the 14th century.

During the Zhent occupation of Daggerfalls the enigmatic man known as Thagdul found the East Gate of Tethyamar. His motivations for this search have been hardly guessed at, much less discovered, but it is known that his operation had at least three slave-worked mining operations in the region.

A trunk belonging to the long-dead wizard was discovered by an amateur historian in Tesh Valley Farm, and this trunk was turned over to the White Cloaks in their mission to stop the Dark Garden, in 1480.

This trunk, among other things, contained a map of Gorimdun Mine, which although covered in secret runes and signs, was clearly a map to the East Gate.

After Discovery, and the arrival of the Host of Tethyamar and the pivotal point of the war with Netheril during the Siege of Fort Lastsun, migration of dwarves into the dale began, and the current era of Tethyamar was begun.


The Two Princes of Tethyamar
The throne of Tethyamar has been controlled by Clan Iron House since its founding nearly 1600 years ago. The head of this Clan has always been the King of Tethyamar. This lineage has been monitored, and the title passed down even during centuries of exile from the city itself, within the Clan. The last uncontested owner of this distinction was Ghellin Thordbardson. He died in 1469 DR, and left behind twin sons, Tasster Ghellinson and Tezster Ghellinson. These two dwarves are unfortunately not on good terms and have split their Clan and the dwarves who have migrated back to the Kingdom into two factions.

Tasster is the more militant of the two brothers, and a dedicated follower of Clangeddin Silverbeard. His following is the larger of the two and is also more aggressive and enthusiastic. His faction attracts most of the militant dwarves that have come to the region, for obvious reasons.

Tezster is a follower of Dugmaren Brightmantle, the exarch of scholarship. Tezster has long used libraries and other sources of lore to look for his ancestral city. It was in fact Tezster who helped establish the Tethyamar League several years ago; he funded the League and furnished it with all the resources he had to help find key locations.

The two brothers both have a different approach to unearthing their kingdom; while Tasster wants to rush in with as many hammers and shields possible, Tezster prefers to do cautious probes and research. His is a small but disciplined following.

The two cannot agree who should rule as King, nor even how to proceed with the retaking of their kingdom. As such, there are two distinct camps in the Upper East Halls of Tethyamar, and each is conducting its own campaign of recovery.

In order to provide a unified polity to the dalesmen and to their enemies, the dwarves assembled the Council of Silver to make decisions. This Council is made up of 12 dwarves, one from each of the 13 major clans (excluding Clan Iron House) that has come to the region to retake Tethyamar. The Council of Silver is represented in Daggerfalls by Gambledin, who holds a seat on the Governors’ Assembly.


Dwarves of Tethyamar
These are almost exclusively shield-dwarves. They come from all around the Sea of Fallen Stars (one clan is from Chessenta) and the North. The males are mostly large, at about 4 ½ feet tall. They speak a common dialect. They are mostly fair-skinned, with a variety of hair colours ranging from white, to bright red, to black. The dwarves that have come to the region are optimistic and outgoing. They generally get along with the humans of the region and are working towards a mutually beneficial relationship with them, as Tethyamar of Old was known for.
DDC – 1481 – 2: An Account of the Beginning of the Reclamation of Tethyamar
Being notes taken and shared by Captain Iolus Warburton, reproduced here with permission and gratitude.-Br. Darred
GFD Notes:
Being reproduced here were with permission and additional gratitude.
-GFD
Situation Report, Ches 28th 1481 DR, Loedegan’s Hall
This morning I was again diligent in my attendance of the daily Situation Report at Loedegan’s Hall. So diligent, in fact, that I now have a regular spot in the Hall; second balcony, behind the Order of the Lambent Shield. Having come every day to the Report, I have noticed a pointed increase in attendance today; yesterday there were only a handful of people here, but this morning the place is nearly full. The blessed light of Amuanator has broken through the snows on the trails in the mountains, and the campaigning season has begun.

The report begins with the requisite benediction from our Zenith Lord Whitegate, this morning constantly interrupted by the jostling of late arrivals whom I hope will be educated in their manners. The Zenith Lord’s older brother and Lord of Castle Radiance, Luminous Whitegate then made his usual address to the crowd; it is no different today for the 100 men in the room than it was for the 8 or 9 yesterday. He is brief and to the point, and quickly calls on reports from various scouts.

A dozen men scattered around the room step forward to give reports, marking significant activity on the huge sand-table map in the centre of the room. There is much activity to report, as the mountains and the hills around them are starting to come to life, and new conflicts are just starting to blossom.

However, it is the final report that everyone has come to listen to this morning. Knight Commander Cassius of the Order of the Lambent Shield arrived late last night after a hard ride through treacherous mountain paths to deliver his message, and word of his late arrival got around quickly.

Cassius, like the many other Knights at the report, stands in the first row. His men make way so that this large man, made larger for his prodigious and gleaming plate mail armour, can move past, and into the centre of the room to take a spot before the map. He clasps wrists with the Lord of the Castle, who is also the highest-ranking Knight of his Order. Cassius addresses the room, and with his impressive helm under his arm, the face of the man is clear to all. He is not a handsome man; his is a nose that has been broken and worse a dozen times. His face is a map of battle scars that make for a confounding topography, and the one ear he has left is rugged and cauliflowered. Despite this, the man has a bright demeanour, and when he is at his most enthusiastic in his orations, there is a barely perceptible nimbus about his crown that even the Whitegates become distracted by. Cassius is the very picture of a Knight of the Order, and his sanctity is a crown.

The voice of the Knight Commander is loud and clear, but he lacks the brashness of many of the leaders of his profession. He takes his time to choose his words, and uses those sparingly and deliberately. His is more the voice of a patient father than an aggressive warrior.

“I bring intelligence from our north-west” Cassius begins, pointing his sword at the sand-table in the centre of the room, aiming it at a small carved wooden tower that represents Fort Sansum. “Our war with Netheril is not over, but it shall be much different this campaigning season. We will not see armies arrayed against us, or hosts of thousands on the march. Prince Melagaunt does not have the resources to conduct such.

“However, he has multiplied his efforts to locate the West Gate of Tethyamar. The mountains to the north of Fort Sansum” and with this, he points at several key locations on the sand table, and a yellow- garbed clerk quickly inserts little flags at each one “are crawling with scouts and spies. Excavations are under way at a dozen locations. Melagaunt’s Curator, Loki Mouvranesh is conducting this operation. Netheril is aware of the War in the Deep, and Melagaunt has tied his fortunes to this war.

“Tethyamar is the means by which Netheril could march a host into the heartland of the dale. Contrarywise, it is also the means by which we can place a new ally in an aggressive posture at the edge of Netheril.

“I, Knight Commander Cassius of the Order of the Lambent Shield, have been given the task of stopping Mouvranesh before she can find the West Gate. I have the resources I need to make it difficult for her, but I think it is time for some of you in this chamber to commit yourselves to the War in the Deep.”

The room is then filled with dozens of voices, some hushed, many not, discussing this development and the advice given by Cassius. There are heated discussions within and between many groups, and clearly, the politics and strategic significance of Tethyamar is a complicated issue. Finally, Lord Whitegate raises his hands and the room falls to silence.

“Thank you, Knight Commander” Luminous says to his subordinate, who bows and gives off one last nimbus that catches the eye of all in the room. He returns to his spot among his men. Luminous then continues.

“Cassius is right, and his report is timely. I have been in negotiations with the Embassy of Tethyamar recently. The War in the Deep is not going well; the Lower Halls are held against our dwarven allies, and they are in a defensive posture. I am confident that they will not give ground; who can extract a host of dwarves from a hall of stone?” A short round of chuckles and grunts of approval follows this comment.

“But Tethyamar is vast, and their numbers few. Currently, they wage war against the monstrous squatters that have violated their home for centuries. These foes are proving to be difficult and intractable at times. Our peril is this; that Tethyamar is not taken before Netheril finds the West Gate, and either eradicates the monstrous denizens therein, or worse, makes allies of them. In either event, we do not want Netheril in there before our dwarven friends and allies can make the West Gate and hold it against them.

“For our part, the people of Daggerdale will fund the effort to stop Netheril, by waging an intense campaign in the mountains. But we will also need volunteers to assist our friends in the Deep. It is time for us to repay Tethyamar for the Siege of Fort Lastsun. Who will declare themselves for Tethyamar?!”

With this, the room is again a noisy chaos of dozens of conversations, arguments and gesticulations. Bargle’s voice is heard above the din, temporarily bringing silence and focus to the room. “Is there a bounty tied to this call to arms?” True to form, Bargle has turned this into a discussion of payment. All eyes then go to Lord Whitegate.

Luminous looks Bargle in the eye, and the slightest glimmer of annoyance, or perhaps disappointment, crosses his face. “There is not.”

Again, an eruption of voices interrupts the proceedings. This time, a few captains begin to leave, their clattering armour and weapons and jostling a conspicuous distraction. The meeting is brought to order by the booming voice of Lord Whitegate.

“Attention!” he booms, his voice now that of the legendary battlefield commander. None can resist his command, and many who were leaving stop dead in their tracks, Compelled. “There will be order here, even if courage and honour are wanting!” The heads of many men bow in shame.

“There is no bounty tied to the War in the Deep, because it is outside of the jurisdiction of Daggerdale. We recognize Tethyamar as an autonomous state, an ally and friend. We will not usurp their authority with our gold. However, I will let Tethyamar speak on the matter. Give ambassador Gambledin your attention and respect, or I will correct you personally. Ambassador…”

The dwarf that ambles down the steps to stand beside Lord Whitegate is known to many in this room; the Tethyamar League, which the Embassy was known by until this year, posted dozens of bounties, and this dwarf lined the pockets of many a company in this room, including mine own. He is known to be direct and a little gruff, in the manner of his people, but also fair and generous. He is a little red in the face after the admonishment of the crowd on his behalf by Lord Whitegate and begins with an awkward laugh.

“Well, now that that’s settled!” Gambledin begins with a wide-eyed expression of something between surprise and fright. “Tethyamar does in fact need help. The War in the Deep progresses slowly, which is the way our people normally like things. However, this problem with Netheril getting involved changes our timeframe and expectations.” As he is saying these words there is a little bit of commotion in the crowd; first, a dwarf standing with Captain Hastle Redwater of the Redjacks says something that makes those nearby all take him and the captain in. Shortly after that, a well-known scholarly-looking fellow named Brother Darred begins to descend the steps. Before Darred reaches the bottom of the steps, the dwarf beside Redwater speaks up.

“Oi! I’m Crudach Geldrickson! Cousin to Tasster Gellinson! Hammer of Clangedin Silverbeard! I have hired the Redjacks to assist Tasster in reclaiming the Pillars of Moradin, and to defend his claim to the Throne of Tethyamar!” The large, mail-clad dwarf slaps Redwater on the lower back firmly, then raises his hammer in the air and shouts “For Tasster! For Clangedin!”

Redwater draws his blade and raises it and echoes his new employer’s oaths; “For Tasster! For Clangedin!” A barely perceptible grin crosses his lips as he does so.

This begins a new round of discourse in the aisles of the room which is quickly diminished with a scowl from Luminous. At that moment, the priest from Candlekeep makes the bottom of the steps and bows slightly to Luminous and the dwarf beside him. Gambledin speaks up again.

“I see that Brother Darred, Emissary from Candlekeep, has taken the floor. Speak your piece, friend!”

The old monk clears his throat and looks around nervously. The Candlekeep Emissaries aren’t known to frequent the situation reports, and only rarely do they give voice. “I speak on behalf of Tezster Gellinson, brother of Tasster and claimant to the throne. He too is ready to find champions among his human allies to help him conduct his campaign in the Deep, to free Tethyamar from the clutches of evil creatures, and to provide a strategic ally in the war against Netheril. Tasster offers friendship, titles and allotments to those who declare for him…” His words trail off as there are hushed protests and snorts of amusement and disapproval at the offer.

Luminous again scowls, reigning in the room as it begins to overtake the timid monk. Again, in his commanding voice, he asks “Who will declare for Tasster? Who will champion this friend and ally?” He looks first to Bargle. Bargle’s lips press together tightly in annoyance, before he looks about, sighs, and responds;

“My men need to work for something with a bit more jingle than friendship and titles. Allotments we are familiar with, but I doubt most men in this room would find the…payment schedule…to their satisfaction.”

Luminous gives the man a contemptuous look that forces Bargle to lower his gaze. The Knights and Sun Blade captains in the room shake their heads in reprimand, sharing the unspoken sentiment of their leader. Now, eyes begin to turn to the Cormyreans. They have a spot on the second balcony of the round chambre, and their host is always noticeable; Purple Dragons in gleaming armour escorting the reputable diplomat, John Tunbridge. Today, John is joined by General Stuart Angleton, head of the military arm of the Cormyrean Embassy. These two men have been having a quiet discussion between themselves every time the room acted up, and now, they find themselves fixed by the gaze of Lord Whitegate.

John raises his hands a little by way of announcing he is about to speak, then calmly and confidently folds them on the desk in front of him. “The cause of the Tethyamar is just and consequential.

However, I think that the lances of the Purple Dragons would do more good on the open plains of Netheril and the trails of the mountains than they would in the deep.”

With this, the General gives a frustrated, angry growl, and shoots a glare into the side of the adjacent diplomat’s face. “Do not suggest limits for my men, Tunbridge! We will fight in tunnels if need be. I’ll march my men into the ocean or upon clouds if that is what’s called for!” There is a brief outburst of

cheers and laughs from the audience, which Lord Whitegate allows to play itself out; he seems to enjoy it.

“I meant no disrespect for the venerable Order of the Purple Dragons” the diplomat continues, his demeanour seemingly unaffected by the support the general seemed to get from the crowd. “The limitations I suggest are not those of military prowess, but rather political will. King Azoun does not wish to engage his men on a battlefield so distant from his own lands; Castle Radiance is distant already; those mountains north of Fort Sansum are another week away as an army marches. We are too few to commit to such an ambitious theatre of war. I apologize, but I cannot commit the King’s men to such an endeavour, even though I must acknowledge the vital importance of it.”

The calm words of the diplomat have a sobering and quieting effect on the room. Brother Darred seems utterly deflated, and Luminous wears a stoic face, trying subtly to scan the audience for a champion for this ally.

Lord Whitegate continues to scan the room, his clear eyes squinting slightly. “Who…?”

"The White Cloaks will assist with the exploration and cleansing of Tethyamar and will do so, aligned with Tezster Gellinson." I declared.

With this declaration the room erupts into a brief uproar; there are cheers from the military orders; Cassius himself turns around and looks up at me, nods approval and offers his hand. Many of the Sun Blade captains around the room and their lieutenants likewise give a cheer and offer gratitude. General Angleton, standing on the same level but across the room from me salutes and his four knights do the same in unison, following their leader.

From the floor, Lord Whitegate smiles and nods; he looks to me then takes in the support from the rest of the room, and marks with a sharp eye, those that do not offer their support. He and Bargle lock gazes for a moment, but Bargle is forced to look away. Bargle collects his sergeants and begins to depart.

From the third aisle, Geldrickson snorts in derision, and begins to leave as well. Captain Redwater of the Redjacks, who stands across the room from me, catches my eye. He had been cowed by my voice but has again regained himself. He shoots a menacing smile towards me, and lays a finger upside his nose, then points it at me. With this, the Redjacks begin to leave with their dwarven employer.

Lord Whitegate raises his arms patiently, a call for order. A couple dozen men have filed out of the room by this time, and others are shuffling about. The Situation Report is drawing to a close. Before it does, Whitegate says “We thank Captain Warburton of the White Cloaks, again, for his service and the service of his men. And women, indeed.” Lord Whitegate gives me a look of genuine gratitude, which is also mixed with something akin to what I hope might be the pride a father might have for a son.

“That is all for today, men. Dismissed!” With this, the room begins to empty, but there are, as usual, little groups that form and carry-on conversations between themselves. This morning, being the first fully attended Situation Report, the small group of clerics that was taking notes, marking the sand table and carrying on other duties are formed up by the Zenith Lord, and they begin a melancholy but beautiful chant to see the men on their way. Their unearthly voices fill the large stone room and resonate in the bones of those therein, causing our hair to stand up on the back of the necks.

Lord Whitegate motions for me to come down to the floor to discuss things. Ambassador Gambledin and Brother Darred are there beside him, as well as Knight Commander Cassius. The lot of them offer their deep gratitude. Luminous crosses the floor to meet me and clasps me on the shoulders; the old Knight is nearly a head taller than me, and decked in his armour such as he is, seems like a mountain next to the me. His face is beaming, and behind his eyes there is a subtle glow; the light of Amaunator burning inside this man, stoked by the presence of another of the faith.

“If we had ten men like you, Captain Warburton, I think Melegaunt’s head would be on a pike outside these walls.” I receive another slap on the shoulders from this huge old man. “There is much for me to attend to today. You too, eh? I’ll leave you to it and pray for your success!”

With this, Lord Whitegate, his brother the Zenith Lord, and Knight Commander Cassius begin to depart. Cassius stops briefly, and the other two turn to watch him address me. Again, there is a faint nimbus of light about the man’s head, and his eyes shimmer like Lord Whitegates’. He again offers his arm and in the warrior’s embrace, says “You punch through from the east. I’ll keep Netheril from punching through on the west. Deal?”

Standing, arm in arm with the Knight Commander limned in divine light, we were the focus of those left in the room; the Whitegates, Ambassador Gambledin, brother Darred, and the few miscellaneous men scattered about the chamber. There is a certain acuity to this witness, and a palpable weight to the ‘deal’ that Cassius offers; there is something of a divine contract playing out between us.

“I’ll meet you in the middle” I swore. And I will, with Amaunator’s guidance and strength. Brother Darred then speaks;

“I’m sure you’re wondering why it is Brother Darred, and not me, asking directly for help. The matter of the Throne is complicated, as you know by now; Tasster and Tezster will not share it between them, and the Silver Council has declared that the first to actually take Thorbardson’s Throne will be the King of Tethyamar. That is common knowledge.

“What isn’t so common is this; over a decade ago, Tezster actually spent most of his fortune on establishing the Tethyamar League. He himself appointed me as Ambassador, and I have been spending his money looking for his kingdom ever since. Now that it is found, and the race is on to claim the throne, Tezster finds himself short on money, while his brother is not. I am getting ahead of myself, though, and must remember my new mandate; I am the Ambassador from Tethyamar herself and I serve at the pleasure of the Silver Council. Tezster relinquished any claim to my office willingly, despite his investment.

“So you see, I cannot choose sides. I am here to assist the reclaiming of our City any way I can, short of getting involved in partisan politics. I will see a dwarven king on our throne, whether it is one or the other.

“This brings us to Brother Darred and the Candlekeep Emissaries. You have heard Tasster’s cousin declare for Clangedin Silverbeard, the warrior-god of our people. Tezster is a little more organized in his approach to life and is a dedicated follower of Dugmaren Brightmantle. Brightmantle’s portfolio is difficult to explain to men but suffice it to say that He and Oghma share many interests, as do Tezster and Darred. I have facilitated a long and mutually beneficial exchange of information between these

two like-minded men, and now that Tezster needs a champion, Brother Darred stepped forward to take up the cause.”
Brother Darred then spoke;
“I have had a long correspondence with Tezster Gellinson. We have supplied each other with lifetimes of discovery, as one professional academic to another. I only know him through is letters, I am ashamed to say; though he has been in the area for many months, his duties keep him below ground, and I will not make myself a liability for him by getting in the way of his campaign. I am no warrior.

“Someday, though, I will travel to his halls, and spend the days that are left to me translating the histories upon the walls therein. Until such time, I will do what is in my power to help my friend from here.

“I am clearly biased in the matter of choosing between one Gellinson or the other to be king, but I believe that Tezster is the type of leader Tethyamar needs. If the histories be true, it was military bravado that lost Tethyamar in the first place, when simple planning and wisdom could have kept it safe.

“As to what help I can offer you now, I must confess it is very little. The timing of this matter is tricky; normally I would have a number of artefacts to offer you to aid in this endeavour, but tomorrow is our auction, and all we have will be put on the block. The timing of the auction itself is beyond our control. Lord Whitegate ordered us to have it before the Greengrass Festival this year. His motivations for this are his own, though some are not difficult to guess.

“Finally, I will offer the gift I feel is greatest; to the White Cloaks, I offer what knowledge is at the disposal of the Candlekeep Emissaries here in Castle Radiance. We shall offer freely any knowledge asked of us, until the Unmaking, so long as our fellowship persists.”

I accepted the challenge and the help offered and set about rounding up my team to announce our new mandate. We would find a way through Tethyamar, and meet Cassisus in the middle.


DDC – 1481 – 3: Situation Report for Administrator Reks, 29 Mirtul, 1481
Being a note delivered by runner from Base Camp Silver to Loedegan Close, from Captain Iolus Warburton
GFD Notes:
Here we read the first real account of how difficult things are in Tethyamar. Iolus explains the difficulties to the Administrator, and effectively tells him to staff up, whatever the cost.

This note was graciously provided by the Administrator, who seemed over-delighted to show it to me. I think this is the first legitimate order given by Iolus in his new capacity as captain to Reks, and it legitimized the Administrator.
-GFD

Reks;
Paper is difficult to come by at Base Camp Silver, so I’ll keep this short.
We have just been delivered from the black maze of the depths after more than 30 days of wandering lost in the dangerous Lower Halls. The size of Tethyamar is incomprehensible to me thus far.

I report that Bollinger, Durandan, Creed and Guggenheim have all returned relatively unharmed with me, though we needed rescuing by the very dwarves we are there to help. We will tie up some loose ends here, and return to the Close in about 3 days.

We will need to redouble our efforts in Tethyamar; please arrange a tournament presently to select a new team. I am sure Troia will have some candidates up at the Castle. Be sure to talk to her before you declare the tournament. I’ll say it again; talk to Troia first, and get her help.

And start figuring out how we’re going to pay for all of this. We have nothing to share out from our first delve into Tethyamar, and although that might change as we start to make progress, this endeavour is going to cost us more than it gains for several months, I expect.

I’ll be expecting a full report from you in 3 days. Prepare yourself accordingly.
-Captain Warburton


DDC – 1481 – 4: A Discussion with Administrator Reks about Tethyamar
From our meeting on 15 Flamerule, 1482
GFD Notes:
This is another verbatim recording of a discussion with Reks, this time about Tethyamar. I have transcribed it as close to the actual discussion as possible. Note that we had this discussion in ’82, but the conversation starts where the letter from Warburton leaves off, so I have tucked it neatly into the narrative here.
-GFD
Grafton Fitzdecker: I wonder if we could now turn to discussing Tethyamar, and the involvement of the White Cloaks thereunder?

Administrator Alen Reks: Oh, dreadful! Would you not rather prefer to discuss any other sort of thing? Perhaps what weeds grow in manure around here in various seasons, or perhaps some of the stomach- bugs that colour the stools of the orphans? What what?

GFD: If it’s all the same to you, I should love to hear about Tethyamar. There is a lot of discussion on the other side of Netheril about it, and I think the folks at Candlekeep would love to get your opinion on the matter.

AAR: I know when my ego is being stroked, my handsome interrogator, so don’t think you’ve fooled me. But do stroke away, all the same. If I am as important as you say, and I hope at least half of that is the truth, I should give you at least the other half. What exactly would you like to hear about?
GFD: Can we start with the first mission?
AAR: Do you mean when the Cloaks smacked Deadnettle on her rump and sent her on her way? I see you do not, so I guess that you mean the first mission after the dwarves came back, is that so? It is, isn’t it? Dreadful! Oh well, here we go.

It was early Tarsakh of 81’, not that long ago, even though it feels longer. The Captain, who’s leadership I would never question, who’s decisions are as a sound as can be, pledged us…pledged us, you see?

Should we talk about the difference between pledges and oaths and promises and whispers into the ears of your sweetheart? Let’s do. There’s no difference! They all amount to the same; no terms, no coin. Pledges are terrible things, and this was the worst of all, because as I understand it, and I do fully, and I’ll do my best to get you at least halfway to that, this was a pledge made between two warriors of Amaunator while in the warriors embrace…as delicious as that sounds, it was even more expensive.

Some day I shall have to send an invoice to Knight Commander Cassius, who dragged Iolus into this with his handsomely mutilated face and similar words.

Anyway, yes yes where were we? Tethyamar, early Tarsakh. In goes the Captain (though he wouldn’t have been my first pick for a dungeon-delve, but who’s listening to me, besides you?) along with Durandal, Bollinger and Creed. They meet a dwarf named Guggenheim who would join the team at the end of my story, but I’ll try to not jump ahead, unless you’d permit it, and we can discuss something else?
No?
Fine, let’s continue. Our team heads down to Base Camp Silver; this is the big staging area in a place called Blue Balls’n’All, and it’s quite something to see, or so I’m told…
GFD: Do you mean ‘Thorbardson’s Hall’?
AAR: [Waves dismissingly] who can remember all those dwarven names? It might be. Anyway, at the time there’s a hundred or so dwarves down there, in two camps, as I’m sure you’re aware of by now. What a mess! Why a few hundred dwarves can’t sort out who’s in charge is the very reason they don’t deserve to run an entire city, if you ask me, and you have, so I’m telling, and I’ll tell you again, though people won’t like to hear it; dwarves really have no business underground running cavernous cities.

Look at the fine work they’ve done constructing the best stone buildings in our fine Town, in under two years! That is their calling, indeed; to add something to the cities of Men, not to run caves of their own. But you’ll strike that, won’t you? I’m quite fond a few of them, and there is one lass that comes around here I rather like, though they tell me she’s young ‘for a dwarf’, but what’s that to me? I’m not sure what her real name is, but I call her ‘Cheeks’ and she seems to like that well enough. She has the most darling rosy cheeks you see…Anyway, where were we?
GFD: Base Camp Sliver
AAR: Right, terrible place. Dark, cavernous, hot as Avernus haha! You’ll be asking me more about that soon enough, and I’m happy to jump ahead! Do you know we profited nicely fighting the Sons of Bel?

Perhaps not from a human resources perspective, but all the Sembian gold they had was quite useful, and they parted with it pretty easy. Would you like to hear about Sier or Abigor, or Azbael first?

GFD: I should very much like to hear about what Iolus found in the Lower Halls if it’s not too much to ask.

AAR: Well, I should say it is rather too much to ask, and it’s good for you that the shape of your mouth pleases me, or I shouldn’t answer anything that comes out of it. But I’ll sing for my supper, precious.

The place that ended up being the immoveable mountain, as it were, in the terrible depths, is the Caulderwell. [An animated gesticulation of surprise follows for an uncomfortably long time]. Yes yes, the Caulderwell. One of the most impressive feats of engineering in thousands of years of dwarven tinkering. This huge cavern was an underground lake (those terrify me, by the way, and I hope never to see it), and of old, the clever little beardies turned it into a plumbing system; they made a massive pump in the middle of it, and it supplied fresh water for 1000’s of dwarves in miles of tunnels, though what they used it for, I’ve never figured out. It wasn’t washing up, I can tell you. Though Cheeks gets her name because of her tidy little round face, and I’m sure she’s as clean and pure as the water that used to run from the Caulderwell.

But anyway, after the dwarves abandoned Tethyamar thousands of years ago, or whenever that was, the Caulderwell quit working. It backed up with sewage or some damned thing, and anyway, it’s a swamp now. Do you know it’s so hot and humid down there, that it actually rains?! Iolus was quite surprised. That little red-headed-lizard-tamer of his, Guggenheim, he said it’s completely natural and tried to explain condensation to me, to which I explained the only condescending thing was his assumption of his place in the intellectual hierarchy of things, and I can tell you that we’ve never really gotten along well since. He insists that I don’t like dwarves, to which I tell him I like Cheeks well enough, to which he tells me I’m breaking some silly rule of theirs about suffrage, and the whole thing really is a suffrage of sorts for me…[takes a very deep breath, drums his fingers on the table, craning his neck back to look at the ceiling]…they are a difficult people, dwarves. And for all the tales of their mining- begotten-wealth, the only value I’ve ever seen out of them is from laying stone on the surface.

But I see you are again hoping I’ll return to discussing the horrors of the deep, and I’ll wrap it up neatly by saying this; the Caulderwell is broken, and they’ll never be able to get enough water to actually have more than a few hundred dwarves or their slaves…not slaves in the whips and chains sense, you get me of course, but those who take pledges…anyway, yep, it’s so hot down there you sweat without knowing it, and men…men-men…not dwarf-men…they don’t do well so deep. So you need a lot of water, and well, where once was a great lake and machine for moving it where it should go, now there’s a swamp (in a dungeon…how dreadful), and it’s full of Duergar, who are like dwarves only they eat more mushrooms, and they aren’t happy about the dwarves wanting to move back in, and I’m not sure if I blame them. How long do you have to let go of something before it’s not yours anymore?

And honestly, wouldn’t’ they all just be happier above ground, where they can lay stone and friends (short and tall…delicious, so delicious), and have a proper bath once in a while, like my Cheeks? Do you know that she puts a bit of Lilac in her bathwater? Well, someone does, isn’t that just mouth-watering? A delight for all senses, her.
GFD: So you don’t think we should be down there?

AAR: We? Which ‘we’ is that? Not you and I, certainly! Not the White Cloaks, just as certain. The dwarves are supposed to be from there, and I’m not sure they should be down there, but I’d never call them ‘we’, unless Cheeks convinces me otherwise, and she just might yet.

I can tell you this; my ledger doesn’t lie when I don’t want it to, and we’re many thousands into that damned cave, and not a PENNY has come out. Sure, we have some title to some hall, and that’s all well and good, but someone has to maintain it. I for one won’t pay for a single tallow-candle to light it, or I wouldn’t if I had my way, which is usually not the case, and more’s the pity, because I’d have new stuffing in the very chair you’re sitting in as I tell you all this if I did. But no, we’ve got sore rumps, empty pockets, and half my team in a dungeon.
GFD: ‘half your team’?
AAR: I’m rounding and taking ownership, of course, but you follow me. I’ll tell you this; those five men that came out of there weren’t the same. Well, Guggenheim was OK, by dwarven standards, and even most of our own, his personal hygiene notwithstanding, but the others are all a little off, and Mr.

Bollinger, whom I’d prefer to have here in the workshop, has a cough that no one can get rid of. I’d send him to the Sisters at Charnel Priory if I had my way, but I don’t, and so he’s in the Deep again, with Durandal, Creed, Guggenheim and a phlegmy chest. Iolus is back up at the Castle, which is a good place for him. When he was lost, we were all a little lost. If I’m honest, and you know I’m compelled to be, I wrote to Lumina many times that month, asking her what to do, and if she’d like to return. She ‘prayed’ for Iolus, which seemed like too little, but in the end he turned up, and that’s the way it works you see; once in a while, if you pray for everything, you get a morsel here and there and you say “praise be wumpanumpa” or whoever it is you think made it rain, and you keep on, and you tithe…anyway, this isn’t where you wanted to go, is it? I see it is not.

So yes, we have a team down there, and they’ve been to the Caulderwell a dozen times, and rebuked each one, but I’m told their making progress, if not any money.
