The worst of it is that the Redjacks, those brutal mercenaries working for Tasster, they’ve actually taken and held a couple major objectives in the Upper Halls, and they are now gaining ground in the Lower Halls as well, or so I hear (and I hear quite a bit).

So, yes, we’re losing in the Deep. We’re losing money, we’re losing time and people. The Redjacks are beating us, and that’s shameful. We’re getting routed by those mushroom eaters. And if all that isn’t enough, we’ve learned that most of it isn’t as disorganized down there as we thought; there is a deep- menace named Vestibulon or something like that, and he…she? It’s probably a she; the worst things underground always are. Vestibulon runs things, or some cave-version of running things. The Duergar are afraid of her, as are some of the other semi-intelligent things we’ve met down there.

So yeah, if the heat, and the distance, and the cost, and the swamps and internecine disputes, and the dark and the smell and the cost weren’t enough...did I mention the cost? There’s a monster in charge of it all. So I wish Iolus would go talk to Cassius and tell him “Sorry, mate, I think we need to change the deal”, but those Amaunatori never change a deal, which is their biggest strength and weakness all at once, if you ask me, and you have, so I’ve told you as much.

Now, I have a jar of Honey of the Marque and a fresh loaf of sourdough bread that pairs wonderfully with Ferguson’s Red, a bottle of ’71 of which I have uncorked and in peril of wasting, and no patience left for refusals of such fine victuals. Shall we…?

DDC – Chapter Six – Foreword and Summary
Xx xx
DDC – 1481 - 1: A Letter from Andrea Stuard to Alen Reks
3 Marpenoth 1481
Notes from GFD:
Graciously provided by Andrea herself on my one-day visit to Dwimmerholme. I am happy to report that the sun shines bright there, and that the White Cloaks were altogether successful in executing this mission. This is important to observe, as Dwimmerholme was also the first victim in the Dark Garden campaign, the year before. Very poor luck…

The letter below really is the start of the White Cloak involvement with the Sons of Bel, and this new plot hatched by Prince Melagaunt and his Curator, Loki Mouvranesh.
-GFD
Mr. Reks;
I am writing to inform you of a terrible thing that has happened here, at Dwimmerholme. I am sure that you have heard about it from the clerks at the Yellow Abbey, but I’ll tell you what I know, and what I saw.

Yesterday, when many of the families were in the fields harvesting the last crops of the season, pumpkins and some winter corn and such, there was a tremendous ruckus on the road, just to the south of the village. There have been rumours of abductions on the roads for a few weeks now (more on that below), and so Lt. Oakdale lead two squads of Sun Blades out to see what the trouble was.

It turns out this was only a diversion; as the soldiers drew away from town, some of the families in the northern fields were attacked. As I write this letter this morning, the village is still reeling from the terrible outcome of that attack; three entire families were abducted by gods-only-know what. One man, Macalister Dale was killed. I personally helped the Cultivar dress his body; he suffered only one blow to the head from something blunt; there was but a terrible lump there, and no other wounds on his body.

By the time news of these missing farmers reached the village, it was too late; the villains that took them were long gone, and though Oakdale and many of his men tracked them all through the night, they were unable to catch up. One of his sergeants convinced him that charging into the woods in the middle of the night was the worst of plans, and so they returned. As I write this, Oakdale is pacing in the courtyard outside my door, and wringing his hands; he has been up all night.

This is the second abduction that has happened in our area; A small caravan company was here last month, and they were attacked on the road. Oakdale’s men only found the site of the attack; overturned wagons and such. No bodies. And they didn’t take everything. Oakdale has told me that he thinks the men were taken into the forest. There is no trace of them now. There were 10 men in that

caravan. The owner is, was…a man named Belligereath; he had three men with him that scared the hell out of me every time they came into the ‘Hart. I find it hard to believe those three could be abducted so easily.
The following people of our farm are missing;
Dale Family; Aelwyn (Macalister’s wife, 30), Aella (Macalister’s younger sister, 27), Lorella (daughter, 14), Aella (daughter 13), Boregar (son, 11), Suserah (daughter, 6), Jakobus (nephew, Aella’s bastard, 7). Macalister (44) is of course, dead of a blow to the head.

Weaver Family; Dannus (father, 35), Maribella (wife, 25), Dannel (son, 10), Stephiani (daughter, 8), Maxus (son, 8).

Fletcher Family; William ‘Dirty Bill’ (father, 40, widower), Michael (son, 19), Darred (son, 17), William, (son, 10).

The Fletcher boys and their father were also bruisers. That something could haul off so many so quickly is a troubling though.

We are in desperate need of aid. I only write you because I think Magistrate Renfrew is too honourable and capable a man to ask for help. Also, Mr. Dretch was here only a few days ago, and I know that he was heading to the Shadow Dale to investigate something. He was muttering about Zhents and Cormyreans, and said that there were answers in Shadow Dale.
Please send help if you can. I’ll try to convince the Mayor to reward you.
Yours in Trust, Andrea Stuard.
PS; I have been watching Mr. Dunland like Mr. Dretch always asks. Dunland has not changed his habits since Mr. Dretch ‘cured’ him of heresy 2 years ago. I think we can rule him out of the problem.


DDC – 1481 - 2: Excerpts from the Yellow Abbeye Booke of Measures and Surveyes
1480 Edition - Dwimmerholme
Notes from GFD:
I have included this interesting excerpt, as it relates to the size and nature of Dwimmerholme on the eve of their problems both in 1380 and 1381. For the sake of keeping my own notes in order, I have included it herein as DDC-1481-2, as it was tucked into a pile of correspondence that Administrator Reks provided me regarding the Sons of Bel, and the events of 1481.

It also illustrates the level of detail and bureaucratic aptitude that the Yellow Abbey is capable of. The ‘Booke of Measures and Surveyes’ is completed every year.

-GFD
Population: 333
Non-Humans: 3 of partial elven descent, 6 dwarves (of one family)
Governance
Mayor Darius Winters, 4th Co. Sun Blades Foresters (retired), aged 44, council of 5 elders elected biannually.

     Magistrate Ankger Willems (c.f. Yellow Abbeye Grande Accounting of the Clergy, 1480 Edition), aged 51, 3 clerks in Rotation
Military
7th Sun Blade Bright Spears, 3rd Platoon; bolstered Platoon of 5 Squads, under command of Lt.
Kesh Oakdale, aged 30.
Militia under-strength; reported at only 35 men, 30 of which are retired from the Sun Blades
Real Holdings
Class IV fortification, barracks for 150
     Fortified holdings; 147 acres inside class IV perimeter, accounting for all inhabitants and ¾ of livestock

     Cultivated holdings; 664 acres, 1/3rd each in rotation of Wheat, Barley, fallow. 100 acres of private gardens with all known varieties of vegetable, fruits and herbs.
Holdings
     Of Livestock; 46 dairy cows, 39 goats, 88 swine, 145 chickens, 140 (or so) rabbits, 43 sheep, 18 plough-oxen

     Of Common Wealth; town hall furnishings worth 955 gold (itemized in Appendix M/S-D4), common market accoutrements worth 245 gold,

     Of Ecclesiastic Wealth; chapel furnishings and accoutrement worth 2045 gold (itemized in Appendix M/S-DA4).

     Of Military Stores; 200 long spears, 30 cross bows, 2000 bolts, 200 wooden shields, 40 pikes, 26 maces, 24 long swords, 2 large military hammers.

     Of Mounts; 44 horses privately owned, 44 horses assigned to the garrison, 12 horses commonly owned.
Tax Revenue for 1479
Coin; 2980 gold to the State Coffers, 2980 to the Ecclesiastic Coffers.
Kind; 10,000 measures each of Barley and Wheat, 4 dairy cows, 16 swine, 33 chickens, 35 rabbits, 5 sheep, in roughly equal measure to both coffers.

Taxable Revenues for 1480
Possibly 3330 gold each for the state and the church. Suggest increasing taxes for demihumans.
Locations and People of Interest
Locations
The Old Stones – ½ mile south east of the village, just inside the forest at the edge of the fields. A place of Chauntean worship

The Cathedral – 60’ x 100’ stone building; centre of town, extending to eastern wall (access from eastern edge of square)

The Castle – 150’ x 150’ stone building, 2 stories, 3 story towers at northern edge which extends to the northern wall (access from the northern edge of the square)
Amber Hart Inn – See map details; access from western edge of the square
The Market – barn-like building 60’ x 100’ on the southern edge of the square; many businesses inside

Bronze Hammers – small smithy, named for the dwarven family that owns and operates it
Daily Bread – large bakery operated by part of the Weaver family
Butcher’s – busy, clean, unremarkable butcher run by a family with the same name.

Barns – western wall is lined with 3 large barns where livestock are brought in most nights.
People
Mayor Darius Winters – Retired veteran of the 4th Company Sun Blades – Foresters. Young, capable.
Magistrate Renfrew – new, young magistrate.
Andrea Stuard – proprietor of the Amber Hart Inn
Cultivar Marissa Dale – priestess of Chauntea, and aunt to some missing villagers

Lt. Kesh Oakdale – Lt of the local platoon of Sun Blades. Young, capable, wracked with guilt/grief.

Roger Dunland – Son of the last mayor, and one of the ring leaders of a failed cult of Shar. Reformed but now solitary.
DDC – 1481 - 3: Administrator Reks Welcomes Us
Marpenoth 5, 1481 - From the Journal of Nathan Gale
Notes from GFD:
I have been fortunate enough to have shared with me the journal of Nathan Gale, which was sent with a package of other White Cloaks possessions from Charity, after the unfortunate conclusion of events there. There is much to be said about Mr. Gale,

and we hope against hope for his (and others) return. He was a wonderful writer, and it would be a treasure to have more of his hand.
-GFD
Marpenoth 5, 1481.
For what seemed like an hour, we had been seated at the ornate table set in the second-floor dining room of the Close. Stern wooden benches supported our battle-weary bones as we bided our time. Two comfortable-looking chairs sat at either end of the table, suspiciously unoccupied. At the very least, the gradually warming scent of fresh dinner wafting in from distant halls, tempting our imaginations and stomachs, was enough to ease any anxious or impatient thoughts that may have crossed our minds. The proceedings directly following our victory were something of a strange blur. Disconcerting, to say in the least.

Abruptly hurried inside, dried off, dressed in all manner of threaded finery by several servants sporting severely stressed countenances, and then hurried back again up an overlong flight of stairs to be seated for a dinner we hadn't expected with a host who had yet to arrive, despite his being in clear attendance at the conclusion of the tournament. Administrator Alen Reks had invited us to a celebration devoid of any attendees other than ourselves. Or himself. Or anyone.

Silence lingered in the air, periodically disturbed by the awkward squawk of benches being adjusted, forks and knives being fiddled with, side-long small talk and discussion of the tournament battles prior and what, perhaps, has yet to come now that the lot of us stand victorious as the new White Cloaks Bravo team.

Such discussion, however, was put on hold at the growing pitter-patter of tiny feet. A swelling ruckus of children's voices calling out in excitement, arrived in the dining hall, followed shortly thereafter by the children themselves, crashing like a wave in a vicious scramble against the rocky shore of the oaken table. Within moments, the benches were filled on either side of us by an assortment of youths ranging from toddler to teen, nearly twenty or so in total, all of them bickering amongst themselves over spots and utensils and other things of dire importance, including the attention of ourselves most importantly.

(Before we went to sleep tonight, Lady Blackmane explained that many of the children were orphans from a place called Liberty Hill, which I’m vaguely familiar with, but which few want to discuss.)

The clamour died down almost as quickly as it had begun, however, with a high-pitched whistle cutting through the shouting as though it were the sharpest of blades. The children quieted down and sat themselves on their hands and their bottoms, eyes turned towards the doorway they had just emerged from, faces puckered with anticipation. The abrupt silence was broken once more by the arrival of Administrator Reks and Lady Blackmane on his arm, which she seemed less than enthused about to those of us capable of noticing any hint of emotion hiding amongst the statuesque expression on her pretty face. Alen, in stark contrast, was smiling brightly as ever. The elf was well dressed and cut a dashing figure as he escorted the Lady to her seat, afterwards slowly making his way to the head of the

table and his own cushioned seat, eyes rolling steadily over the accumulated faces on both sides of the table as he did so.

Without a word, Administrator Reks reached into the folds of his jacket, withdrew what appeared to be a small bird, and tapped the top of its feathered head with two delicate fingers. The creature whistled once more, a different but equally high-pitched tone as the one from moments earlier, and within seconds servants were sweeping into the dining hall carrying trays and saucers laden with a variety of delectable meats, vegetables and breads still steaming from the oven, placing them one-by-one in front of the occupants of the table, with the sole exception of us five.

The servants sweep out of the room like clockwork, and the Administrator quickly replaced the bird within the folds of his jacket, nodding at Lady Blackmane from across the table.

"I would request a toast," Alen said in a smooth voice, "but with children present, such a thing would be most disagreeable. This rabble is more than enough to handle without liquor thrown into the mix, eh? Ah hah, yes."

And without any further words, Alen speared a piece of potato with his fork and popped it into his mouth, chewing the morsel slowly and deliberately, eyes wandering over the accumulated faces. Hasting appeared to be disinterested as ever. The children were enthralled and horrified all at the same time, eyes flicking between the Administrator and their own plates, along with the empty ones occupying the places in front of Bravo Team.

After an awkward minute of chewing, smile ever-widening, Alen swallowed and sighed contentedly, then waved a hand at the table.

"Mhmm, mhmm, no poison tonight. It's delicious, proceed with your meal." And with that, the children set upon their food with great purpose, and the dining hall was filled with noise once again.

For nearly fifteen minutes Alen and the children were at it, enjoying their dinner while we sat and watched, decidedly non-plussed and perhaps a bit irritated. At any mention, or attempt to do so, Alen would wave a hand at us and place one index finger over his food-stained lips, wagging it back and forth so as to insist on our patience. As soon as they finished, the children took up their plates and utensils and scampered out of the dining hall piece-meal, until all that remained was us, Administrator Reks and Lady Blackmane, to whom Alen passed a pleasant glance, before gazing about us.

"I must offer you my sincerest congratulations, you've all done marvellously. Were I a better host, which I am, of course, disregarding current circumstances, I would offer you a meal, but you five, alas, will not be remaining here for long."

And he affected a shocked expression.

"But what do you mean, Administrator? Which is how I will be addressed from this point onwards, owing to the fact that you lot are now official auxiliary members of the White Cloaks, designated White

Cloak Bravo team. The current state of the White Cloaks leaves much to be desired in terms of competent bodies. As such, you five have proven yourselves to both be competent in battle and in possession of said aforementioned bodies. Therefore, I consider this entire endeavour a success. You'll be walking in the footsteps of giants, my friends, and therefore I expect at least an ounce of professionalism and decorum when representing the White Cloaks. What we stand for, what we hope to accomplish, and the means we go about doing it -- all of these reflect not only individuals, but the company as a whole, and therefore I expect you lot to act in an... approvable fashion. But I digress. This has already been explained to you before the tournament. Pay and lodging and all that contractual nonsense will be hammered out in your absence."

For a moment, Alen's eyes acquired a blank stare, as though he had fallen off his carefully laid path. He looked to Blackmane. Her heavy lids lowered a smidge as she regarded the Administrator, shuddering beneath a generous measure of disdain. Reks clapped his hands with delight, train of thought restored.

"Ah, yes, you won't be here for long. Apologies, I honestly don't know why you all bothered getting so nicely dressed when you would be heading out so soon. I'm flattered, of course, but it was a waste of time. You see, you have a mission which you will be embarking upon immediately."

With this statement, the Administrator's tone sharpened noticeably, and from somewhere beneath the table he withdrew three crisp letters, neatly sealed with a dab of red wax. With a sharp flick of his wrist, the letters slide across the table, coming to a rest before Sergeant Paros.

"The one addressed to you is for your attention only, Paros. The other two will be explained in your letter. Share this information at your discretion, delegating as you see fit."

The Administrator leaned forward and gazed at us over the smooth crest of his knuckles, green eyes examining us one-by-one.

"At the conclusion of this briefing, you will make your way to the servants’ quarters in the western wing of the Close. There you will change into appropriate attire for a group of individuals travelling by caravan. Outside you will find three carts laden with nothing of any particular interest to anyone. You will take these wagons north to Dwimmerholme Farm at a casual pace, and once you arrive you will acquire lodgings at the Amber Heart Inn and rest there. You will make contact with a liaison of mine and she will assist you in your... investigation."

"I'm sure you're aware of the recent slew of disappearances and abductions taking place in the region. Dwimmerholme is the most recent lead we have on these happenings. Your objectives are two-fold.

First, you will be investigating the disappearances of three families worth of townsfolk from Dwimmerholme Farm. Finding them and, if necessary, rescuing them is top priority. Their safety is paramount. Second, in the process of finding these individuals, you will be investigating the rumours of Zhentarim activities in the region. Encountering such individuals is a definite eventuality that you will have to be prepared for. Subdue and question them by any means available to you. The safety of the dale depends on it. For the good of Daggerdale, we need to know where they're operating out of, what they're doing, and how they're doing it. If you have any questions, now is the time."

We basically packed our things, and prepared to leave before the break of dawn, and I now weary, must lay down my head…
Further Notes from GFD:
As it happens, I have the note that Reks had given his new sergeant, and I include it as part of this entry, mostly for the purposes of entertainment, and to illustrate the nuanced nature of the Administrator.
-GFD
Note from Administrator Reks to Nathan Gale,
5 Marpenoth, 1480
Hello and Congratulations!!!

By the time you read this letter, you should be well on your way towards Dwimmerholme farm. If not, what am I paying you for? Ha ha, but in all seriousness, please make sure you're keeping to the schedule. You are, for the most part, in charge of things on this expedition.

Don't make me regret choosing you.

Ha ha! I jest. You have my complete confidence. Where was I?
Ah, yes. You have in your possession, in addition to this letter you (I hope!) are reading, two other letters. The larger letter is to be given to a certain Miss Andrea Stuard, proprietor proipriet owner of the Amber Heart Inn. She is a White Cloak liaison, and a trustworthy individual with much local knowledge that will no doubt be integral to your investigation. Once you establish contact with her, she will be your means of communication with myself, which I hope you will take advantage of quite thoroughly (keeping me abreast of the situation that is, not the lady herself ha ha!!!).

I must stress the importance of keeping a low profile while on this investigation. The hart is quick to flee at the hunter's scent, eh? If word gets out that White Cloaks are investigating the rash of disappearances taking place in the area, who knows what problems may arise for you. We want to close in on these slavers without their being any the wiser, follow? So make sure you put on your clever boots for this one, if you please. Keep your people in line, and make sure that whenever you deal with Andrea, you're certain to keep her position safe. This is top priority.

I trust you to go about your business intelligently. I'll leave the execution up to you.

At the Amber Hart, order a Truestar Special. Stuard will take that as a sign that you're a White Cloak. It's been pre-arranged. Give her the letter. Be discreet. She will point you in the right direction. I've paid her enough to warrant that, at least.

The smaller letter goes to the Mayor. It's a matter of fees. For services soon-to-be rendered, if you catch my drift. Right? You strike me as a catcher, yes. Alright. Again, I must stress discretion with how you go about delivering this. If you're frightened, give it to Andrea to deliver. This is imperative. The White Cloaks are a company first and foremost, and money is something we are most assuredly not made of (by the way, please make sure the carts and horses are taken care of, they are expensive and it'll come out of your pay if anything goes south regarding their condition, short of a dragon swooping down from the sky and making off with the lot of them, ha ha heavens forbid).

We are not looking to milk Dwimmerholme of all their copper and silver, leaving the farmers to fling mud at each other by means of paying for their loaves and turnips. But some recompense will be required. I'll leave it to you to hammer out the details, although I'm certain as the quality of your pay share depends on the amount we receive from potential clients, your motivation on the subject is all but guaranteed.

Finally, I suppose it's only fair to inform you that you and your team are actively acting as bait during your travel to Dwimmerholme. Keep this to yourself if you wish, I could not care less if it bothers any of you. You lot are rough and tough and you like to fight, so I imagine if you're accosted by slavers, you will be more than capable of giving them the old what-for. Why chase your prey when you can get them to chase you, eh?

Ha ha. But seriously, mind the wagons. We're running on a budget here.

What knowledge we have of the abductions is scattered and disorganized at best.

From Dwimmerholme alone, three families have been abducted, and there have been skirmishes all over the dale, mostly on the roads and trails, in the last tenday.

According to a reliable source, an entire caravan vanished from Charity Hill as it made its way to Liberty Hill. Eyewitness accounts from rescued individuals indicated that perhaps the slavers had an accent of a particularly Cormyrian bent, specifically from close to Marsember, which I find unlikely, but foreign mercenaries would indeed be concerned less with enslaving locals than natives to the Dale, I suppose.

But I will cast no judgements, not yet at any rate. Keep me updated. I will keep an eye on things. I have many eyes. Many fingers in many pies...

Oh, and keep Shae away from the money. Fanatics are notoriously open-pouched when it comes to group funding. We are not a charity.

Cheers, and please do not get yourselves killed. Another tournament so soon... garish.
Administrator Reks Marpenoth 5, 1481 DR

DDC – 1481 - 4: Dwimmerholme Farm and the Sons of Bel
A Summary penned by Grafton Fitzdecker, Elesias, 1482
GFD Notes: A Summary of the Events at Dwimmerholme Farm as I understand them, based on numerous reports and interviews with Bravo Team (those that remain), residents of the Farm and experts at the Yellow Abbey.

Some of the broader strokes in the Background have been put together by triangulating many sources, but I think they are all reasonable assertions. It should be noted that I had access to some source material from Candlekeep that rounded out the broader geo-political machinations that the Yellow Abbey may have lacked, which were inserted in ‘83.

Some of these events are confusing, and the finale to this chapter of the Chronicle is tragic, as you’ll read later. Had I the time and ability to return to Daggerdale, I should love to elaborate more on this in a subsequent edition of the DDC. For now, this will have to do, and I hope you find it useful, fair reader (and you will if you are taking up arms in Daggerdale; the Sons of Bel were never fully eradicated).
-GFD, 29 Elesias, 1842 DR.
Background
After the failure of the Dark Garden to infiltrate the towns and farms of Daggerdale in 1480 (c.f. DDC – 1480 - 10: The Shadow Lifted), and with the escalation of the War in the Deep during the summer of 1481 (c.f. DDC – 1481 - 21: War in the Deep), Prince Melagaunt was forced to take a desperate measure. He contacted a devil known as Adramalech, one of the Dark Eight of Avernus, who answers directly to Lord Bel himself.

Andramalech has an organization in Marsember called the Sons of Bel. These are devil worshipers who steal the souls of victims to buy the services of more devils for their cause. The Sons have been a thorn in the side for Cormyr, and as such have been a boon to Prince Lamorak, whose job it is to bring Cormyr under heel. Lamorak has been more successful than Melagaunt, and threatens his younger brother’s position in the council. As such, Melagaunt was happy to draw off these resources that are unwittingly helping his brother, while employing them for his own means.

Melagaunt and Andramalech had a deal (the past-tense is important to note here…); Melagaunt provided the Sons with some resources, intelligence and funding, in order to get them up and

running. He would continue to keep pressure in the Deep on, so that resources can’t be brought to bear upon this new threat, which was to attack the heartland. For Andramalech’s part, he was not to reveal who he is working for. In return, he had been promised the seat of Dagger Falls when it is taken over, and friendly terms with Netheril. This is an unsteady arrangement, because the rest of the Lords of Shade would not support making deals with devils, especially those that are connected to what remained of the Zhentarim (or so we thought; the Zhents appear to be thriving again).

The initial deployment of the Sons in the Dale was in Elesias of 1481. This coincides with a dramatic step-up of the conflict in the Deep, and a vast movement of troops and resources to this front. Three teams were set up, under the direction of three independent Bearded Devils, or ‘Barbazu’, and each were given a region of the Dale to harass.
• Seir – North East zone
• Abigor – North West zone
• Azbael – South West zone
This summary is about the efforts and the end of Seir’s coven in the North East.
Currency of Souls
The goal for and means of carrying out operations for the Sons of Bel was (is?) the procurement of souls. They do this through a variety of means but the main is an elaborate ritual involving torture, in which the victim usually gives up their soul. These souls are then transferred to a Soul Key or Soul Coin, which can be used as currency for the indentured service of lesser devils, or for limited services of greater ones. The plan in Daggerdale was to use the keys to amass an army of devils to besiege the town of Dagger Falls. This was a long-reaching plan to be sure, and never came to fruition, though we haven’t heard the last of Andramalech or the Sons of Bel.

The ritual that is used is called Bel’s Bargain. Specifically, the Sons in the dale had been using it against families, taking the souls of parents and siblings in return for the release of children and other family members. In most cases, these released prisoners were hunted down and killed at any rate.

Those that forfeit their souls become Thralls of Bel (aka Derelicts); they became zombie like creatures with no soul that follow the commands of one of the lieutenants. These creatures were dangerous and likely lost and damned. However, there is some small hope for them, if they can be captured, as well as their soul keys, and then saved. An elaborate ritual by the Amaunatori ultimately was able to restore the souls of a few very fortunate residents of Dwimmerholme, and later, Charity.

By the time the White Cloaks Bravo Team got involved, Seir’s coven had collected a half-dozen souls and was well on his way to building a small army.
The Thinly Veiled Guise
In order to throw people off of his trail, Melegaunt had the Sons of Bel pretending to be Zhentarim slavers. It is well known that the Netherese destroyed Zhentil Keep, and these two factions have been at odds ever since (over 100 years). Furthermore, it is commonly known that the Zhents are active in many places around Daggerdale. As such, the Sons began their campaign of terror disguised as Zhents interested in slaves. This explained the abductions, without people looking for the devils hiding in the country nearby.

To bolster the disguise, Azbael, operating in the south-west, had set up a small group of real Zhent slavers to deliver a few prisoners to Mulmaster. These were intercepted on the road in Eleint, and ever since then, people had been whispering about the Zhent slavers in the Dale.

Timeline
• Elesias – All three covens are established in their zones, and begin doing small-scale raiding exclusively on travelers. The Pilgrim Road from Crossed Blades Farm to Liberty Hill was a choice target for weeks, until the ‘Zhent’ encounter a month later.
• Elesias – Late – War in the Deep escalates – all White Cloaks are called below
• Eleint 20 – A group of SoB disguised as Zhent slavers is taken on the Pilgrim Road and put to death. A small group of hostages is freed and sent safely to Liberty Hill.

• Eleint – Late – Alystair Dretch begins his investigations, meets the other Avenger (Shea) at Liberty Hill, sends her to meet Alen Reks.
• Marpenoth 1 – Reks begins the tournament to recruit Bravo Team.
• Marpenoth 2 – Seir’s coven makes its first attack on a farm; attacks Dwimmerholme and abducts members of three families

• Marpenoth 2 – Seir’s teams arrive at their camps and begin the Bel’s Bargain ritual on the victims
• Marpenoth 3 – Stephiani is allowed to escape from Dungorgan’s camp
• Marpenoth 5 – Tournament wraps up late in the day; Bravo Team are given word at night about what is happening. Alen tasks them to taking care of Dwimmerholme
• Marpenoth 6 – Bravo Team arrives late in the day at Dwimmerholme
• Marpenoth 7 – Bravo Team eliminates Dungorgan’s Coven, and later in the day captures the tiefling, Xaphan, effectively scattering that coven.

• Marpenoth 8 – Pitched battles with the remaining cultists including the command elements in caves nearby the fortified farm – Vetis escapes, but is unable to fully summon Seir, as the White Cloaks have taken all the soul-currency needed for the ritual – victory…?
Structure of the Coven of Seir
• Command – Barbazu Seir
• Captain – Vetis – Tiefling Warlock
• Captain’s Aid – Semiazus – Imp Familiar
• Dungorgan’s Coven – Humans good at disguising themselves to be Zhents
• Sabnock’s Coven – Goblin Hexer with hobgoblins and a dryad Thrall that helps with forest-traps
• Xaphan’s Coven – Tiefling Wizard with Ogre body snatcher
For a final first-hand account of this, please see entry DDC-1481-5.
Finally, a note on the members of White Cloak Bravo Team, as it was composed for this mission;
Sergeant

DDC – 1481 – 5: Letter from Phinneas Hoetmer to Roger Dunland
27 Flamerule, 1479 DR
GFD Notes:
This is an extraordinary letter, as it was written more than a year before the trouble of the Sons of Bel appeared in the Dale. This letter was sent to Dunland (son of the mayor of Dwimmerholme), accompanied by the book “Belial Prayerbook”. When the White Cloaks came to the settlement, they checked in on Dunland, whom Mr. Dretch had some dealings with in the past, and remained suspicious of.

Dunland said he felt compelled to give the book to Gale, who was the only White Cloak that was able to read it; it is written in Modern Netherese and interspersed with Infernal. Of course, this book would prove to hold the key (quite literally in the terrible closing act of this chapter) to solving many problems started by the Sons of Bel, but I’m not sure Dunland did Gale good service in the end…
-GFD


Master Dunland;
I am not sure why I am sending you this, but I feel you will need it more than I. Maybe not right away, but you will have cause to use it, or to put it to use sometime in the future. It is a diabolical looking thing, I know, and the title is a little frightening. But, rest assured this is a work of disciplined academia. This is not a magical book in any way, but one that explains a terrible magic, and some other foul things besides.

Put it aside, and let none know that you have it. You will know when it is time to put it to use. Until we meet again,
Phin Hoetmer.
27 Flamerule, 1479 DR.


DDC – 1481 - 6: Incomplete Salvation – A summary of the closing events of the Dwimmerholme Abductions
9 Marpenoth, 1481 - Journal of Nathan Gale
From GFD:
Another entry from the journal of the missing gunslinger…
-GFD

The 8th of Marpenoth was the bloodiest day any of us have ever seen. It started with the frontal assault on the cave-network in which Vetis was hiding his command-element of the coven. Bolstered by the Sun Blades assigned to help us, we managed to slaughter dozens of cultists and evil creatures in the cave and woods nearby.

Using the intelligence from Xaphan, we were able to set up an ambush on Vetis and the rest of his minions as they teleported from Dwimmerholme. A slow, steady effusion of blood followed, as we cut down wave after wave of villains as they attempted their escape from Dwimmerholme. The victory would have been decisive, if not for the liberty of Xaphan and the unnamed female tiefling that managed an escape from the cave.

(From GFD: The female tiefling was Vetis, and she remains at large as I write this.)

The 9th was a day of convalescence for the town and ourselves. Some of us had a hard time coming to grips with what we had seen; children turned into soulless husks, families destroyed, souls being taken from a sea of torment on a fiendish world. But there was still work to do. Late in the day, a platoon of Foresters from the 4th Company arrived in Dwimmerholme exactly on schedule. Knowing that there was still one small group of cultists in the woods, and 4 citizens still unaccounted for, we set off in the middle of the night to finish this nasty business.

By the first rays of light on the morning of the 10th, us and our escort of 24 Foresters surrounded the last encampment of Sons of Bel. Lt. Leedo Forester, the commanding officer of the platoon, had been told by Mayor Winters (who had been his commanding officer in the Foresters only two years previous) to give tactical authority to White Cloak Sgt. Paros. So it was that Paros came up with a plan to send in our team to secure the citizens (husks and intact alike), before the Foresters closed in. In the end, all the citizens were safe and secure, and the platoon of Foresters destroyed the cultists to a man. We found that the remaining cultists here were more men masquerading as Zhents. They had actually been under the command of Doghan, who we had killed early in the campaign. They did have one interesting ‘husk’ with them; a dryad that they used to control the forest to hinder the travel of the enemies of the
cult. Without Doghan to command it, however, it had been inert since his death.
(GFD: ‘Doghan is actually Dungorgan, and Gale is mistaken about it being him that controlled the Dryad Husk, but all’s well that ends well…)

Our team returned with the Foresters and the citizens by mid-day on the 10th. A package had arrived for me earlier in the day. I opened it to find that it was a copy of a ritual called the ‘Prayer of Adduction’, from the booked called the ‘Codex of Prayer’ that I had learned of. I brought the prayer to the local Magistrate, Renfrew, who then assembled as much clergy as he could to begin the

prayers. The ritual took many hours for each derelict body, and so the ritual went on well into the 12th of Marpenoth, with an exhausted clergy returning the souls of 7 victims.

Though 7 people had their souls brought back to their bodies, at the end of the day, the biggest challenge was attempting the ritual on the derelict of the dryad. Several attempts were made to free the soul of the creature, but by the witching hour, Renfrew announced that the ritual could not help a fey being. She was taken out of town, and burned in a field. Many stood on the walls and towers of the town to watch the distant pyre; the last bitter flames of this devastating tragedy.

As the flames from the dryad’s pyre began to dwindle, the light of day struck on the 12th. People flocked to the small cathedral of Amaunator in such numbers as Dwimmerholme had never experienced. Renfrew, exhausted from days of praying, seemed completely refreshed when so many parishioners came for morning prayer. As he was greeting the flock gathering on the steps of his small cathedral, Paros and I both decided it was time to leave. There were loose ends to wrap up, and reports to write. “After Matins” was the retort of the Avenger, who was already walking towards the rest of the Amaunatori.

The rest of us packed up our things in the cool morning of late fall, awaiting Shea’s return from what turned out to be the longest sermon of Renfrew’s career. By the time it was done, all of us were at the gates, packed and ready to go. She came out of the cathedral, embraced both the Magistrate and the Mayor, and then strode towards us.

“A new day has fallen on Dwimmerholme. Everything will be just fine” Shea said. The morning light reflecting off her eyes made it impossible to look straight at her.

With that, we are off for Daggerfalls, to check in with Reks, and follow up on some other leads that we expect are related to other branches of these Sons of Bel.
Below is a list of the outcomes for all of the victims involved.
Dale Family (At the hunting lodge)
• Father: Macalister (40). Dead; killed in the fields by mistake.
• Mother: Aelwyn (30). Rescued
• Sister: Aella (27). Rescued
• Daughter: Lorella (14). Derelict – Burned by Bravo Team
• Daughter: Aellia (13). Rescued
• Son: Boregar (11). Freed of his sister, but hunted and killed.
• Daughter: Suserah (6). Freed of her cousin Jake, hunted and killed.
• Nephew: Jake (7). Derelict – Burned by Bravo Team
• There were also 2 derelicts that were caravaners at the site – Burned by Bravo Team
Weaver Family (at the cave)
• Father: Dannus (35). Became derelict for his daughter, Stephiani – Soul rescued
• Mother: Maribella (25). Became derelict for her son, Max – Soul rescued
• Son: Danibus (10). Rescued
• Son: Max (8). Freed of his mother, but hunted and killed.
• Daughter: Stephiani (7). Freed of her father; allowed to escape.
Fletcher Family (in the woods – rescued by Foresters and Bravo Team)

• Father: William “Dirty Bill” (40). Rescued
• Son: Walter (19). Soul rescued
• Son: Darred (17). Rescued
• Son: Michael (10). Freed of his brother, hunted and killed.
• There were also 4 caravaners made derelict, who had their souls rescued
   • The ritual was found to be ineffectual for the dryad, who was burned outside of Dwimmerholme N.Gale
9 Mpnth, 81
DDC – 1481 – 7: Report on the Essential Elements of Charity
A report about the obscure town known to the Dalesmen as Charity Hills Farm, 1st Alturiak, 1481 DR
GFD Notes:
I was delighted to find another report from Sarah Estelmer, who’s work drew me to this project in the first place. Herein, she is simply covering off a check-list of places to go and people to see shortly before she departs the Dale for good, on her journey back to Waterdeep.

The Yellow Abbey does not extend its book of surveys and measures to the settlement of Charity, and as far as I know, this is the most detailed account of the workings of this curious town this side of Westgate.

It should also be noted that she seemed to trust Basil Muloch, who would become one of the most vital correspondents in the struggle with the Sons of Bel in 1481. He came to a bad end, unfortunately…
-GFD
Preface
I should begin by saying straight away that my time in Charity was very brief, and not as productive as I would have liked. Our contact, Basil Muloch, was actually away from town; I had taken for granted that most people of this town do not travel and was disappointed to learn that he was away in Cormyr and was not due to return until spring had loosed the grip of winter on the roads. I could not gain access to Earl Muloch’s chambres, and could not, therefore, verify the facts which I was sent to investigate.

However, knowing that so few documents existed about Charity, I decided to stay on for as long as they would tolerate me in that town. That was exactly a tenday in the coldest weather (both of nature and of company) of Hammer that I have ever experienced.

The information I provide below has been committed to our archives only; there has been no copy left in-situ, as I regard this work as something of an unverified document, awaiting those better than I to complete. Ideas half formed are more dangerous than those left in the void altogether.

A brief work demands a brief preface, and so I commit this work to our archives presently.


Sr. Sp. S. Estelmer
1 Alturiak, 1481 DR.


Charity
On all the maps of Daggerdale in the current century, the town of Charity is noted as ‘Charity Hills Farm’, in the cartographical taxonomical system of the culture of that dale in this age. However, those that live there simply call it ‘Charity’.

Charity is the oddest of the farming villages of the dale. Like the others, it is a walled settlement that is largely self-sufficient. It is steeped in agricultural and resource-gathering endeavours and has a strong militaristic background. However, the place has an air all its own.

Charity was founded in 1388 by a group of families from the Dragon-Coast city of Westgate. These settlers brought their own culture with them, and it has endured through several generations; the names, buildings, religions, speech, and every aspect of life in Charity is profoundly different from that in the rest of the dales.

The walled settlement itself is home to over 3000 permanent inhabitants, with several hundred working in the rich mines and other resource operations of the area. This makes it the second largest settlement in the dale, behind Dagger Falls . The town straddles the Charnel River and is enclosed by a network of walls from the various stages of the town’s growth. There are over one hundred buildings within the walls, and almost all are stone structures built in the tall row-house fashion of Westgate. The streets are expertly cobbled, and wrought iron lamps burn oil at every street corner.

The people of the town stratify themselves into three different castes; landmen, middlemen, and freemen. Lower castes give complete deference to their betters, though even the dirtiest coal-mining freeman can be heard to say ‘better to be free of Charity, than lord o’ the Falls’. All Charity folk are xenophobic in the extreme, and they are not given to travel; hardly any have friends or relations even in the nearby settlement of Liberty Hill. These people have a very strong accent which quickly betrays them in the rare occasions they are encountered outside of their settlement. They are proud to a fault, and it is not uncommon for this pride, combined with a clashing of ideas and alcohol in the taverns of the dale, to result in brawls between the Charity men and others on the rare occurrence of their meeting.

Charity is wealthy. Everyone in Daggerdale knows it, because just about everyone in the dale burns coal from their mines, has steel and brass from their forges, and oil from their retorts. Charity is also known to produce the best quality wool as a result of their other big industry; innovation.

The original settlers of the region brought the religions of knowledge with them, including Gond. As such, this small settlement has always been open to learning, invention and change. They have produced complicated processes for refining ‘candle coal’ into the oil that is now common in the dale. They produce steel in a process they call ‘cementing’, and brass in a similar process. They produce gunpowder in such a quantity that they have a militia almost entirely armed with firearms. The result of these innovations, combined with the vast resources of the area has been economic prosperity that is utterly unknown in this part of the world. The homes of all landmen and middlemen are appointed in a fashion that exceeds that of the finest homes in the rest of the dale, and even the homes of most freemen are comfortable and well lit.


Brief History
In 1388, the families of four retired sea captains from the navy of the city of Westgate migrated to the area at the end of a very successful naval campaign. The original caravan of settlers numbered over 100, with all the attendants and staff belonging to the families. Though it has never been proven, it is suspected that the navy captains knew of the deposits of minerals in the area

that are needed to make the precious gun powder that they had grown fond of during their campaign.

Right away, construction of a stout fortress was begun on a strategic hill overlooking a fertile valley, with line of sight to most of the key strategic resources and militarily important sites in the region. This keep would later become known as Silverstar Keep.


The settlement established good trade relations with the towns of Dagger
Falls and Shadowdale immediately, beginning the prosperity that it has enjoyed

Muloch Coat of Arms

for nearly 100 years. At least one of the original four families were devoted followers of Waukeen, and that religion is openly accepted and encouraged to this day.

The region as a whole was relatively peaceful until the 1400’s. Even the catastrophic events involving Mystra and Lathander which had some impact on the rest of the dale, had essentially no impact on Charity, as these gods did not factor into the religious makeup of the settlement.

The 15th Century DR in the dale began with the siege of Dagger Falls by the orc warlord, Zguumush.

This siege was masterminded by the ambitious Netherese prince, Melagaunt, and this conflict is ongoing to this day. At the time, the Whitegate Family was firmly entrenched as the leaders of the Dale, though they had aloof relations with the Westgate families of Charity. However, Ardelusk sent an appeal to Lord Falconer, then Chancellor of Charity, to come to his aid in lifting the siege. Falconer agreed, under certain terms; specifically that Charity would always remain free of the governmental and religious structures of Daggerdale. The men of Charity brought their guns and lifted the siege, and the settlement has maintained its independence ever since.

In the 1420’s, the population of orcs and other creatures in the nearby mountains had grown to such a degree that they flowed forth like a plague. For nearly 10 years, the old captains and their sons held Silverstar Keep against the onslaught of orcs and other monsters, their guns and firearms proving more than a match for the vast hordes set against them. During this time, the military structure of the

settlement (more on that below) was forged and tempered, and remains the same to this day. Charity has prided itself on its military accomplishments ever since.

Between the intense fighting of the ‘20’s and the current day, there has been sporadic light military conflict in the area, mostly echoing the demographics and politics of the nearby bands of orcs.

However, there has been no significant threat to the settlement in this time, and it is believed that prince Melagaunt sees Charity as a waste of resources. Some believe that the relative peace around Charity is the result of secret treaties that the Lords of the town have with Melagaunt, rather than the deterrent of the military prowess of the men of Charity. The heterogeneous and xenophobic nature of Charity does little to dispel such speculations.


Religion
Selune is the main religion among the landmen and middlemen of Charity. All the settling families worshiped Selune as the prime religion of their native city. Selune is also the second-most important deity for sailors and was a natural fit for the old captains. The local temple to Selune is a beautiful structure that has a small, elite order of soldiers called ‘Silver Stars’ that have defended it and the rest of the settlement for decades.

Gond the Wonderbringer figures heavily into this settlement; Charity has been a home to invention since its founding and remains so today. Though there is only a very small clergy, all in the town praise Gond for the innovations which make their lives safe and comfortable.

Denier, the Scribe of Oghma, is an important figure in Charity. Children of all castes are required to attend school until they are 13, and there has always been a culture of learning and intellect among the landmen of Charity.


Waukeen is one of the driving forces behind the success of Charity. While Gond has provided miraculous inventions, it is Waukeen that has allowed the

Whitmore Coat of Arms

town to exploit them in a mercantile fashion. Waukeen is largely worshiped by the growing caste of middlemen, and the success of these men, visible to the rest of the dale when they travel with their wares, is beginning to take root in Dagger Falls and some other places.

The Red Knight is the primary military deity of Charity. The armed forces of the town have always been ordered into the traditional structures of armed lords and their men-at-arms. Discipline, superior firepower and the tactical prowess granted by the Red Knight have always kept Charity safe. Even the lowest-ranking soldiers pray to the Red Knight to inspire their captains and lords to give good orders in battles. Other military traditions and religions are mostly kept out of the fighting ranks, for fear of challenges to the chain of command and the primacy of armed lords.

Originally accepted by the landmen of the town because of her resolute opposition to Shar, Sharess has grown to become the primary deity of the large caste of freemen. Most freemen and their families are hard working people who attempt to enjoy their free time as much as possible. This has made the Old Fort Festhall (the temple to Sharess) a lively and prosperous place, and a key political as well as religious site in the town.

Kelemvor is venerated by all in the town, in the Westgate fashion. All burials are proceeded over by the local clergy of the Grey Lord, and all dead are buried in the Potter’s Field.

Ilmater has a strange hold on the town; a sizeable monastery, once located at the edge of town, but now within the most recent ring of walls, contains a moderately sized clergy for such a small settlement. The place has the unfortunate name ‘Charnel Priory’ after the river it sits upon, and it is home to the sick, elderly, orphans, the mad and even many lepers. It has long been a place of pilgrimage for many sick or desperate in the dale who know the reputation of this beneficent organization. The Priory is supported by the other faiths in the town, and by the charity of the Lords and even some middlemen. It should be noted that this Priory is gaining notice among greater theological institutions as a place of exemplary pastoral care, and its leaders, being by nature of the town itself, well educated, are known as peers among even local Loremasters.

GFD Notes: Charnel Priory has a relic from St. Maturin, specifically his lion-pelt cloak, which is used to treat the sickest patients.

Siamorphe is worshiped by the landmen of Charity. A marriage between the Falconer Family and the Maernos family of Waterdeep before the migration to Charity brought this Sword Coast religion to Westgate. This religion took hold in Westgate during the 1380’s political conflicts of that city of the time. The families that left Westgate for Charity were all royalists who supported King Verovan, and their descendants in Charity are still known to honour his name, and venerate Siamorphe, who eternally supports the rights of Noble Rule.

Amaunator has the smallest presence here of any settlement in the dales. There is a beautiful church that was built in the 1450’s, but the locals all call it ‘the embassy’, which underlines both the outside nature of this religion in the town, and the local xenophobia of such. Still, this church enjoys good relations with the other faiths in Charity. It does not have any official political power, and the Magistrate is likewise called ‘ambassador’ by the locals, and functions more like a dignitary than a spiritual leader. There are almost no locals in the body of this church, and none at all in the clergy.

Beshaba has an interesting relationship in Charity. The people of Westgate, mariners especially, often invoke Beshaba’s name in both curses and oaths. While there is no formal church or clergy in Charity, the name crosses the lips of many, especially the lower castes.


Resources and Industry
The resources that brought the Westgate families to the region in the 14th century continue to make Charity the most prosperous town in the dale. The hills of the area are rich in many minerals and coal. The iron mines of the area and the coal mines are the largest sources of revenue. Copper and zinc are also both mined in great quantities.

The hills of the region provide excellent conditions for sheep and cattle. While they do not export livestock or meat, the men of Charity do export wool, though exclusively in refined form as finished yarn which they produce on sophisticated looms.

Agriculturally, Charity is known best for its animal husbandry, and is not known to export any crops at all. However, they do grow a hearty breed of hops that they use in their copious brewing of beer. They

produce barely enough grains to feed the town, and not enough of anything else. They import food stuffs from nearby Liberty Hill, which they buy with coal and oil. The only foods they export are beers and cheese.

Charity is best known for its metals. It produces vast quantities of wrought iron, brass and steel. Great foundries are found at all mine sites, having been moved out of the town proper over 20 years ago because of the poisonous fogs that were produced. The town exports only refined ores and finished products. They trade ingots of iron and brass to both Shadowdale and Dagger Falls, but only trade steel as refined goods such as knifes, swords, spear tips, and so on.

Glass is also a well-known commodity from Charity. The sands on the banks of the Charnel are ideal for the blowing of glass, and the town has provided glass and glass products to the dale from the very first years of its settlement. In the town itself, most window openings are filled with the characteristic diamond-leaded glass patterns that typify the common architecture.


Politics
The citizens of this settlement, from the lowest freeman to the Chancellor, all declare loyalty to King Verovan II of Westgate. They hold several letters patent from King Verovan

I, declaring the region part of the Verovan Dukedom. As such, Verovan is both their king and their duke, and all titles flow from his grace. Four families (Falconer, Ferguson, Muloch & Whitmore) hold lands in the region that they call ‘Earldoms’, and each family has an Earl at its head (always a male, not necessarily the eldest; the system of primogeniture is unclear in this curious place).


It should be noted that these Earls control tracts of land that would be considered small in their native Westgate. The titles themselves were likely honorary titles given because of the military accomplishments of the men that settled this region.



Falconer Coat of Arms

A Chancellor is appointed by the King every Shield Meet, usually by remote correspondence. The Chancellor acts as the head of the polity, but in reality, is more of a chairman in the highest court, called the Royal Assembly. Here, only men with titles are permitted, and the highest-level decisions about Charity are made.

Below the Royal Assembly is the Common Assembly, in which 33 middlemen, some with titles such as baron or knight, hold office. The day-to-day decisions for Charity are made here. This Assembly elects a Speaker every year. The Speaker is the only real full-time politician in the town, and could be thought of as something akin to a mayor.

Below the Common Assembly is the Labour Assembly, which has a representative from each of the trade guilds in town. There are 15 guilds, and they are all powerful organizations; citizens earn the title ‘free’ from membership in a guild. While middlemen and landmen inherit their titles, freemen must earn their title by membership in a guild. The guilds have been a powerful force in both politics and finance in the town; they underwrite many developments for their members, and ensure the quality of

goods that are created and more importantly, exported from Charity. The Labour Assembly has no head, but rather a Secretary, that reports to the Common Assembly when it
sits.



Military
All armed men in this settlement belong to the personal army of one of the four Earls. The size of these forces varies tremendously; the largest and most prosperous house, Falconer, has 80 full time soldiers, and perhaps as many as 200 militia (summoned from the freemen living on the properties of the Earl).

The head of each military force is the Earl himself, and to be sure, every Earl is a veteran of many battles, and is both physically and tactically fit to lead.







Ferguson Coat of Arms

Beneath the Earls are the knights of his household, which may or may not be blood. These are mounted soldiers that all have a small group of mounted, professional soldiers attached to them, as well as a larger number of footmen (both professional and militia).

All houses have at least one company of artillerists that operate the cannons and other war machines that each house is responsible for maintaining.

All soldiers, both foot and mounted, train with the ubiquitous firearms which the town produces. Mounted soldiers tend to carry one or more pistols, while ranks of foot set up columns of rifles.

The land around the town itself is divided into four Earldoms, in which you can routinely find patrols from the livery of their commander. In the town itself, these liveried soldiers are usually only seen in the inner bailey of the old town, close to the homes of the Earls. It is customary for the Chancellor to provide the policing of the rest of the town through his own expense, and his men are ‘dressed down’, as they put it, in the livery of the town itself (field and emblem inset).


The town does have a small and professional police force that is organized
by the Common Assembly. The Constable is the head of this small force of a half dozen men armed with clubs, and although these are all freemen, they are professional, intelligent men who keep the town orderly.
Personal Economies


Charity Coat of Arms


• Freemen (i.e. miners and other labourers, soldiers, etc.): Make 3-10 SP/day. Wives of Freemen can make about the same working from home, or working in the homes of wealthier citizens.

• Middlemen (i.e. shop owners, skilled artisans, priests, etc.): Make 2-5 GP/day. Some very successful ones might make 5 times that. Wives of Middlemen don't do as much work as the wives of Freemen, as a general rule. Some might have a cottage industry or do some work for wealthier citizens, and might make 5-10 SP/day.

• Landmen: Are exceptionally wealthy, gaining vast incomes from rent on their properties, licenses to conduct business and harvest resources. These families bring in 50-100 GP/day from various activities.
Expenses
• Rent - Freeman Cottage or Rowhouse: 1-5 SP/day
• Rent - Middleman's Rowhouse (2 levels; ground shop and second floor residence): 1-5 GP/day

• Food - 1 day/person/simple fare (healthy, respectable portions, good beer): 1 SP (about 3cp/meal)
• Food - luxury meal for 5-10 people: 1 GP
• Taxes - Earldoms: All citizens pay a head-tax to their Earl. This is 1 GP/person/year

• Taxes - Town: All citizens living in Charity proper must pay 1 GP/person/year in order to be 'Free of the Town' (A 'Freeman' with all the rights and obligations that go along with it)

• Taxes - Church: All citizens are expected, but not required, to tithe one major church, and quarter-tithe both a secondary church and Charnel Priory. About 90% of citizens tithe, while about 50% do both quarter-tithes.

Example of a Freeman's Family Finances - The Hammersmith Family

John Hammersmith (35 years old) is a journeyman blacksmith and is Free of the Town.

He is married to Elizabeth Hammersmith (30), who works as a maid in the Ferguson Manor.

They have 4 children, aged 15, 13, 11, 6. Their two youngest attend the school during the day, the two oldest both work as common labourers in the town (they are not yet 'Freemen' or 'Free of the Town')

Income: 13 SP/day
John - 7 SP/day
Elizabeth - 4 SP/day (plus scraps of food from the Fergusons, old clothes and other discarded things) Oldest boys - 1 SP/day each

Expenses: 10s1c/day
Rent: 3 SP (they live in a respectable rowhouse, with 3 bedrooms, a water closet, and a small garden in the back)

Food: 4 SP (they eat well, with meals supplemented by the wife's benefits from her job at Ferguson Manor; without this extra bit of help, it could cost 6 SP/day to feed them)
Schooling: 4 CP (2CP/day for each of their children still in school)
Tithe: 1s7c (They tithe the Old Fort 1s1c, they quarter tithe the Priory for 3 cp and the church of Denier 3cp)

This leaves the family with nearly 3 SP/day for extras. John is likely to spend 1sp every few nights at the Old Fort. The kids and wife have good clothes. The house is brightly lit and has good (not fancy)

furnishings. They have been able to save 1 SP/day for several years, and will be able to retire when they are too old to work. John will have a pension from the Black Smith's Guild, so they will have a comfortable retirement. They are in 'good standing' with the Priory, so they will also have good access to medical treatment for the whole family.
DDC – 1481 – 8: Selections for the Journal of Nathan Gale
12 Marpenoth, 1481 - Journal of Nathan Gale
From GFD:
Another entry from the journal of the missing gunslinger…
-GFD
12 Marpenoth
On this cold evening we arrive in Dagger Falls at our new home, Loedagan Close. As we were going through the wrought-iron gates, we see the silhouettes of many people back-lit by the open double doors of the main building across the courtyard. We can see the shapely figure of Lady Blackmane in the door, waving at a man that is making his way from the steps, towards us. This tall, lean, quick figure is followed by a swarm of children of many ages, and I can hear them sending off this man with enthusiasm.
“Bring hell to their doors, Mr. Dretch!” “Take no prisoners, Avenger!”
Many other implorations are mixed in the chaos of this send off. Then everyone notices us coming through the gates. Alystair continues his quick pace towards us, but we see the children hesitate and squint into the darkness of the night to figure out who we are.

Dretch strides up and I can now see that he has already donned his grim leather mask. “I know that Reks wanted to be the first to congratulate you on your mission and to welcome you into our organization” the avenger says from behind the mask. “Congratulations on a job well done, White Cloaks.” I could detect the barest hint of a smile somewhere behind that mask.

He offers no other salutations and doesn’t wait for ours. He continues on his previous trajectory forcing us to split and get out of his way. As he passes by Shea, he slows his pace for a few steps, and tilts his head towards her a little. “Invictus is a good man. You can trust him” he says, and then he is off at full speed again, vanishing into the night like a spectre.

The children of the Close, orphans of the war with the Dark Garden, then close in around us, and they are just as enthusiastic about our return as they were about Dretch going hunting.
“The heroes of Dwimmerholme return!”
“Devils fly! The White Cloaks are on your heels!”
They seem to know only a bit about what transpired at Dwimmerholme, and congratulate us on many mixed up facts as they usher us into the warmth of the Close. At the doors, we are met by Lady

Blackmane, who welcomes us back, and tasks some of the older boys with helping us with our things, and some of the older girls to get a warm meal and baths ready.

Within an hour, we are all seated in clean things at a freshly-laid table. There are as many children buzzing about the Close as there were when we left, but there is a conspicuous absence of the adult staffers; there are no adults in the Close besides Blackmane. And Reks, I presume, but I hadn’t seen him yet. Blackmane explains that “financial exigencies have dictated a reduction in staff” and that “the children are happy to do the work, and need to learn the value of work at any rate.” I now notice that there are fewer candles burning in the halls and rooms than when we left, and that those that burn at our table are tallow, not wax. The fire in the hearth is ½ the size of the one that blazed when we left.

All of these subtle details amount to the suggestion that money is tight for the White Cloaks.

We were all well into our meal by the time some of us demanded to see Reks. It seems unthinkable that he would not come down to welcome us home, but then, the man is very strange. Blackmane explains that he has been really withdrawn lately, looking at the books and a large volume of correspondence.

He is locked away in his study for the night, and will receive no visitors. When pressed, she expertly diverts the inquiries to discussions of our recent mission, and finally, when put hard to it, she says “I would consider it a favour if you just let him stay in his room unmolested for the night”, which disarms even the most incensed of us. She’s good at her job, Blackmane.

After the late meal, one of the children, a girl about 8 years old named Karindra Oakdale, says to me that there has been a letter waiting for me all day. She led me to the aviary, where the White Cloak’s messenger pigeons arrive, live, and depart from. There, she points out a bird with a note still tied to its ankle. I have transcribed it below;
Nate;
I have discovered that the enemy you fought in Dwimmerholme is called the Sons of Bel. I strongly suspect that there is a coven of these villains operating in Charity Hills. I am awaiting direction from Loremaster Solemnius, but you should begin to plan for an expedition to that strange town. I will meet you in-person at Quick Axes on the 14th…
Br. Darred.
13 Marpenoth
This morning we are summoned to the dining hall for breakfast, where Reks is found putting plates on the table with the children. He is making a show of being a ‘working guy, just like you’ to the children, although everything he does requires correcting by an older girl that follows behind him.

As we file into the hall, he claps his hands together excitedly. In doing so, he absent-mindedly drops a plate that is caught by the same girl that was following him, before it hits the ground. “Brilliant!” he exclaims. “The heroes of Dwimmerholme have returned at last! What kept you? I was expecting you yesterday…anyway, I know that heroing is difficult business to set one’s time piece to, so I won’t press the matter. Ha ha!”

What follows can only be described as a ‘production’. Reks has gone through some trouble to orchestrate a ceremony welcoming us all as official members of the White Cloaks, no longer with the ‘Bravo Team’ designation. We are mantled with crisp white cloaks that Reks explains have been

purpose-made for each of us. The acceptance of each cloak comes with an oath that was doubtlessly penned by Reks himself; it is lengthy and more than just a little odd and inappropriate.

In the end he explains that the cloaks have been tailored to help “the next generation” of White Cloaks more than the old, standard issue cloaks. These have been enchanted to enhance the specific skill set of each member.

To his credit, or rather the credit of the tailor who made them, the new Cloaks are incredibly powerful and useful. Mine offers me protection, can shed light, and also makes my senses a little sharper, though I feel a bit jumpy while wearing it, like I’ve had too much tea.

After the pomp of the ceremony, the children are dismissed. At this point, some bags of money are brought to the table; there is a bag of 300 gold from Mayor Winters, and another bag of 500 which apparently was delivered by the Yellow Abbey this morning as a reward for our efforts in Dwimmerholme.

“800 gold, my colleagues!” Reks claps excitedly. Now, let’s just share this out, shall we?” The gold is divided into 10 neat stacks of 80 each.

“Each of you can take a stack” Reks announces as though he is giving us the keys to heaven itself. Each team member takes a share.

“Sgt. Paros” Reks addresses Hennigan. “You get one discretionary share to payout.” He slides one pile to Hennigan, and moves on.

“One share, for some reason that I was never involved in the discussion of, goes to the Church. Not that I’m complaining too much; they gave us 500 after all, ha-ha! A good arrangement if you ask me!”

“Finally, 3 shares go back to the company” and he swipes all of the remaining money on the table into a bag with one flourish. “Meat on the table tonight, eh boys?!” He smiles, and then cranes his neck backwards for an awkwardly long period of time. Still with his head back; “now, 3 shares to the company seems dear to some of you, I suspect. But those are our terms. This company needs operating capital for…well; just think of all of it! This building, the fine candles we burn, the warmth of the fire.

The very cloaks about your shoulders! How much do you think those are worth? A fair exchange, I think you’ll agree!

“Now, if you’ll excuse me, I have to see some men that will finally be happy to see me!” and with a jingle of the bag, and a wink, he is out the door. This time, I do not let him off the hook. Before Reks is halfway to the front doors, I grab him by the shoulder to stop him.
“Charity Hills Farm” is the only thing I say.
“Dear no…” Reks says, his face going pale. He squirms from my grip, puts the bag down and turns to face me. “Wherever did you hear that terrible name?” By this time, the rest of the team are at the archway of the dining hall, watching and listening.

“There’s more Sons of Bel there, Administrator. We need to go there soon. Like yesterday. Start putting it together.”

“You’ve mistaken me for someone other than your superior, I fear, Mr. Gale” and with this, Reks composes himself, crossing his arms in front of his chest. “I am calling the shots here, you see, and I’ll tell you where and when your next assignment is.”

“Is that so? You’re sure that Dretch isn’t calling the shots? It seems to me that he left here in a hurry last night, and you wouldn’t show your face afterwards. We all know that he was in Charity. Could it be that he told you not to send us there? Could it be that you follow Dretch’s orders?” And I smile only slightly.

“I call the shots here” Reks almost whimpers to himself. After a pause, he declares “The White Cloaks are heading to Foothills Farm later this week to follow a lead there. You have a few days to rest. Now, I am off!” Out the door he goes. Reks is at large for the rest of the day, and indeed doesn’t show up again until long after dinner. He is again aloof the rest of the night. What is he hiding?
14 Marpenoth
I meet with Brother Darred in a private room at Quick Axes tavern in town in the afternoon, as he arranged. Darred is sitting with a man who would become a fast-friend by the end of the day, Artorias. The only person in the room is a mousy serving girl named Hannah that comes and goes with food and drink as ordered.

Darred slides an ornate wooden box across the table and a leather folio full of papers.

I open the box and marvel at the pistol found inside. It is more like a work of art than a weapon; the handle is a piece of reddish exotic hardwood, inlaid with brass grips and other hardware. The barrel is damasked steel that presents as a wavy pattern of materials that look like silver and brass, though they feel harder and colder. There are words and symbols carved into the barrel and other metal hardware- bits; the only one that I immediately recognized is a symbol of Gond.

"This is a most useful tool, Mr. Gale" Darred begins. "Rafter herself crafted this for a client that...didn't survive…no fault of the weapon's I am sure. It is a marvel of both craftsmanship and dwimmercraft; it is magical, though she wouldn't tell me what it does. She said you'd figure it out as you used
it. Sometimes I think she's daft.

"Anyway, there are a couple of reasons you are being assigned this weapon. For starters, we need to make sure you are well looked after; you are about to embark on your most dangerous task yet, and while we will pray for your safety, we'll hedge our bets just a bit, hey? Also, you are headed to Charity Hills, where people love firearms. This piece is fine, even for them, and I hope it will help you transition into that town.

"There is enough ammunition for 200 rounds of fire, and more will be readily available in Charity, I'm sure. There is more..."

He reaches into the bottom of the box, shuffling around ammunition components, and pulls out a small piece of cloth that makes the hair on the back of my neck stand up.

Founders Linen. All full members of my order wear a 4" x 4" patch of linen that was taken from a

garment worn by The Founder. This piece is the requisite size, and the transparent nature of the fine linen is a dead giveaway. This little patch is frayed at the edges and has a number of stains that make the transparency somewhat muddied.

"Yes, brother” Darred addresses me. “Today you are a full member. I guess you were expecting some sort of ceremony full of pledges, candles, incense, and the like, but it just doesn't work like that. What happens is this" he says, as he leans across the table, and stretching both hands out towards me, opens my cloak, and pins the linen inside. "You are now a full member of the Order of the Tome, brother. This doesn't mean that they are going to reveal the secrets of the universe to you. I don't know much more of that sort of thing than you. But, know that you are part of an Order that is older than either of us ever expected. More will be revealed as you prove yourself; our goals, methods, and so on. For now, you take orders. Can you live with that? Most of the orders are reasonable, and many are fun.

"I personally spoke for you with Loremaster Solemnius; your accomplishments in Dwimmerholme, painted in the right light, were enough to earn your Linen.

"But, you only scratched the surface. There is something much more insidious at work in Daggerdale, and there is an evil book at the core of it that we have been seeking for decades. The Diabolus Itineris. I know your ancient Netherese is current, hahaha! There are very particular translators, however, that say that means 'A Devil's Diary', while others say it means 'The Devil's Journal', and still others that argue for 'Devilish Agenda', but it all amounts to the same for guys like us; evil book, must get it.

"Here's how we know..." and he opens the leather folio, and sorts through the papers. He picks one out and gives it a rap with the back of his hand, and hands it over to me. "This is from our associate, Basil Muloch. Go ahead and read it..."
GFD Note: c.f. DDC – 1481 - 9
After I read the letter, he hands over another batch of sheets; 7 pages written in Ancient Netherese which I recognize from the Belial Prayer Book. This is the ritual known as 'Bel's Bargain', and I am horrified to think of it being used against the people of Charity.

"I can assure you that Earl Muloch translated this expertly. His manner of writing tells me that he is worried to send any message that says he knows too much. As such, I have returned no letters to him. Instead, I am sending you. And not just to bring a letter to an old man.

"You will notice that your prayer book is full of the infernal text, but it has been written for a Cormyrean to read and translate. This text, this copy of a copy that was sent to us by our ally and associate, this is written in Ancient Netherese, and the details which he has asked me to uncover reveal that it was taken from an original manuscript. We think that it might have been copied from the Diabolus Itineris itself."

"Your orders are to go and find that book, Mr. Gale. If that book is in Charity, it is most assuredly the centre piece of this Sons of Bel business plaguing the dale. You will need to assemble a discreet team; convince the White Cloaks to go if you can. Convince that crazy administrator to send you and his men. Or find a few trustworthy allies that can assist you and make your way to Charity."

At this point, Darred introduces Artorias. “This man is from an associate order with great expertise in matters such as this.”

GFD Notes: Artorias Brave is a ranking member of The Watchtower, well known by the Keep for their efforts in battling devils across Faerun.

“I have heard that the White Cloaks are in some financial trouble. Normally, they would send off the best-appointed adventurers in the dale. I can see that Reks spared no expense with the cloaks, but still, those can’t be expected to carry the day. The Order is willing to provide aid up front for this mission.” With this, he slides a heavy bag across the table to me. "This is for your expenses" he explains. The bag opens, and a few coins spill out (there is 500 gold in the bag!)

"I wish I had more to tell you. Try to gain a discrete audience with Earl Muloch. He won't be hard to find, but it will be hard to meet with him without raising suspicions.
