He is a good man that you can trust; he is an associate of the Order, and a dedicated follower of the Scribe. He will help you, but he has much to lose, and will play his hand cautiously in all matters."

He gets up to leave. "Pour over all the information in that folio. We'll talk again before you set out. I'm in Town for 2 more days, but I have to head over to the Yellow Abbey just now."



Contents of the folio;

1. A Report on the Essential Elements of Charity, by Sr. S. Estelmer
2. A Note from Basil Muloch to Brother Darred
3. A copy of 'Bel's Bargain' in Ancient Netherese
4. A copy of the Yellow Abbey Booke of Measures and Surveyes, Charity Contents of the box;
1 Gond Pistol with Rafter's Maker's Mark 200 rounds of ammunition
Cleaning kit for the gun. Leather holster

Marveling at the boons delivered by the Order, I almost forgot that Artorias was sitting opposite me. He doesn’t leave with Darred, so I invite him back to the Close, and introduce him to the rest of the team. He is an experienced devil-hunter and will be a great help in this struggle.

Just before dinner, I meet with Shea, who seems to be out of sorts. She is wearing a new ring which she can’t take her eyes from. I pull her aside and share my news, showing her my Founder’s Linen, which she does her best to appreciate. Then she explains to me that she was caught in the street after Matins by Magistrate Invictus, who came back to the Close with her. Alone in our drawing room, he told her the following (as close as I can recall):

“My darling avenger, you have certainly lived up to your title. I have heard of your heroism in Dwimmerholme. It was I that authorized the funds for your organization as a reward. But I have brought a gift that is for you, my dove. For both of us. For you, this ring is safety, and for me, peace of mind.”

It is a ring of brilliantly polished gold, plain except for a slightly broadened face upon which a symbol of Amaunator is etched. It is warm to touch and gives a slight tingle when worn. A feeling of safety and euphoria washed over Shea for a moment, making her feel almost like she’s had too much to drink. The feeling then subsides, but not completely; the feeling of safety in the pit of her stomach lingers.

“This will guard you from our enemies, avenger. Of course, you still need to do your part; you must pray and be vigilant and uphold our laws and values. And duck when you see a sword coming at your throat. But in your most dire need, it will protect you. It will also help me find you if you get into more trouble than you can handle. Finally, I had our brothers charge it as a very potent prayer conduit. We have charged this ring with the great deeds of many that have come before you; the honour they won for our Lord have all been enshrined in this ring for one purpose; once, and only once, you can use this ring to make a plea to Amaunator himself. He will hear you and he will answer. When you are in such a situation, take the ring off, clutch it in both hands and pray until you are answered. Do not take it off before. Do you understand, Sister Shea?”

Shea is spellbound by the thing, but I can tell she is also somewhat put off by it. I suspect that Invictus will use it to spy on us, as though he needs more spies. But if it does what it says, the balance of the thing is clearly in her favour.
15 Marpenoth
Marpenoth is a cold month here. The trees seem to know it better than most, although this year they seem less than inclined to admit the coming of Winter, stubbornly clinging to yellowed leaves still hanging off their branches. Most of the oaks on the property now stand stark and naked against the stern black walls of the Close, crowding around my new home like the grasping hands of the dead and dying. The entire estate has felt stripped bare, skeletal almost, since the departure of most of the staff. If not for the pitter-patter of young feet we hear so often in distant halls, the Close could pass as a funeral home with little effort. Last night, after I had finished the day’s entries, we were summoned to the dining hall to meet with Reks, around eleven.

The second-floor dining hall we gathered in is quickly growing cold, in both temperature and atmosphere. The clock hanging above the mantle reads quarter past eleven, but we’ve all been waiting here since well before the hour struck. Administrator Reks is certainly taking his time in addressing the meeting he himself scheduled, although he has been somewhat on-and-off again these last few days. Hastings Blackmane, statuesque as marble and ever in silent attendance, strides carefully to the eastern door of the room. She leans through it, whispering to one of the many young orphans waiting just outside of view. She smiles, motions to pat the child upon his head, and turns to face us with a faint nod of her own.

“It would seem that Alen has lost track of the time. He will be here shortly."

Footsteps from the corridor outside the dining hall gradually reach our ears, and after five minutes of quiet waiting, Administrator Reks enters the room with what can only be described as a listless stride. He looks up from the sheaf of documents in his hands, eyes the lot of us suspiciously from behind a pair of delicate spectacles, and furrows his expression into one of annoyed confusion.

"You're all here quite early." He notes in a low voice, eyes dragging across our collected selves before stopping at the clock on the wall behind him.

Musing, he taps his chin. "No... that's not right. I appear to be late."

With a sigh he strides towards the mantle, fetches a fire poker from the basin flanking his leg, and prods the minute hand back up to the twelve, despite the resentful grinding and clicking from within the timepiece's innards.

With a tiny smile on his face, he places the poker upon the mantle, turns to face us and gestures slightly with his free hand.

"And now everyone's right on time, ha ha. Perfect. I suppose we should get down to business, then, hmmm?" Alen says, removing the glasses from his sharp nose and tucking them into the pocket of his vest, pausing for but a moment to toss the sheaf of important-looking papers he held into the dying fire of the hearth.

"Bills," He explains with a grin. He approaches the table, draws his chair slightly aside so as to allow him room to stand, and places a single delicate hand upon the polished oak surface. He stares at himself for a moment, face reflected back in orange and yellow, before looking up once more and drawing a deep breath.

"There is work to be done, White Cloaks. Dwimmerholme, I fear, was merely the beginning of something greater. Just the tip, so to speak."

"Demons." A flick of his wrist on either side to punctuate each word as he continued on, the Administrator's voice betraying no emotion on his part. "Devils." A shrug. "Cultists."

"Nine Hells, I cannot stand before you an honest man and your honest superior, and lie to you by saying I fully understand this debacle that we, brave citizens of this fair Dale, have found ourselves so unwillingly embroiled in."

Alen throws his hands into the air, shaking his head with blatant false melancholy. "I am no man of the cloth, no delver of damned arcana, no seeker of secrets. I push the pencils, cross the T's, sign upon the dotted lines and all that boring business that keeps the real heroes doing what it is they do so well without being bogged down in the bureaucracy of it all.”

Hand upon his chest, Alen sighs. "I am but a humble elf, doing what best he can."

And he smiles, turning to pass a warm glance at Blackmane, still standing against the far eastern door. "And so it falls to me to guide spirited individuals such as yourselves, those who are truly fit to settle these dangerous matters by means of thoughtless swordplay and blind faith and all the other crude yet heavenly virtues - "Praise the sun" he mutters off-hand “... dearly within the bosom of our beloved Dale. Under the leadership of Lady Lumina, Amaunator bless her dearly, we were content with charging about with nothing but piety to guide our smiting fists. Were those days these days, however, this devilry plaguing our fair land would have gone unseen until far too late."

"The time for blind faith is long past, I am afraid. Raw zeal is not enough to ferry us from one day to the next - we must temper our might with wisdom, if we are expected to survive. These cultists, these Sons of Bel..." Alen rolls the word around in his mouth for a moment, judging the weight of it as it rests on his tongue, "these Sons of Bel do not stand in the light. They have no obligation to. It is a knife's edge that we will be expected to walk, I am afraid, while dealing with them. Hard choices have already been made, and more are sure to follow as we wade into this abyss."

Slowly, the Administrator claps his hands together and paces around the side of the table, eyes focused on our backs. He laughs gently.

"Aha, but what am I saying? We're not heroes, not at all. We are a business... and like all businesses, we run on silver and gold, not well-wishes and kitten-whispers, delightful as they are. Lions, scratch, coin, what have you. Budgets necessitate tough decisions. To operate at top capacity, I have to be aware of things. Ev-er-y-thing. If it has happened in Daggerdale, the White Cloaks will know. This is my mandate."

Reks pauses after a full rotation around the table, finger drumming against his slender chin. "Though eyes and ears are expensive in the Dale, and it cost me nearly an arm and a leg just to get my foot in the door. These people keep their noses to the ground for me, and give me a taste of what's what for a small touch of coin. I have heard... a great many things." His eyes fall upon us, lingering overlong on me before passing over the newcomers at the table, Artorias and Abigail.

Quick as a jackrabbit, the Administrator darts behind me, resting his arms on Shae’s shoulders and mine, leaning in close between the two of us, a broad smile spreading across his lips. "Unfortunately, the White Cloaks are not above petty politics. A lot of hungry little lads think they can stick their fat little fingers in my pie without my knowing it."

An edge of ice, cold as the Marpenoth wind, clings to Alen's tone. "The White Cloaks will not be danced about. If someone wishes to have a say in how things are run, they will have to toss around the moneybags like everyone else, and they will do it plain and clear where the sun doth shine." He pats Shae and I softly on the shoulders before leaning upright once more, hands resting together at his belt line.

He clearly knows about my meeting with Darred, and Shea’s meeting with Invictus. He’s said that he has many eyes…

Briefly, the Administrator seems frozen in place, eyes set against the far wall of the dining hall, eyelids

hung low over a tight, mirthless smile. Then he claps his hands together and chirps a tiny ha-ha, pacing around the table before arriving at his proper place once more.

"Of course, due to all of this, I have had a change of heart these last few days. The budget is tight, and some leads are less than lucrative when compared to others. I've heard long talk from many different faces that bad business is a brewin' in both Foothills and Charity. Unfortunately, neither you nor I are competent or bothered enough to deal with both simultaneously. You lot," Alen says, idly drumming his fingers against the tabletop, "will be attending to the later. Post-haste."

The Administrator quickly affects a swift change of tone, his voice piping in concerned falsetto, "But Administrator, what of Foothills! If we are investigating Charity Hills, surely whatever villainy brewing over there will run rampant without the brave White Cloaks to swoop in and save the day!"

In a dull bass, he replies while leaning in the opposite direction, hands sweeping in a placating fashion. "Worry not, worry not, for Alystair Dretch himself is currently there doing his fair share of the work!" Alen's smile positively drips sarcasm as he leans forward onto the table, hands cupped against his cheek. "Of course, he might be cross with me. He requested you lot hop along behind him like wee ducklings chasing their mother, but I didn't form my Bravo team to serve as a simple clean-up crew for a masked lunatic who can't even be bothered to wash the blood stains out of his knickers. You lot are here to take point, like the well-behaved expendables, pardon, non-expendables you are."

"And so, Charity Hills it is." Alen nods, arching his back as he casts a weary yawn against the ceiling. "Hennigan Paros will be continuing his role as acting Sergeant, for a job very well done. It warms me deeply to know that there is at least one member of the White Cloaks willing to go... the extra mile, both on and off the battlefield. His reports have been both informative and invaluable to me." His tone becomes less animated as regards me.

"You," he points with a dagger-like stab of his finger, "will be taking care of the Quartermastering once again as well. Be sure to get an even share out of Charity Hills. Despite the name, they are certainly sitting upon a fat share of wealth. The White Cloaks could make do with some of that, so do what you do best. I'm counting on you. All of you."

Alen's attention then swoops to the newcomers at the table, a heavy-set man and the woman seated next to him. His brow dips for a moment, a thin frown biting his chin. "Something is off over... you two aren't Bastian. There's not even the slightest resemblance. Where is that lout?" He twists his head, eyeing each chair lining the table. "I said eleven sharpish."

Blackmane meanders softly towards you, stopping to whisper softly in Alen's ear. A bemused expression embraces his face for but a moment, before he turns to her and nods. "Ah, of course. I remember now. What a shame. However," He says, addressing the two at the far end of the table, "The paperwork has already been dealt with, and you two will be considered associate White Cloaks for the duration of this mission. Bear in mind that your actions will reflect upon us as a whole, so please do nothing to embarrass myself or the faith our organisation has placed in you."

The elf retrieves a delicate pair of leather gloves from behind his back and gradually slips them over his hands as he speaks. "You all will be expected to act with dignity and decorum. Any fool could tell you that by now the Sons of Bel are well aware of our goals and movements, so I beg you, please endeavor to remain as low-key as you can possibly manage. The White Cloaks are not the battering ram they once were. The time for crass zealotry is over. We must fight fire with fire. Strike without warning, and when you do aim for the vitals. Leave those damned devil worshippers guessing at your every move. But most importantly, and again, I have to stress this..."

"Keep." And he drags one glove down to his wrist. "Your heads down." And he straightens the other. With a sharp snap of his fingers, the Administrator produces a sealed letter seemingly from nowhere, flicking it deftly towards Paros.
GFD Note: c.f. DDC – 1481 - 10

"The letter will inform you of everything you need to know to prepare. Just like last time, I have sent word ahead to Charity Hills. You will leave by dawn the day after tomorrow and make your way by the most subtle means possible. Wagons and horses are ready and waiting, just as before. I will leave the rest to you. The details of the Sergeant's letter will lead you to one of my contacts. She will assist you in whatever... whatever way she can," Alen assures us with a strange smirk upon his face.

After that, the Administrator merely nods his head, seemingly content with the volume of information he has bestowed upon us. "And now I must bid you farewell for the evening. You have your duties to tend to before morning, and I have much work that still needs doing. No rest for the wicked and all that nonsense, eh?"

And with a swift double-clap of his gloved hands, the air around Alen explodes into a cloud of white smoke that lasts but a few seconds, fading fast to reveal an empty space where the Administrator of the White Cloaks once stood.

Across the room, you notice Blackmane wrinkle her nose as she turns to stare into doorway beside her. A gloved hand reaches out and places a folded slip of paper between her fingers before slipping back out of sight. Rapid footsteps then echo down the hall, followed by what seems to be at least half a dozen young children in pursuit, whispering excitedly. Hastings looks aside and shakes her head before warming us all with a polite smile.

"I would wager that concludes the meeting."
I am not sure what changed Reks’ mind, but I’m certain it wasn’t my demand from the other morning, as I found this note in my room (left there by Blackmane, I think; this appears to be the note Reks left with her after he ‘vanished’).

The next time your friends at the book club decide to poke their noses in White Cloak business, do inform them that my office at the Close is always open to visitors.

Fondest Regards, Administrator Reks.
At any rate, we spent the rest of the day getting ready to head out to Charity, and I’m glad of it. There is

work to do there. A vile tome to be recovered, and a cult to put down. I have direction, good allies, a fine pistol and my Cloth. Who can stand against us?




DDC – 1481 - 9: Correspondence from Basil Muloch of Charity, to Brother Darred of the Candlekeep Emissaries
11 Marpenoth, 1481
Notes from GFD:
This is the start of the White Cloaks involvement with the Sons of Bel in Charity. Brother Darred is (as I write this) stationed at Castle Radiance in the Candlekeep Emissaries tower, and was a receiver of good intelligence from odd corners of Daggerdale and further abroad. I spent some time with the man up at the Castle, and he is as reliable as he is hospitable (my stay at the Castle was comfortable). I never met Muloch, who’s fate you will soon learn of.

It is vitally important to note that this is one of the unfinished chapters of the Daggerdale Chronicle, and I hope others will pick up sword and pen and close this chapter in good order.
-GFD
Br. Darred;
I send this correspondence in haste and beg your forgiveness for abandoning the usual formalities of our all-too-infrequent epistles.

I have uncovered, I think, and through no great effort of my own, but rather through what might be interpreted as lucky happenstance in one instance, and perhaps divine intervention in another, a fiendish plot in our otherwise sleepy and, heretofore thankfully uneventful little towne.

I enclose for your purposes, and would deign to impose upon you for your expertise in the matter and roundly-acknowledged puissance in translation, a copy of what I suspect is a copy of a most malign and certainly devilish bit of script that I don’t doubt is in some way related to that nasty business up in Dwimmerholme, that is so vile that even within our news-resilient walls, such terrible stories have violated the talk, and no doubt the dreams, of our erstwhile uninvolved citizenry.

The means by which I came upon, or rather, had thrust upon me in a most assuredly unexpected and certainly unwelcomed and completely unsolicited manner, such a terrible and, I would dare say, Mephistophelian bit of text, I shall spare you, and thereby spare the delicate and, I would hazard to

wager, innocent, conduit through which this missive found me. Suffice it to say, that intentions in the hearts and minds of all parties that I have first-hand knowledge of in this diabolical affair, are pure and well-meaning, unless I am greatly fooled in this manner. I think I am not and will rest upon my reputation with you and your organization, and leave it, succinctly, at that, kind friend.

So, you have now my copy, crude though it most certainly is, because I have never mastered the nuances of the hated language in which this even-more-hated script is written, and I beg that you will complete, and where necessary, and certainly this will be in myriad places that I haven’t your wits to identify, correct me, for our mutual benefit. I’m afraid, sir, that I have the general meaning of the thing, and this, combined with some very unsavoury recent events in what I have already described as an otherwise sleepy and, heretofore uneventful little towne, and this combined with what black rumours trickle from Dwimmerholme, and with the cosmos being what they have been this last moon, suggests to me that there is a plot to equal that of the unfortunate Dwimmerholme in my very sleepy, uneventful little towne.

Kindly sir, put any doubts I have to rest, and do not spare my sensitivities. I would have the truth of the matter, and sharpish if you can spare the time and consideration for your most indebted correspondent, whose fair weather rescriptions are not to be excused, but certainly admonished after these bitter affairs are put in order.
Indebted, B.Muloch.
GFD Notes: I found out that the document Mr. Muloch referred to herein was the ritual Bel’s Bargain, and the nuance he detected was this; that it was in the Infernal language but written by a Cormyrean. I have never seen the original; Br. Darred had already sent it to Candlekeep for safe keeping a year before I arrived…
-GFD




DDC – 1481 – 10: Letter from Administrator Reks to White Cloak Sgt. Hennigan Paros
Marpenoth 14
GFD Notes:
This is a direct copy of the letter, which was provided to my by Reks.
-GFD


To the esteemed Hennigan Paros,

Congratulations once again on being elected acting Sergeant for this mission! You're a man of action, and you're willing to make the hard decisions that no one else seems to be capable of - worry not over broken eggs and all that noise. In a conflict as muddied and twisted as this, lines will, regrettably, be crossed time and time again by those of us who stand firm against the machinations of the unjust. Just be sure to remember what they say about he who fights monsters, Mr. Paros.

But on to more mundane matters! Denelius Ormanth's caravan will be leaving Dagger Falls at first light on the 16th, less than 2 days from now. Guess where he's heading? Charity Hills, of course! I'd like you to head out with Mr. Ormanth. He'll be stopping in Liberty Hills, and arrive in Charity by the 17th, or so I've heard.

Of course, that would be the quiet way. Feel free to ride out for Charity Hills at first morning's light. I honestly don't care how you get there, as long as you get there without informing anyone untoward about it, understand?

When you arrive at your destination, find Medea Rowan. She's a Priestess of Sharess (oh la la), and loves learning new things, so get in there and try to squeeze some information out of her. As politely as possible, of course, she is a lady after all. She tends to favour information over coin, so make sure you don't tell her anything that may compromise your presence in Charity Hills... we can't trust anyone these days, it would seem.

Lastly, keep an eye on Gale. He'll no doubt want to run off and attend to his own business. I say let him. He knows more than he's leading on about all this nonsense, but a lead is a lead, so humour him a bit. Try not to butt heads, though. You are his immediate superior, after all. Just keep a sharp eye on his sneaking.
I expect you to hold them in line. Don't disappoint me now!


Forever Yours, Administrator Reks

DDC – 1481 – 11: Abandon Hope, All Ye Who Enter Here
The following are some key entries found in the large tome, Abandon Hope, All Ye Who Enter Here, discovered between Marpenoth 20 and 22, 1481 DR. Penned by Robert
Tuugaarth, 1097 DR Translated into the Chondathan by Phineas Hoetmer, 1454 DR


GFD Notes:
The following are some key entries found in the large tome, Abandon Hope, All Ye Who Enter Here, discovered between Marpenoth 20 and 22, 1481 DR, in the library of Basil Muloch.

This ancient book, which is known to us (though its author is not), has many editions, and has always been a double-edged blade. It has served for some as a weapon to arm oneself against dark forces, and for others, a manual of strategy. Still other times, as I fear is the case with Mr. Muloch, the thing has been a meaner tool for a cruder purpose…

It is important to note that the Sons of Bel were never fully exterminated, and that the White Cloaks that went to Charity to deal with the head of the coven didn’t succeed (see later in this Chronicle).
-GFD


Forward to the Chondathan Edition
I found this book in a less-than-reputable shop on Candle Row in Waterdeep when I was a younger, more adventurous man. I had at best a tenuous grasp on Damaran at the time, but even then I could see that this was an important work. I would like to say that I made a pointedly academic, exacting translation, but that is not really the case. I was pressed for time, when I finally got around to translating this tome, and this was a secret labour; the Yellow Abbey had just been completed, and what I knew was going to be an age of stifled ideas had begun.

At any rate, this is what I put together. I pray that we never need to study the contents of this tome, but the world is a dangerous place, and when the veil is thinnest, we must prepare our minds as well as our bodies.
-Phineas Hoetmer, Clerk of the Yellow Abbey, Marpenoth 29, 1454 DR
Forward to the Second Edition
The purview of this tome is exclusively the denizens of Avernus, the first, outer-most layer of Hell, and their known schemes in our Realms, especially those that have been played out in Narfell, Damara, Thay and Rashemen. I have had the misfortune of spending a lifetime chasing the devils of the First, and more usually, their henchmen, and I have what some consider an encyclopaedic knowledge of these cursed villains. I am told by my commander that I am now too old to fight with the Sword, and so I now fight with the Pen.

The title of this book has been kept deliberately foreboding. This is not a tome for the weak-of-heart, or the soft-of-mind. Of course, I make no endorsement of any of the practices found within these pages, but the misguided, if so armed with my knowledge, could easily become a threat. The title is also taken from the infernal script above the Gates of Malsperanze. I was criticized after the first edition was released, by some who felt that the title was an indication that this book, like the Gates of Malsperanze themselves, is a gateway to deeper and greater evils. I would argue that ignorance is the true gateway to evil, and I have kept the title for the second edition.
-Robert Tuugaarth, Mirtul, 1097
Primer for Avernus, the First Hell – Account of Tuugaarth
The first layer of the Nine Hells is Avernus. It is the surface of Baator’s ruddy orb. It is a desert of stone, pumice, and ash broken by the occasional range of low, jagged mountains or a flowing river of lava. The fortresses of devils dot its landscape surrounded by the debris of countless battles. During the fiercest outbreaks of the Blood War, hordes of demons often invaded Avernus. Consequently, it is defended by legions of infernal warriors and daunting strongholds.

Unlike the deeper hells, Avernus has a sky. In the sky, sullen, roiling clouds of red and black constantly flicker and burn with gouts of orange flame. Streaking fireballs pelt the barren landscape below at odd intervals. The air is hot, dry, and acrid, fouled by volcanic fumaroles.

The mighty pit fiend ruler of Avernus is Bel, chosen by Asmodeus for his loyalty and his military genius. Bel is a cool, calculating creature that carefully avoids the intrigues of the other lords. A circle of pit fiends known as the Dark Eight serve as Bel’s vassals and councillors. Bel governs only at their pleasure, and he must constantly consider whether his actions will meet with the approval of the Dark Eight.

Avernus is the largest and most desolate of the hells, so many outcast devils or those few damned who escape their torments hide in its barren mountains.

The Bronze Citadel: The Bronze Citadel is the seat of Bel’s power. It is a mighty fortress of fourteen concentric rings, each studded with forbidding towers and infernal war machines. Thousands of spined devils, bearded devils, and legion devils are housed in its vast barracks.

Gates of Malsperanze: Many caves in Avernus lead down to other hells below, but the most notorious is a great archway guarded by towering gates of iron. Molten runes above the gates read, “Abandon hope, all ye who enter here.” The gates stand open, and beyond them a road descends steeply to the iron city of Dis, second of the Nine Hells.

Lake of Despond: This large, bitter lake marks the birthplace of the River Styx. Souls newly arrived in the Nine Hells awake on its rocky shores where they are quickly snatched up by devils assigned the task of collecting the damned.
Currency Of Souls – Account of Tuugaarth
The currency of Hell is that of souls. This is well known. What is not as well known is that this currency actually takes physical form in our world; that of Soul Keys. These evil, reddish stone tokens contain the soul of a victim from our world, and they can literally be traded like gold, among others who deal in such currency. Many of those able to acquire this currency use it to purchase favours from their

masters. The simplest and most common exchange is for devilish servants. A soul can be exchanged for

the service of the least of devils (see ‘Taxonomies’, below) for the duration of 111 days, which is 1/6th of a Baator year. Some souls carry greater value, however, and might demand something more.

I have known the most diabolical of Bel’s sycophants to exchange dozens of these souls for the aid of Hamatulas and even greater servants. It should be noted that the term ‘servant’ does not always accurately describe the bargain that is struck for this currency. One usual arrangement is for the exchange of souls, in conjunction with the requisite summoning rituals, for the presence of one’s patron. In all cases I know of, this has resulted in the eventual demise of the foolhardy who think they can command their masters.

What is most important to note, and something that I regrettably found out too late in my career, is that these souls can be returned to their derelict bodies. I have personally witnessed this ritual, though I am unable to perform it. The details of this ritual can be found in the Codex of Prayer.
The Currency of Souls – Account of Zullmared the Mad
I discovered a sheaf of papers that Zullmared the Mad had tucked away in the corner of his cave. The originals were in his barely-legible hand. I have reproduced them as well as possible below. I fear that he has, once again, left me with more questions than answers. There is still some small chance that we will meet again, though certainly this will not be to my benefit.

Zullmared, exiled from his homeland for centuries, still insisted on using his native calendar; the date below is Mulhorandi Reckoning.
17 Ra 3017
I am finally ready to record my accounts…accounts haha! Time is on my side, but she says I am growing…growing madder. So I take up quill. After one more drink…
The Abacus of Avernus – Account of Zullmared the Mad
To begin, we must understand the value of a soul; let us assign a value of ‘1’ to most souls, for that is what most are worth, and none are worth fewer.

However, let us then understand that some souls carry greater value, and this value is derived from the actual ‘value’ of the person whose soul is being evaluated, and also by the means of realizing that value. Much like stones from the earth; some are more treasured for their beauty, some for their rarity, and those most of all that are both rare and beautiful.

Let us also consider race. Above all else, the souls of Humans are the most abundant currency for the bankers of Avernus. Do we not use silver, but value more the sapphires of the Blistering Wastes? Silver is more abundant, but still more precious. What is the value of the soul of the High Fey? I couldn’t say.

Next, let us consider the lifespan of this currency. Like precious metal, it does not vanish, and rarely changes its substance, though some metals are mutable to Zullmared, aha aha! But no; once stamped, the coin of the soul cannot be un-stamped. Except through the works of those in this Realm. In Avernus, that currency is fixed, and this is the basis of the entire oeconomy of the bankers therein.

Let us consider next the marketplace for the soul. Marketplaces, rather, as there are many, but two that most men of Faerun are concerned with, though Zullmared has accounts in four, does he not?! Who but

Zullmared has exchanged the Pineal Gland of a Captain of the Far Realm, for that which I exchanged it for?! But the marketplaces are mostly two; here and there.
Here, a soul can be traded for some of the following;
Of Pawns, such as the Lemure, 1 for 666 days, or 6 for 111 days, or any other balanced exchange, and this always with the owner of the host.

Of Assistants, such as the Imp, 1 for 333 days, and this is the only contract between such creatures and the trader.

Of Soldiers, such as the Barbazu, 1 for 66 days, or any other balanced exchange, sometimes with the creature, sometimes with his captain if he has one.

Of Sergeants, such as the Eryines or the Osyluth, 1 for 33 days, and this is the only contract between such creatures and the trader.

Of Lieutenants, such as the Hamatula or the Gelugon, 3 souls are needed for 33 days. Of Captains, such as the Cornugon, 1 soul is needed for 1 day.

Of Generals, such as the Pit Fiend, 3 souls are needed for 1 day. Of greater creatures, I know not the accounting.

Of power, those creatures above will lend their strength at the same rate of exchange to mortals. Zullmared would never make such an exchange, however; why borrow strength and risk your own skin, when you can borrow the skin too? Such is the false-oeconomy of the Sorcerer. Surely these devils laugh at the desire of moral men for power, rather than the results of power.

What I do know is that the accountants of Hell are the finest and most diligent in any Realm I have known. Their abaci are true, and legions march, or not, based on the beads found thereupon.

The marketplace there…I shall give an accounting of at a later date with any luck oho!
The Preponderance of Threes – Account of Tuugaarth
This chapter is forged of my own experiences.
I was challenged by a certain Azbiel (found later as Azbael, and again as Azbial, and yet again as Ahzbeal, but these are likely the same), hard by Val’Murthag when it was called Val’Korthir, and was not as it is today.

Azbiel, a quaternary of Bel himself, waiting in the wings while his minions did the necessary work to bring him to our world, could not but direct his logisticians to construe all arrangements by threes. He had 3 lieutenants, each with 3 sergeants, each with 33 soldiers.

Later the same decade, I struggled against the Melphanigan, hard by Bildoobaris. The Melphanigan did not trace lineage directly to Bel, but was still compelled to arrange his organization into threes. Three cells, with three spies each, with three agents/traitors each.

Again, at the close of that century, attempting to root out the wickedness that nearly consumed the Duchy of Soravia, I found the Belial Cult to have 3 distinct Belial, each with 3 Magi. Only the number of Supplicants varied thereafter, but often was found to be 11 or 33.

I surmise that the Administration of Avernus is under compulsion to arrange things by threes, and that they venerate this number for some reason that I have never discovered. Certainly, their main iconography, the pentagram, lacks this number. There is some deeper meaning here, some weakness which we may ultimately be able to exploit. Until I or those that follow after me figure out the meaning of this number, we will use it to inventory our foes, and to account for that which we don’t see.
Bel’s Bargain – Account of Tuugaarth
This is one of the most terrible rituals I have discovered. This is the primary means through which Soul Keys are created. I should add that I have known other devil-binders who employed (or were employed by) denizens of Stygia and Minauros to have possession of this currency of souls, which leads me to believe that just as we have dozens of minters in our world creating coins, so too are there many ways to mint this terrible currency.

Bel’s Bargain is as eloquent as it is horrible. The victim is pressured into making a contract for his

soul. It is interesting to note that this ritual is rarely successful where one victim is involved; a lone man with even the slightest of convictions will endure the tortures and torments put upon him, to save his mortal soul. However, when faced with the torment of his loved ones, he often trades his soul for their safety. It is common for a torturer to flay a family in front of the man in order to have him put up his soul, and when the bargain is struck, the torturers might just kill the family, or do something equally as terrible, so long as their actions are not interdicted by the terms of the bargain. While this seems to support the common belief that devils like to make clever pacts with loopholes and all manner of legal ensnarements, I hardly think that torturing a mortal or his loved ones in order to force a deal can be considered a legitimate venue for negotiation. But here we are dealing with the Lawyers of Hell, and their codes extend, regrettably, to our world.
Additional Notes from GFD:
Bel’s Bargain is the ritual that was used on the innocent people of Dwimmerholme Farm in 1481, which I provide more source-documents for earlier in this Chronicle. It is as hideous as it is effective, and was ultimately the undoing of the White Cloaks expedition to Charity to root out the Sons of Bel.
-GFD

DDC – 1481 – 12: Reports from Sgt. Paros
18 – 20 Marpenoth
GFD Notes:
Provided by Reks, these are very clean and reliable summaries of what must have been a trying adventure.
-GFD
18 Marpenoth
I’ve never been to Charity before today, and I have to say that it is quite different than the rest of the dale, as I’ve always heard. For starters, it looks much wealthier at first glance, but looking a little closer, I wonder if more than half of the people here aren’t worse off than everyone else in the dale. But that’s not for me to report on now.

The caravan arrived unmolested, though a day later than we would have liked. The rain made for slow going for the wagons with the mud and all. The road along the Charnel River passes just a bit south of a ruined and abandoned village called Whittenhead, about 5 miles before Charity. We saw movement in the ruins, and it seemed clear to me that we were being observed as we passed them by.

A little while later, we were happy to see the walls and lights and smoke of Charity as we got near, but our happiness was short-lived.

In the last 100 yards before the gates, we were able to start taking in some of the details of the place; wrought iron embellishments adorn most buildings, dressing up eaves, the peaks and corners of roofs, and so on. The windows are mostly diamond-patterned leaded-glass, which while prohibitively expensive in the rest of the dale, seem to be common in even the poorer homes here. As we began to pick out detail after detail, our attention was drawn to a flash up high; from a tower perched high in the inner bailey, a fireball blew out the windows on the topmost layer. The flames belched out and subsided, leaving only a flickering flame inside that cast a chaotic, moving light. There was an audible gasp from the dozens of men in the caravan, and some people on the walls of the town. There was one silent instant that was quickly broken by the screaming, flailing, flame-engulfed form of a person coming out of the window and plummeting downward. The flaming spectacle vanished behind the walls in its terminal descent. The spectacle was added to by the forms of what first appear to be large sparks flying from the windows. However, the flight-pattern of these sparks soon revealed them to be burning birds, and before long, their determined flight from the building subsided as the flames took their lives; they fell to the ground leaving contrails of smouldering feathers falling softly behind them. We would find out later who it was that fell burning from that window to his certain death…

With this, the hue and cry went up, and the town came alive, as people came out to either help address the threat of fire, or simply to spectate. It is in this chaos that we were welcomed to the streets of Charity.

We parted ways with the caravan, and sought out our contact at the Old Fort, Medea Rowan. I’m quite suspicious of this woman; as the Madame of the Old Fort and a self-declared priestess of Sharess, she is at the very least a woman of forbidden tastes who encourages excess and vice. But her hospitality was

enormous, and she offered more than any of us would indulge in. She was quite busy and insisted that she’d connect with us during the day tomorrow at a place called Arwencroft (from which I write this very note). She then introduced us to a woman named Flora Scarlett, who had been hired by Basil Muloch many days ago to be our steward. Flora is a wonderful young woman, a native of the town whom everyone seems to admire. She had the keys and a legal agreement for Arwencroft, which I am happy to report is ours to use until we’re concluded here.

Tired and wet, we were happy to retire to Arwencroft, which typifies the middle-class comfort of Charity; there were many coal-stoves warming the place up, many lanterns to light it, and fine furnishings the likes of which one does not really find in the rest of the dale. A warm meal awaited, made by Flora’s own hand, and we took heart.

Flora stayed up late with us, to give us all the recent news that she thought relevant to our mission here.

First, she told us of Dretch’s visit, 10 days ago. He came to Charity, knocked some heads around in the Old Fort, and then headed to the inner bailey (this is the part of Charity at the top of the hill, upon which the estates of the ‘Landmen’ are located). What he did or who he spoke to there is unknown, but he shortly after went into the foothills to the west. This is where his trail goes cold.

Second, a woman named Sarah Gideon died in an accident on the 15th; walking through the gates from the Inner Bailey to the Middle Bailey, a loose stone fell from the gatehouse, struck her on the head, and killed her instantly. Though there are some structures needing a bit of upkeep in the town, this is a tremendous coincidence, as Sarah Gideon was seen coming in and out of the Muloch Estate a couple of times in the previous days.

The third bit of news came to us by way of a runner from the Inner Bailey. He sought out Flora, to give her the news that the commotion we saw was an explosion in the library-tower of the Muloch Estate, that Basil was confirmed dead, and that the Silverstars (a quasi-religious part-time fighting force made up of followers of Selune, Waukeen and the Red Knight, mostly Landmen), had locked the estate down, fearing for the safety of any who would wish to enter.

This is terrible news, as we intended to speak with Basil tomorrow, and indeed, Flora had booked a meeting with him for early morning. We will try to get into Muloch Estate and find out what happened.
But now it is late, and it has been a long journey…
19 Marpenoth
Today was a whirlwind of activity, which I will summarize as neatly I can.
We set out first thing in the morning to investigate the Muloch Estate. This was not easy; the Silverstars,

Lead by Captain Archibald Ferguson, would not let us on the premises. On top of a few of these capable-looking men, there were a score of Ferguson House Guard around the walls of the Muloch Estate, armed with the rifles for which this town is well know.

Using an abundance of caution and diplomacy, we utilized the influence of the local Ambassador to Daggerdale, Ridge Oakdale. This is a man I knew as a child, and though he has no real authority here, and no mentionable resources, he is an able diplomat, and knew his way around the Silverstars. He waited for Archibald to vacate the scene, and spoke this his cousin, Simon Whitmore, who saw his duty

and our place in this investigation clearly. We were permitted entry after many hours of waiting for diplomacy to run its course.

The Muloch Estate was the hunting-ground for a devil that Artorias later identified as a Watcher. This devil-snake thing hunted us with great cunning through the Estate, and had some minions assisting it in what appeared to be a sacking of the library. In the end we bested the thing, but currently, many of our team have pustulent wounds from the bite of the thing that won’t heal. We have sent these team members to Charnel Priory for healing, which I am told will be complete by tomorrow.

The Estate had been ransacked by the Watcher and its helpers. The top-floor of the library-tower (it is a 3-floor affair, very opulent and well-appointed with learning) was still smouldering from the fireball which consumed Basil and his aviary, and most of the books on that floor. We could find no natural reason for the fireball (it wasn’t caused by explosives), and neither the Watcher nor its henchmen were capable of this sort of magic. Someone else caused this destruction and death.

In the kitchens, we found a few very valuable sources of information, which I have collected and enclosed copies of.

GFD Notes: c.f. DDC – 1481 – 13: Note from Phinneas Hoetmer to Basil Muloch and c.f. DDC – 1481 – 14: Selections from the Journal of Loedegan Whitegate. I’ve not seen the other ‘valuable sources of information’ that Paros alludes to here, but he does describe one…

I have just copied a couple of pages from a book of notes from Muloch’s hand, which he took in Cormyr this winter during a long visit he made there. Why he went there, no one knows, but he was gone for most of the winter. His notes are full of family histories, one interesting one attached.

I have given this book and some other valuables to his nephew, Arthur Whitmore, who we met today. Arthur is a stand-up fellow (I’m writing like these people talk…), and everyone in the party, our steward included, thinks we can trust this man.

There were some notes about some of the locals in this pile as well, which I have copied and included. We will be following up tomorrow at the houses of some of these people, who I suspect are tied up in the Sons of Bel business in some fashion.

So, we missed our meeting with Medea Rowan today, and she has rebooked us for tomorrow, but did have the courtesy to send along nice baskets of food and gifts to Arwencroft for the ‘inconvenience’, even though it was us providing the offense.

All of this and a couple of brawls in the street with the locals. The ‘freemen’ of the town are both distrustful of strangers and fond of fisticuffs. No real blood spilled in either encounter, but this is a difficult place to do good work in…
20 Marpenoth
We have made some real progress today. The very first thing we (we being half of us, as half were convalescing at Charnel Priory) did was visit the house of Niles Gideon, the husband of the woman who died in an accident several days ago, who also holds the title of Guildmaster of the Scriveners and Editor

of The Loyalist (the local news publication). As I write this, Gideon is at-large, having escaped us at Whittenhead Ruin…

Investigating his house early in the morning, we found him missing, but clear evidence in his basement of devil-worship. There were two Derelict women in the basement, and two dead men. A nearby pentacle and evidence of torture told us that this was a makeshift site of a Bel’s Bargain Ritual. As I write this, the two women have been taken to Charnel Priory, where they are conducting the Prayer of Adduction presently, to recover their souls. We pray for their success.

One other hideous discovery was made; that Gideon’s young wife Sarah had also been made derelict, and that her ‘murder’ was simply a matter of disposing of the inconvenient husk of a woman who’s main value was as soul-currency. Artorias speculates that her soul was likely used to pay for something as powerful as the Watcher we fought yesterday at the Muloch Estate.

We found notes in Muloch’s kitchen yesterday regarding the purchase of Whittenhead by Niles Gideon, and guessed that he may have gone there. So three of us decided to do some reconnaissance to see if we were right. Whittenhead ruin is one of several small ruined settlements in Charity Hills, abandoned for maybe 10 years or so. Our recon turned into a full-fledged battle, however, as we discovered Niles Gideon there with a host of devil-spawn orcs. Though we slew the orcs nearly to the last, Gideon got away (as well as his infernal orc-sergeant), and showed his hand as a capable sorcerer; he indeed threw a fireball at us that has landed all but myself in Charnel Priority recovering.

Having defeated and driven off Gideon and his foul orcs, we searched the remains of the town and discovered that one of the better-intact homes was being converted into a shrine for the Sons of Bel, and evidence of other rituals was clear. We took what we could to the authorities in Charity, those being;
o John Constable
o Simon Whitmore of the Silverstars
o Chancellor and Earl John Ferguson – Head of the Landmen
o Milburn Carpenter – Secretary of the Labour Assembly – Head of the Freemen
Walter Keystone, the Speaker of the Common Assembly and the Guildmaster of Merchants, was summoned but could not be found. Many are looking for him presently, as he remains unaccounted for. We hope that he has not been a victim of Gideon and his schemes.

We were roundly praised for our discovery of Gideon’s plot, and the rescuing of the two common women from his basement (I wish we had gotten there in time to save their husbands). The authorities were quite interested in learning about the orcs at Whittenhead, and we reported exactly this;

There were three sorts of these foes; regular orcs that you might expect to meet in the mountains, a fiendish orc that was possessed by a powerful devil, and the offspring of the two. Artorias knew quite a bit about this type of enemy, thankfully. The orcs were as difficult as you might expect; fierce and stupid, but they were led by the devilish orc who was clever, and managed to get away. His offspring proved to be the most durable; though young and inexperienced, they were incredibly strong and resilient, requiring magical weapons to harm.

These authorities had much to order after our report and pledged their assistance to our investigation.

Some of our team concluded their convalescence at the Priory in the afternoon, and continued to do more legwork in the town. We procured some silver bullets for Nathan’s pistol, as these are needed to damage some devilkin, and we finally made our meeting with Medea Rowan.

Medea proved to be very helpful. In her line of work, she and her subordinates learn many things, and although, she explained, they wouldn’t normally divulge the secrets of their clients, she felt no particular need to protect Niles Gideon, who’s location she thinks she knows. She’s sure that he was seen headed out the Charnel Gate shortly after our encounter in the late morning, and he had a large group of men with him.

Later in the day we were visited by Earl Ferguson, who we found waiting patiently at Arwencroft, after a runner had been sent for us at the Old Fort. The Earl is not the eldest of the Fergusons, and at about 55 years of age, he is quite fit and sharp. He was accompanied by his wife, Victoria (nee Whitmore) and his sister-in-law, Morgan (nee Muloch, younger sister of Basil). Morgan was very grateful that we uncovered the guilty party to her brother’s murder, and the Earl, who is the highest-ranking man in Charity, gave us a letter-patent to Arwencroft (it is now the possession of the White Cloaks ad infinitum), and a chest of 500 gold as reward for our service, and to aid in any further investigation. He further committed a small group of soldiers to accompany us west, when we told him of our plans to track down Gideon and the men that fled with him. I suggested that he could make a map of the other cultists by taking a head-count in town right away, as the men who are missing would likely be those involved, but he countered saying that Freemen, Middlemen and Landmen alike all travel quite a bit between the various camps and mines of the region, as there is a degree of safety (usually) that permits it.

After many long well-wishes, the Fergusons departed, and our team took to their beds early. We everyone are exhausted from our battle with the Watcher (and the horrible wounds it inflicted), our participation (some of us) in the Prayer of Adduction, which took nearly 16 hours of continuous labour, and now from infected wounds from the orcs at Whittenhead. We will rest a bit before we take to the road to pursue Gideon.
DDC – 1481 – 13: Note from Phinneas Hoetmer to Basil Muloch
Written on 27 Flamerule, 1480, Hoetmer once again displays his prescience, if not his ability to make others take it seriously.
GFD Notes:
This note was in the archives in the Historic Wing of the Yellow Abbey, and was, I think a copy. The original must be at Loedegan Close with the rest of Gale’s things, but Reks didn’t disclose it. From Paros’ journal, we do know that this was recovered in the kitchen at the Muloch Estate, where Basil liked to do most of his reading, when the White Cloaks investigated his home.

I am forced to wonder what it was that Hoetmer didn’t send to Muloch. I never found out, so others will have to discover that secret.
-GFD

My Old Friend;
There will be a Blue Moon in a couple of nights, and when these fall in Flamerule, the whole world seems to go crazy. I certainly do; I have been pouring over old records like there won’t be a tomorrow, and I found something that immediately put me in mind of your ‘sleepy little towne’. This is a copy of some passages of the journal of Loedegan Whitegate that I found in the Yellow Abbey. When I read the one enclosed, I immediately thought of you and yours. I know you are tired of hearing me say that it is Him guiding my hand, and in this case, my pen, so I’ll save all that this time. Please do take consideration of this transcript, however. I feel it will touch upon events in the near future in your part of the dale.

I nearly enclosed one other thing as well. It was a locket that I thought somehow connected to the journal. I will keep it a while and ruminate upon it. I trust my gut, and I trust Him, but sometimes a slow approach is best.

I believe this missive puts me in an awkwardly advantageous position for two old correspondents. I look forward to your next letter, hopefully this decade. If not, I will be happy to have tea with you Hereafter.
Until we meet again, Phin Hoetmer.
27 Flamerule, 1480 DR.
DDC – 1481 – 14: Selections from the Journal of Loedegan Whitegate, 1448 DR.
Copied by Magistrate Phineas Hoetmer, Flamerule, 1480 DR.
GFD Notes:
This was work that Hoetmer was fascinated by; going through old journals of dead heroes to find links to threats in the present. Here was a relevant find; devils breeding orcs. For some reason of divine inspiration, Hoetmer sent this copy of the journal to his friend, Basil Muloch, a year before anyone knew there were problems with devils in the region. Muloch left this in a package in his kitchen, with other things, for the White Cloaks to find. This letter was ultimately used to attempt to triangulate the origins of this coven, and locate the known cultists that fled town after the White Cloaks starting banging heads together.

It is one of the rare instances in which the evidence proved unhelpful, which you will unfortunately read about shortly.
-GFD
9 Mirtul, 1448
South East of Nevermore Lake

We were in the area today following another lead from the confounded dwarves. I hope my brother will soon realize that we will never find Tethyamar, and that we should stop looking.

What we did find today was a demon. My chaplain corrected me, saying that it was a devil, but they are all the same to me. However, the scene we found was not the same as any other I’ve witnessed. We happened upon what we knew was a nest of orcs; the smell of their fires and the way that they roast meat, bursting guts and all, gives them away for a half mile. We stormed the camp immediately; pause and planning are the ruin of any chance encounter in the wilderness, as any good campaigner knows.

Had we stayed our blades only a moment and watched, we may have figured out what was going on, but we did what we thought was best.

We came upon the small camp like an avalanche, and the slaughter was as fierce as it was joyous. I don’t think I’m happier than when I’m killing orcs. However, there was a demon in their midst, and of all things in the world, he was mounting some female orcs. Indeed, one of the men says that there was evidence that he had fornicated with at least a half dozen of these monsters before we showed up and put an end to his damnable rutting. I personally cut both heads from the randy thing, sending it back to the Abyss!

When the dust settled, we searched the rough camp, and found that they were actually roasting a man. He was rotted and cooked beyond recognition, so I never learned his identity. Or what he was doing in the same neck of the mountains as these devil-breeding orcs. I am forced to hope that he was some sort of summoner who got more than he bargained for and exactly what he deserved, but I am not sure.

And in the end, the notion of orcs breeding with devils is both repugnant and worrying.
14 Mirtul, 1448
Northwest of Bloodpine Lake, not far from the Castle
Today we found a camp that looked similar to the one we raided a few days ago by Nevermore Lake. Orcish, foul, recently used.

Someone tried to wipe out an arcane symbol that had been drawn upon the ground, but the very act of doing so only served to highlight the general shape of the symbol; it was what the chaplain calls a pentagram, and he is certain that this is related to the devil (he says) that we killed a few days ago.

There was evidence that a man, or some other creature of a more gentle nature than orcs, spent some time in the camp.

We suspect that the man we found roasting lived with these orcs, and summoned this devil for some deranged, depraved purpose. But we can’t be sure; we killed them all before we had a chance to ask!

DDC – 1481 – 15: Issue of ‘The Loyalist’
21 Marpenoth, 1481
GFD Notes:
I would love to have spent more time in Charity. This place is an anomaly in Daggerdale, as it is a miniature replica of the great city of Westgate. It has its own weekly publication which is distributed to all ‘Middlemen’ and ‘Landmen’ of the town (these being the middle and upper-class men).

This particular broadsheet can still be found plastered on the walls of some of the taverns (they have more than you would find in other Daggerdale settlements) of the town and are not hard to come by.


-GFD




Dauntless, We Go To Press


The Loyalist
21 Marpenoth, 1481 DR

Despite the treachery of the former Editor of The Loyalist, the News must to Press go! Today I, Thomas Page, assume the duties of Editor, as well as those of Guild Master of the Scriveners. There is much mending to be done in both of these Houses, but this cannot stand in the way of Truth, nor will it keep us from our Duty to our Fellow Men of Charity.
The Muloch Estate
With the tragic passing of Lord Muloch on 18 Marpenoth, through the treacherous cavorting with devils of Niles Gideon, our town experiences for the first time since Founding, the complications of primogeniture and the fading of a great House. Below the Loyalist accounts for the remaining claimants to the Estate, and attempts to unravel the complicated issue of how it shall pass, and to whom;

Morgan Ferguson (ne Muloch) – MIDDLE SISTER of Basil. Mrs. Ferguson is married to Benjamin Ferguson, and has by him one son, namely
Godwin Ferguson (A MAN OF 26 YEARS).
Arthur Whitmore (A MAN OF 30 YEARS), son of Chelsea (ne Muloch, DECEASED, and ELDEST SISTER of Basil). That Lord Muloch favoured this nephew is no secret.

Samantha Falconer (ne Muloch, -YOUNGEST SISTER of Lord Muloch). Mrs. Falconer is married to Lord Falconer, and has by him two sons, namely
Oswald Falconer (A MAN OF 20 YEARS) and Byron Falconer (A MAN OF 19 YEARS)
The complications to the settlement of this estate are many, and are inventoried below;

First, that there has never been an issue of succession or primogeniture in Charity, with much praise to Siamorph.

Second, that there are no direct sons beneath or brothers beside the Departed Lord Muloch Third, that the eldest sister of Lord Muloch is herself Departed

Fourth, that the youngest sister is herself married to an Earl, but that her sons are younger than that of;

Fifth, the eldest extant sister has a son more senior that those of her nephews Sixth, that eldest male with Muloch blood has no surviving parents

This entire matter would be enough to confound the Star Chambre of Westgate, to be sure. As such, it is no surprise that LORD CHANCELLOR FERGUSON has put the estate under probate for 66 days, as per the Ancient and Correct Lawes of Succession, which were brought here bound at Founding. That the estate hasn’t passed to Arthur Whitmore, eldest extant living male in the line, and favoured nephew of Lord Muloch, indicates that there are nuances that only Landmen can appreciate in this matter.

It has been suggested that the matter may indeed be brought to the Star Chambre for settlement, and that new Letters of Patent may be drafted and signed by King Verovan II himself!
WANTED: A TRAITOR MOST FOUL – Mr. Niles Gideon
With thanks to the White Cloaks of Dagger Falls, the demon-copulating Mr. Gideon was exposed for the traitor and villain that he is. It was he who invited demon-bred orcs to trouble the lands about Whitenhead Ruin. It was he who, in a most cold and brutal stroke, murdered his own young, beautiful wife, Sarah Gideon. It was he who orchestrated a Felony of Souls, a crime so terrible it is difficult to even put to press. The Loyalist has been assured by Mr. John Constable that Mr. Gideon also played a key role in the death of Lord Muloch, though he is not at liberty, or has not been made privy to, any further knowledge on the matter.

On the 20th of Marpenoth, Mr. Gideon fled our town, knowing that the White Cloaks were returning from Whitenhead with the knowledge of his treachery. He was seen leaving the Charnel Gate in the evening, with 6, perhaps 8, other men. Mr. Constable reports that his guards suspected that 2 men were ‘drunk’ or otherwise out of their wits and were being carried along by others in the retinue.

The Loyalist now suspects that the two ‘drunk’ men were actually Mr. Walter Keystone, Free of the Merchants (and Guild Master of the same) and Speaker of the Common Assembly, and Mr. Percival Silver, Free of the Fine Smiths (and Guild Master of the same). These men were both later reported missing, and subsequent investigations by Mr. Constable revealed that the offices of both men had been the scene of violent abductions.

LORD CHANCELLOR FERGUSON has placed a bounty on Mr. Gideon; 250 crowns for his head, 500 crowns for him to be delivered intact.

The Merchants’ Guild is offering 100 crowns for the safe return of Mr. Keystone. The Fine Smiths is offering 50 crowns for the safe return of Mr. Silver.

By ACT of the ROYAL ASSEMBLY – License is Given to New Free Men
Surely by now, the heroism of the White Cloaks of Dagger Falls is well known to all Men of Charity, Freemen, Middlemen and Landmen alike. Even though their deeds are measured differently by many of our citizens, there can be little doubt that it was them that discovered the treachery of Mr. Niles Gideon. No questions can be raised about the outcome of their investigation, even though many questioned their authority to conduct such herein. Despite mixed feelings from our citizenry, the outcome of their work has been evaluated not only by popular opinion, but by Ecumenical Council and Royal Assembly alike.

Throughout the 20th of Marpenoth, guided by a Divine Rite brought by the White Cloaks, the Sisters of Charnel Priory managed to save the souls of two of the victims of Gideon’s Treachery. Happily, the details of the Rite are known only to those Sisters and victims unfortunate enough to have endured it, and the Loyalist prefers to keep it at that. Even before the last Rite was completed, and that last Soul in Peril was rescued, the Divine Elders of Charity were organizing an assembly to investigate this matter in detail, and to assess the role, and the culpability, if any, of the White Cloaks. Meeting late in the day of the 20th, Ecumenical Council, led by Mattias Greylord, found the White Cloaks to be free of any culpability, and in fact forwarded a petition to the ROYAL ASSEMBLY to make the White Cloaks Free of the Ecumenical Council.

The ROYAL ASSEMBLY met later that same night, at the behest of Mattias Greylord, to discuss the petition for citizenship. Olthough there was reportedly heated debate on the matter, LORD CHANCELLOR FERGUSON ultimately ruled that the White Cloaks would be granted citizenship, and be declared Free of the Ecumenical Council and Act of ROYAL ASSEMBLY.

The proceedings for this Act followed early this morning. Happily attending the brief legal ceremony was Mattias Greylord and most of the Divine Elders. Ecumenical Council, it should be noted, is not often named to attendance in these rare notarizations, but given the circumstances, it is not surprising that it was so in this case.

Making residence in Arwencroft, the White Cloaks will be staying in our Faire Towne for an indeterminate period of time. Invitation to Arwencroft can be gained through appointment with Flora Scarlett (late of the Old Fort), who the White Cloaks have retained as Aide de Camp for the duration of their stay. Needless to say, the Loyalist is grateful for the White Cloaks and their selfless, perilous service to our Towne. Eftsoons of helping the Dalesmen of Dwimmerholme, we are grateful for their presence and heroism here in Charity, and wish them Gods’ Speed wither next they go.
DDC – 1481 – 16: Selections from the Journal of Nathan Gale
22 Marpenoth, 1481 - Journal of Nathan Gale
GFD Notes: Why Reks will only give me snippets of this Journal, and not the whole thing has been a constant source of friendly debate between us. He insists that the journal is full of very sensitive materials of an ongoing matter. How the content below could not be described the same is curious. At any rate, the words of Gale are, as always, interesting and provide a counter-opinion to events.
-GFD

This town is full of liars and villains and secrets and incest. I don’t for one minute think that Gideon acted only with a handful of people that he fled town with. I am suspicious of Medea Rowan and Chancellor Ferguson. They wield too much power in a town so small to have known so little about a cult right under their noses. And they are quick to placate us, while so few others offer the same. I will take Ferguson’s gold and Medea’s drink and whores, but only to deprive them of some small provision they might find useful against us. I will, of course, keep this to myself until there is proof. I must own that I have a bad record of proclaiming things before they’re ripe, so-to-speak.

Here are a couple of things worth bringing to the Order that happened over the last couple of days.
After the Ecumenical Council
The days that followed the Ecumenical Council of 20 Mpnth provided some much-needed rest. For those of us that took part in the Prayer of Adduction, we were exhausted through and through, to parts of us we weren’t cognisant of before this ordeal.

For some of us, the time was spent becoming familiar with the people and culture of Charity. Though we are hailed as heroes by some, this is still a town of extreme xenophobia, and nearly half of the people we encounter shun us, or whisper behind our backs. The disparate treatment of the people towards us mirrors the town itself, for this is a place of contrasts, which I have come to appreciate over the last few days. The stone architecture that is found everywhere is solid and well-laid, though it has clearly been built for form instead of function; there are many embellishments in the stonework that you don’t find in the Dale, but in Dagger Falls you won’t find walls with crumbling mortar or cracked statues. There are fine leaded-glass windows in nearly every building, but the streets don’t get cleaned as well or as often as they do in Dagger Falls, which lends a smell to the town that is now somewhat muted by the accumulating slush and snow.

It didn’t take long for the locals to discover that we are staying at Arwencroft, and to start prying into our business. Soon, visitors were booking appointments to talk to various members of our party, managed mostly by our assistant, Flora. Most come to offer thanks, some to offer warnings, and the rare poorly-screened visitor to offer condemnation. The memory of many of these people blend into two categories; the relatively rough and dirty Freemen, and the relatively friendly and clean Middlemen.
Elizabeth Miner
Elizabeth came on her own early on the morning of the 21st of Mpnth. She insisted on speaking to me alone, and my ill-timed passing through the parlour eliminated any reasonable excuse to not meet with her. She is as respectable as her class allows; she has a clean but old dress and a fancier jacket that is clearly for special occasions. Her face is clean, but her hands are stained yellow from her work as a tanner’s aid. She is humble, and generally does not look up at me when she talks. Here is what she said to me, in as close to her strong and nearly unintelligible accent as I can write;

“I’m dread-sorry to ‘mpose, sir. But there’s those that says you know from demons, and I ‘ears tell that you know of lakes of fire, and skies of ash. Everyone says you rescued some souls, and that’s good work, sure. But there’s souls that need ‘couting yet, sir. I’m talkin’ ‘bout me ‘usband, I am. Griff. Griff Miner, sir. Good man…” she stops to pull a nice-but-frayed kerchief from her pocket, to wipe her eyes, and her sniffling nose.

“Griff is one o’them as got kilt at the Fergy Saltpetre mine last year. Only, I weren’t never sure ‘ee was kilt at all. I dreamed of him, in a lake of fire, under a sky of ash I did. Only, the dreams stopped recently. I know it don’t sound right, but I was glad to see him in my dreams, even though ‘e was tormented. At least I could see ‘im. Remember ‘im. Now ‘e’s gone, e is. I think ‘e’s in more trouble now than even before.” She finally looks up at me .

“Go git me Griff” she says, trying to be brave. She sets her chin and nods, but this countenance quickly dissolves into a very brief fit of sob-filled begging. She apologized for her lack of composure, and excused herself as quickly as possible from Arwencroft.
Now here was more than a bit of news.
This common woman, a tanner, knew about the visions I had of Avernus, and the souls of the damned from Dwimmerholme. This isn’t exactly a secret at this point, but the fact that it has percolated to a woman of her stature means that it is surely common knowledge. For good or for ill.

But also, why had no one told us about the problems at the ‘Fergy Saltpetre’ mine ‘last year’?! I immediately went to Flora, who confirmed that in the late fall of 1480, 12 men were buried in a mine collapse that happened just west of the settlement of Bridgehead, well into the mountains. The little mining settlement is affectionately known as ‘Fergy’s Hole’, and there are 12 families there missing their men. This news combined with what we found in Basil’s kitchen (the journal of Ardelusk), and the general direction of our fleeing quarry, tell me that our next steps are clear. In fact, a couple of the team who have read Ardelusk’s account from 1448, know exactly where he is talking about (‘South East of Nevermore Lake’), and this location is likely the same as Fergy’s Hole.

Our path is clear, and I hope our leader see’s it as plainly as I do. I will share this with him in the morning and see.


DDC – 1481 – 17: Report from Sgt. Paros
Uktar 1, 1481
GFD Notes:
This is the terrible conclusion of the White Cloaks mission to stop the Sons of Bel in Charity. This report was handed to me by Reks with a great deal of solemnity. It accounts for the death of three heroes in one fell swoop, a terrible sacrifice that was made to cripple the power of the Sons. Nothing else left to say except ‘read on’…
-GFD
Administrator:
I am overdue putting this report together. We have suffered great losses, and the last three days have been a blur of travel through unseasonal blizzards. I am nestled warmly again in Arwencroft with what remains of the team and will head out first thing tomorrow morning for Dagger Falls and the Close.

Please forgive the brief nature of this report; I will be summarizing several days of fighting and exploration all while battling a hideous head-injury that I fear has quite rattled my senses. On with it…

23 Marpenoth
The morning started with a pitched battle between Gale and me. He insisted that he knew exactly where Gideon was headed. I agreed with him but wanted to take another day to provision properly for the journey and the battles we knew we’d have with devils, orcs and sorcerers. Shea and Abigail agreed with me, and although this isn’t a democracy, I was glad of their support. Artorias was ready to charge off with Gale, saying that he had everything he needed, except a devil to destroy.

We did procure and order up the supplies and weapons we’d need, to the best of our reconning, and made arrangements to leave on the 24th, as early as possible. We made fast friends with Sir Simon Whitmore, who would accompany us along with a half-dozen riders to Fergy’s Hole. I half-expected Gale and Artorias to be gone when I got back to Arwencroft, but to their credit, they waited for us. My patience as a leader will require more effort in the future.
24 Marpenoth
Set out in terrible weather, rain and sleet. We were aware of scouts following us on the opposite side of the Charnel River but going after them would be a distraction. From a distance, it looked like a single man or man-sized thing. We were set-upon by some orcs just on the other side of Bridgehead, and the wounds we suffered caused us to turn back to that small hamlet and rest for the night.
25 Marpenoth
Terrible weather again today. I think there might be some sorcery at work here, trying to keep us from our quarry, but I’m told I’m getting paranoid (though Gale says I’m not paranoid enough). We fought a terrible fiendish-ogre on a bridge today, and two of Whitmore’s men were killed by thrown-spears from the creature. We destroyed it in the end, though at great cost to our resources; the thing required magic and silver to harm, and it did a great deal of damage to many of us. Artorias says that this creature likely represents a full soul-coin from Bel’s Bargain. I wondered out loud how many such terrible foes we’d face in the days to come. “At least twelve” was Artorias’ answer.

By night we made it to Fergy’s Hole. This is a fairly austere camp of about a hundred people, or was a hundred people. These are the families of the miners, and with half of the miners killed last year in the “collapse”, and the closure of the mine, this village lacks purpose and morale. To make matters worse, they were sorely treated by Dretch several days before we arrived. Here are some details as I recall them;
Fergy’s Hole
This is a settlement of 90 people, mostly working men, but a few families and unattached women. Architecturally, it could be described as a semilunar stone fort against the side of the mountain.

However, it is not typical of other forts in the region. The walls are lower than forts found all around Daggerdale, and they haven’t been constructed with too much care; many blocks are set about by crumbling mortar, and the odd block has tumbled to the ground. Despite this, there are still wrought- iron embellishments atop the walls, and well-crafted and decorative wrought-iron lamps line both sides of the wall.

With Sir Simon leading the way, we were lead through the single gate of the fort without too much difficulty, but the guards all eyed us suspiciously. As we entered the courtyard, we were noticed by

many people bustling about wrapping up their duties at the end of the workday. Most of them shot icy glares at us, and some actually headed indoors at the sight of us.

“It’s your colleague, Mr. Dretch”, a good man named Sheriff Harrison explained. “He put a proper scare into all of us, ‘e did. Now, Sir Simon ‘ere vouches for you, but you better be on your best behaviour, lads…and ladies…you don’t have friends here, and none of you looks quite so scary as Mr. Dretch. Come with me…”

He lead us to a small building in one corner of the courtyard. It is a single-story stone building in a dreadful state of repair. The roof has many gaping holes in it, and there are no furnishings to speak of. “You can bunk ‘ere for the night, ‘Cloaks. But best be on your way first thing in the morning.”

“I’m dread sorry about the attitude of these men, Paros.” Simon began. “We don’t take to strangers much in Charity, and the mining outposts are worse than the rest of us. With the visit that Mr. Dretch paid a while ago, I don’t think you can expect better treatment than this. I have some wounded men to tend to, and some supplies to deliver to these men. I’ll check in with you later.”
Emma Cole
This is a young woman of about sixteen years who visited us in our humble lodge late in the evening. She has long, curly brown hair that frames a dainty face. Her eyes are bright, and her expression firm and confident. She was wearing a dirty, kitchen-stained garb, but her hands were clean, and her clothing in good repair. “Emma Cole, Sirs. Pleased to make your ’quaintance.” The girl speaks confidently and looks us in the eyes when she talks.

“I know everyone ‘round ‘ere ‘ates you, and is afraid. Mr. Dretch asked some very ‘ard questions, and ‘e actually drew on the Sheriff. But I’m not afraid of ‘im, and certainly not you. Dretch was kind to me, ‘cause I was honest with ‘em. ‘E asked about the ‘cave in’ up at the old Saltpetre mine, and I told him I never thought it was an accident. There’s none so careful as the Saltepetre miners. I know, ‘cause my da was one. He was one o’ them as vanished in that mine. I went there a few months ago. I got a proper punishment for it, I did, but I seen that mine, and it didn’t look caved in to me. I also thought I seen a man walking around down in the ‘ole, but to be honest with you too, the man scared me proper, and I run all the way ‘ome, I did.

“I think those men are down there. I think something really evil happened, and I think you’re ‘ere to fix it. I don’t know why Mr. Dretch never came back, though…”
26 Marpenoth
Early in the morning, the Sheriff came to visit us. He had been given some papers to read by Whitmore, and was now properly up to date on happenings in Charity.

“I may have been a little ‘ard on you lot. I didn’t realize what was going on in the rest of Charity. I still don’t think there can be a proper accounting for that Dretch, but you lot can come and go as you will from my fort.
