“I would really caution you against going any further west of ‘ere; there’s a lot of bad road between ‘ere and the old mine. And it has been standard procedure to caution all people from the mine. But Sir Simon comes with orders to help you as we can, and if you aim to head to the mine, we won’t stop you, but just tell you to be careful.”

We would need more than a little care, as this is as far as Whitmore was authorized to take us. For all that, he still rode with us for a few miles beyond his charge, to make sure we were on the right track. We found ourselves missing his blades before the day was over.

This day was the first of three very hard days, and I wish now we had turned back with Whitmore.

With the weather as it was, we didn’t make the mine until nearly evening, and found the area guarded by two cave giants. We weren’t sure that these were part of the coven at the time, but surely they must have been. How they were enticed into the service of the Sons we never learned. Anyway, they broke three sets of ribs in our company, and left us in a terrible state for the next encounter.

We did indeed enter the mines, and found no evidence at all of a cave-in. In fact, it was clear to us that many people had been coming and going from the mine for days, weeks, possibly months. In one of the top-most chambres of the mine we fought with a group of fiendish orcs, this time an orcish sorcerer was with them, and though we had girded ourselves against flame (knowing our foes and having prepared), she attacked us with lightning, sensing our strengths and weaknesses. We killed half of them and sent the other half fleeing into the depths of the mines.
GFD Notes:
Further research indicates that there were still agents loyal to the Sons of Bel at Charity, and that they knew what potions and other preparations the White Cloaks were making for the foray into the mine. Their enemy was ready for them…
-GFD
It was at this point that I started to think about our brothers in Tethyamar, and the War in the Deep. It is dangerous business, and I don’t envy the captain and his men their charge, though I’m ashamed to admit it.

Rather than risk the mine, we camped for the night outside a little distance away. We could not keep a fire going, and were cold, wet and sore the next morning.
27 Marpenoth
This was a day of searching the mines and skirmishing with various orcs and other vile vermin. Fighting all day in the maze of tunnels was tiring work, but we prevailed each time, though it was taking its toll at this point. We were out of healing potions and other restorative magics, and we had a very heated discussion about turning back. We decided to stick it out, as at one point in the day, Artorias noticed something in the mine; a wall with Netherese carvings on it. Ardelusk and his brother had been looking for Tethyamar all those years in this region. They nearly found an old door to Netheril and more.

Tonight we decided to brave sleeping in the mine, rather than face another night of cold and rain. We regretted it, as we were set upon all night by small skirmishes, designed to keep us tired. We would set out the next day unrested and unprepared. We should have turned back…
28 Marpenoth – Kahlmadrid and Tragedy
We went to the Netherese wall and found that it had arcane scrawlings about it that suggested what we’d find on the other side; an ancient Netherese summoning chambre. Artorias and Abigail set about

investigating the wall and the markings and discovered a very well-hidden message carved on the wall. With a source of light held down low to the ground (as only someone searching would notice), there was a barely-perceptible warning carved on the door; “Turn back, you fools! -AD”

Dretch had been here and left a warning for us. Unfortunately, it wasn’t enough to convince Gale and Artorias, though we argued about it for an hour. In the end, Abigail opened the door with the proper incantation, and we went into the chambres beyond, which we now know to be the ruins of Kahlmadrid, of ancient Netherese origin. We had read of this chambre in Abandon Hope, and how a renegade- branch of Netherese summoners cavorted with and summoned devils of old.

The chambres beyond were a horror show of terrible devils, derelicts, and fiendish orcs. Tired before we began, we pressed through battle after battle, before coming to the central chambre of Kahlmadrid. There, we found Niles Gideon, a dozen soldiers all well armed and prepared, and the missing guildmasters, Keystone and Silver. With them were a couple of the lesser devils we turned back in previous chambres.

This battle was the most difficult we faced as a team, but we pulled through, largely due to the magics of Abigail, who displayed a great deal more efficacy in dispatching groups than we’d seen before. In the end, we managed to capture Gideon and a few of his men, and slew the rest. No one and nothing escaped from us. Our greatest discovery was in Gideon’s bags; the Itineris Diabolus was on his person, and Gale and Artorias, even the others, were astonished to find it.

But our real battle was still ahead of us. In the central chambre we found a great summoning portal, upon which was carved a complicated puzzle. We could see that the cultists from Charity had been trying to open the portal but had been unsuccessful. This is when everything went wrong…

Gale recognized the puzzle as being the back of cover of the Itineris Diabolus, and looking closely, he could see that the book itself contained the ‘key’ to the puzzle, which was a simple order in which various symbols needed to be activated on the portal. We might have gathered up our prisoners and left, disregarding the door, the book and the key, but this is where Gideon played his final card.

“Wouldn’t you like to end all of this, heroes?” he inquired bitterly. “Do you know what’s on the other side of that door? Why, it’s my master, Azbael. He is waiting for us to open this portal, so that he may come here without the restrictions of the currency of souls; he would be completely free to stay, to roam, to do…whatever he wished…But you are too frightened to open that door and face him, aren’t you?”

This turned into a heated argument among all of us. Gale wanted to open the portal and face Azbael. I think he wanted to face down Avernus, as he had been doing in his dreams since Dwimmerholme, but I won’t guess at his motivations. In the end, we decided that we would camp out in the chambre and decide in the morning what to do. We had secured many of the derelicts as well as we could and had our other prisoners besides. We set watches, as the entire situation was precarious.

It is at this point that I should own my failure of leadership. We should have marched out of that place, and into the cold fresh air of the mountains. But I was tired and my head throbbed from days of being bashed about, and fighting with my team. I relented, and allowed for camping in a stupid spot.

On third watch I placed Gale and Shea. I knew that Shea was opposed to opening the portal and gave her instructions to wake me if Gale got up to anything. However, Gideon managed to fool us all; he put Shea to sleep with sorcery, and then convinced Gale to open the portal. I shall never hear the words ‘and all hell broke loose’, and not think of that moment, or what that really means. For the room became nearly too hot to breathe of a sudden, and a horrible wailing wind cut through everything, waking and terrifying us all. I saw Gale enter the portal; where once there had been a great stone, now there was a shimmering doorway to Avernus, and many devils waiting on the other side. I saw the hideous face of Azbael, as it smiled grotesquely at Gale.

At that moment, Abigail and Shea (who had been woken by the burning, screaming wind) raced into the portal to come to Gale’s aid. They began a desperate battle with Azbael and a dozen other devils, while Artorias, myself and Imogen tried to organize a defense. Already, devils were starting to approach the portal, and Artorias held them back, screaming for the rest of the team to retreat to safety. “The only safety” I heard Gale say “will come with Azbael dead!”

While Artorias held the door, Imogen was now caught up dealing with our prisoners, who were doing their best to attempt an escape, and to free the derelicts from the next room in which we had them secured. A couple of times I tried to enter the portal, but Artorias checked my advance; “this portal will not stay open long, boss” he yelled “and we must keep it that way! Hold the door with me and pray for our friends”.

But it was hopeless; though Artorias and I held the door, beating back lesser devils of a dozen varieties, we could see our three friends through the chaos; they fought now, back-to-back on a blood-red plateau of hellish stone, and the waves of heat and the evil miasma of the place made them nearly impossible to make out clearly. And now, they were surrounded by a throng of devils that seemed to grow in numbers with each passing moment.

At this point, Azbael himself, unengaged from our friends, strode confidently toward the opening, his 12’ high hulking form a terror. My stomach turned, and I took a step back and wanted nothing more than to run. In a haze I looked over my shoulder, and saw that Imogen was now on her back fighting for her life, with the throng of derelicts atop her flailing mindlessly, their numbers too much for her. The other prisoners were gone, except for Gideon, who now stood in the doorway, poised to flee, but delaying, taking in with sick glee, the horrible and desperate scene he had created.

I had a feeling of despair like I’ve never felt before or since, and I know now that it was the combination of the situation and the aura of the devil that advanced on us. But Artorias held fast, and he bolstered my resolve. Azbael was now at the door, though already it began to shrink, the 10’ diameter opening shrinking at the rate of about 1’ a second. Azbael had little time, and he did his best to get past Artorias; he charged headlong with his great horns, but the armored form of my friend held a divine steadfastness, and Azbael was rebuked; he bounced back fully into the portal off the great shield of my friend. It was at this point that everything slowed down in my mind; I could see it all happen in horrifying slow motion.

Azbael, now laying on his back on the other side of the nearly-closed portal, cracked his whip and it wrapped around my throat, pulling me violently toward the shrinking portal, threatening to pull me in. Inside Hell, as I lurched toward it, I could make out the voice of Shea call out “Blessed Amaunator protect us!”, as she held something over her head in both hands, and a great flash of light seared away

the devils around them, and then all was replaced by a blinding light none could look on. Azbael roared in defiance and pain, and just as the portal was less than a foot wide, Artorias grabbed the whip, and pulled hard and fast, and the forearm of Azbael came through the portal, whip in hand, just as it closed for good and severed the arm.

All the while, Gideon cast one last spell, dousing Imogen in acid, burning her terribly and many of the derelicts that had already beaten her into unconsciousness. She now lay in a shallow pool of acid, and as I tried to pull the whip from my throat (it still seemed to tighten with its own malevolent purpose), and Artorias rushed to rescue Imogen, Gideon fled, and that was the last I saw of him.

In the moments that followed, Artorias dispatched all the derelicts, which was an even lower-low for us; their souls were indeed forfeit now, but we needed to protect Imogen. Imogen was revived with what little magic we had left, and rushed to the stone door, that moments ago was a portal to Hell, and beat her fists upon it. The sight of her acid-burned face screaming and crying at that door I will never forget.

Artorias dutifully secured our things as best he could, while I pulled Imogen away. We then gathered as many of our things as we could and taking one last look at the portal which had consumed our friends, departed Kahlmadrid and tragedy.

On the way out, taking a large supply of Gale’s powder, we rigged up a blast to shut the mine- entrance. This actually worked better than planned; we heard several secondary explosions happen deep within the mine, and the sounds of rock settling lasted for hours. I believe the entrance to Kahlmadrid is thoroughly closed.


With the noise likely to draw attention, we decided that, despite our fatigue, we’d have to keep moving. We marched all night, and found ourselves back at Fergy’s Hole mid-day on the 29th.
29 Marpenoth
Marched and rested at Fergy’s Hole. Gave a report to Sheriff







The Devil Azbael

Harrison, who confirmed that he heard the explosions and rumblings from the mine here, many miles away. There are not means of correspondence with Charity from this settlement. They don’t use messenger-birds the way we do in the rest of the dale, to my surprise. News will have to await our arrival. We leave early tomorrow, and now I must rest.
30 Marpenoth
Marched all day. Met a Ferguson patrol mid-day, who accompanied us back to Charity.
1 Uktar
Arrived in Charity around evening. Went to Arwencroft, and had Flora summon the authorities. Chancellor Ferguson, John Constable, Secretary Carpenter, Ambassador Oakdale and a few others all attended us promptly, and we gave our story.

The group was dismayed at what they heard; that Niles Gideon had escaped, and worse, that the Itineris Diabolus was unaccounted for. We expect that Gideon managed to grab it in the chaos of our battle at the Gate, but we don’t know for sure. The Gate Chambre was such a mess of bodies, gear, smoke and the miasma from Avernus, that our departure was disorderly and hasty.

They were equally sorry to hear about our companions, who remained in Hell battling a ceaseless army of devils, and a prayer was organized for them. Flora and Oakdale both asked if we wanted messages sent to Dagger Falls and the Close, but I declined. I was, and remain, unsure of who our allies and who our enemies are in Charity. Gideon never returned to Charity, as far as anyone knows; there are likenesses of him on every corner of the town, and a 1,000-crown price on his head. Chancellor Ferguson congratulated us on a job well done, and said that they would have to remain vigilant, but for the time being, suspected that the ‘Gideon Cult’ (as he’s calling it) has been supressed. I am unsure it has. I’m only sure that we found the book, found a gate to hell, lost the book, lost our friends, and caved in the mine. I’m not sure how permanent any of those certainties are.

So, in the morning, I will be riding hard, and you’ll have heard all of this first-hand from me, by the time you read this report.
I am tired, and my head won’t stop ringing, so now I must rest.
GFD Notes:
This is the last of Sgt. Paros’ account that I was provided with. His debriefing at the Close was something for which no records were produced. The debriefing is something of a legend, though. All of the children in the Close knew about it, as Cpt. Warburton had made his way to the Falls to attend it, and Mr. Dretch had concluded his business in Foothills Farm (c.f. DDC – 1481 – 18). The shouting at that debriefing rang through the Close for hours (this was during the evening of Uktar 3), until the middle of the night. At the peak of the shouting, dire oaths were issued from all but the Captain, and it seemed as though the company might sunder. Just then, as I’ve been told by the children, Troia Truestar arrived, and calmed the entire thing down. Again, I don’t know exactly what transpired, and if there is a record, I haven’t seen it. But it is clear that the fate of the White Cloaks rested on a fine edge at that moment, and that only the diplomacy of Ms. Truestar kept it all together.
-GFD
DDC – 1481 – 18: Report from Helm Thunderstorm, Foothills Farm, on the Cleansing of the Sons of Bel from that Settlement
17 Marpenoth, 1481. Report sent from Magistrate Thunderstorm to Bishop Whitegate, summarizing the eradication of the Sons of Bel in Foothills Farm.
GFD Notes:
These are the most pristine sources any chronicler could hope for; a formal report issued through formal channels, available in duplicates in several reliable repositories.

But I would trade all of that for thirty minutes of discussion with Dretch to get his side of the story. I was granted neither that nor his report to Reks on the matter. While I do consider the threat to Foothills Farm to be concluded (in fact, it really didn’t get off the ground, before Dretch ferreted it out), there is a growing list of primary sources that could explain what happened but are hard to come by.
-GFD
17 Marpenoth, 1481
Report from Your Servant, Magistrate Thunderstorm of Foothills Cathedral to, His most Holy Excellence, Bishop Whitegate of Dagger Falls.
Bishop:
I commit this report to our library here in Foothills, and by carried correspondence to you for the benefit of the Yellow Abbeye.

The crux of this report is on the doings of our Brother Avenger Alystair Dretch, and his timely interdiction in the development of a branch of what I have come to learn is a cult called the Sons of Bel, ostensibly worshipers of Bel and other such lesser devils.

Brother Alystair arrived here on the 14th of Marpenoth, and after Compline, barred exit from the Cathedral, and had our Lt. round up everyone else in town that didn’t attend the ceremony. Agitated though the Chaunteans (and select others, including a few visiting dwarves from Tethyamar) were, everyone in town complied, with the exception of a few villains who were about to be found out.
Dretch declared that anyone not in attendance be tracked down and interrogated.
Normally I would not take orders from any but your Holy Excellence, but I did assist Br. Dretch in this request, though he was (as is his way) impolite and impertinent in his manner of asking. But he was (again, as is his way) correct; a few men from the local militia hid in their basement when all were summoned, and we discovered that these men, all locals who of late spent a great deal of time ranging to the north, were indeed members of the Sons of Bel. We discovered prayer books and other materials that I have submitted to you with this report, that alone would have made their conviction certain. But Dretch also coaxed the truth from them and discovered that more of their number were camped to the north and were cavorting with hobgoblins from the edge of the dale.

On the morning of the 15th, Dretch departed on his own immediately after Matins, leaving instruction for the Sun Blades to follow him after sunrise. He knew the location of the camp (some three miles north of the farm, and a mile east of the Feyspring River), and wanted to reconnoitre it on his own before the troops arrived.

There he discovered a group of 6 men that had come through in the first caravans of spring, all the way from Cormyr. They had been part of a larger caravan that went to the Castle to trade and broke off at some point to perpetrate this devilish plot. We later learned that these men had corresponded with the locals for nearly a year, getting the foundations of the cult in order, and that they somehow convinced their local counterparts to inculcate a renegade element of the Visideck (the western-most settlement of the Grentzeldeck hobgoblins) to partake in this devil worship.

What Dretch found was a small camp of the Cormyreans and a dozen hobgoblins, three of which were possessed by devils. Dretch decided not to wait for the Sun Blades to catch up to him before engaging, though he did circle the camp, attacking from the north, so that any escapees would run into the Sun Blades coming from the south. However, there were none. Dretch put them all to the blade, and mercilessly tracked down the few that attempted escape, and executed them.

The Sun Blades arrived shortly after to help secure the site and seize all evidence of this cult and materials useful to it. Some were destroyed on-site, and others you will find accompanying this report. It seems that this business is concluded before too much mischief could be accomplished. But I am left with a few questions unanswered, to my satisfaction or indeed of Mr. Dretch’s. To wit:

1. How did the Cormyrean-branch of this cult recruit three of our soldiers, with remote correspondence?

2. How did they know about a renegade element of the Grentzeldeck, when most of the dealings of these insular hobgoblins are unknown to even our most accomplished scouts?

3. What was the long-term plan for this cult? A few fiendish hobgoblins don’t constitute a security crisis, especially for our farm, which has Class IV fortifications, and a constant supply of soldiers marching to and from the Castle and the Falls.

I will leave these questions with your Holy Excellence and pray for your wisdom and my learning on the matter.
Your servant,
Magistrate Thunderstorm.
GFD Notes:
What isn’t mentioned in this report, as it was discovered days later, and I have only heard about it by talking to folks in the single tavern at Foothills, is that the three men of the town in custody all died mysteriously while Alystair was hunting down their co- conspirators. I have only rumour and hearsay to go on, but they were consumed by some unnatural fever which desiccated them over the course of a couple of hours and ended their lives. I SPECULATE that this was some sort of pact they made with their master, Abigor, whom they were ultimately unable to summon, or to be of any further use. So many loose ends here…
-GFD

DDC – 1481 – 19: A Discussion with Administrator Reks about the Sons of Bel
From our discussion on 29 Elesias, 1482 DR
Once again, I record our discussion as it unfolded, warts and all. Apologies in advance…
-GFD
Grafton Fitzdecker: Now we come to the Sons of Bel…
Administrator Alen Reks: Yes! I consider the matter quite concluded. Shall we sup?
GFD: “Quite Concluded”?
AAR: Yes, very quite concluded. And we made a tidy profit, too, human resources notwithstanding. Do you know that Flora Scarlett still ‘attends us’ in Charity, at a fine town home we almost never use any more? That sounds wasteful, doesn’t it? But it isn’t. She’s a useful bird, she is.

GFD: From the reports I’ve read, no one knows how the cult even infiltrated the dale, though it is no doubt the influence of the Netherese, or at least Melagaunt or his agent, Mouvranesh. Are you not concerned that there are more of them out there? Or that we missed some of the ring leaders?

AAR: Heavens, no. Or, yes, rather. Of course, I’m concerned. They did terrible things, especially up at Dwimmerholme, where I think the body-count was highest. Or was it that damned mine in Charity Hills that had the most dead? Who remembers? At any rate, we left no trace of those cults in Dwimmerholme or Foothills. Probably Charity too.
GFD: “Probably Charity”?
AAR: Probably, yes. Shall we talk about probability for a moment? Ah yes, ha ha! It is probable, indeed likely that you and I will crack open a bottle of Immersea Red (I have a ’73 that can’t wait another year to be uncorked), and perhaps a wheel of Mystral Grove sharp cheddar. Then it is probable that you’ll tell me what you’re actually doing here, and what you actually want to know, because certainly (which is at one end of our probability scale) you didn’t come here to learn about dead cultists and their vanquished organizations.

GFD: I remain uncertain…[I pause and Reks smiles]…of the status of the Sons of Bel, and I think the Keep will want to know about it. Also, it seems to me that there is a high likelihood of there being elements of it remaining in Charity. From what I’ve read, Gideon was no mastermind. He was a learned and connected man in his caste, but there is no evidence that he had any connections in Cormyr, where all of this seems to start. Someone else must have given him the translated Belial Prayerbook.

AAR: Perhaps Old Man Muloch? Oh! I can see you don’t like that suggestion one bit, and I confess that I just said it to see if you were paying attention. No, I think he was the real victim here, in fact. Do you know that his household has undergone complete Dissolution? That’s a thing in the Dutchy (which I call it), and their idea of good government. So now there are three great families in Charity, and I trust they

can tend to their own affairs. After all, who am I to suggest that they need our help. They will ask if and when they do. In the meantime, I’ll send my Cloaks off to fight more proximal and exciting foes.

GFD: You don’t find the very fact of their reduction to three houses somewhat…coincidental, or worth concern?

AAR: Not in the least, my pretty-blue-eyed, interrogator! They followed a process, as is their way; after sixty-six days of probate, they underwent a three-hundred-thirty-three day Dissolution, and now, four minus one is three, and the matter is concluded, without cause for further inquiry or worry, wouldn’t you agree?
GFD: I see…
AAR: What matters is that Charity is run by good men and women (it’s mostly women who call the shots up there, you know, and you’d be surprised what actually happens behinds those lovely silk curtains they use at the Old Fort…I hope you spent some time there…), that it is a useful and profitable trading partner, and that they keep their corner of the map clean. If you want an opinion on their quality as a neighbour, go talk to the folks at Liberty Hill. Well, don’t talk to Bannit, or do, but don’t talk about Charity. Or well, do, but be prepared for one of his sermons. He’ll talk for thirty minutes about the vices of Charity, all the while scratching his groin, a condition he’s been to Charnel Priory about, but they can’t seem to fix that particular ‘rash’, and I wonder if he hasn’t confused the doors of the Old Fort for those of the Priory, but I’m bordering on heresy at this point, and I’ll remind you that Bannit is a capable shepherd, and leave it at that. But yes, in Liberty Hill, they know that they will never have problems on their border with Charity. It’s as peaceful as a sleeping babe in that crease of our fine dale. But what were we talking about again? Do you like a bit of jam with your cheese?

GFD: That sounds lovely, thank you. Do you mean for me to read between the lines, Mr. Reks?

AAR: With regards to Magistrate Harbaugh? Oh of course; I made the whole thing up about him going to Charnel Priory. Not the itch though, he does seem to scratch a lot. I think the most logical explanation for that is all the hugging he does with pilgrims. Half of them have lice, and the other half have something worse half the time. But that is the sacrifice we make to provide hands-on pastoral care, isn’t it? He really is a master of it. I think he genuinely enjoys it. Maybe too much…

GFD: I was asking about Charity, though, not Bannit. I’ve met him. He is a good man. He does itch a bit, as you say, though. Still…

AAR: Ha! I hoped others would catch that! Well, not ‘catch it’ catch it. I wouldn’t wish lice on anyone. He really should ask Troia her secrets though. I’ve never seen a single probing finger of hers out of place, and she shakes more hands than the doorknobs of the Cathedral. But she’ll have me skinned alive if I say anything more, so we’ll move on. You’re asking me if I mean for you to read between the lines with regards to Charity. And to that I say, “No sir, Charity is a fine neighbour of the dale, providing peace, superb wool, steel and other trade goods, and the finest entertainment you can get for more than two hundred miles. Nothing to see here, except the girls and boys at the Old Fort.” To wit, I recommend Bailey Buxom (I think her last name is actually ‘Bottom’, which is a naturally wonderful name for a woman in her line of work anyway, but her natural assets made for an obviously different nom-de-guerre) in the former case, and Tommy Timber in the latter, and many have thanked me for the recommendations, though not Madame Rowan, who I think ought to.

GFD: You mean Medea Rowan? The Madame of the Old Fort?
AAR: The very same. She should thank me, and should have thanked Gale too, but that’s another matter entirely, or not entirely, but, well, Gale was complicated, and twice as right half the time as most of us. Which reminds me that Ferguson too, ought to thank Gale by name. Afterall, it was Gale’s dedication (and impetuousness, let’s be honest) that found his boots leaping into Avernus itself, and the Chancellor ought to have a statue of that man made. Oh, and Shea and Abigail too. By all the gods, I sincerely, and I mean this, you scribbling clockwork thing, I sincerely hope their souls are in good order. But in matters such as those, I am out of my depth, and I believe you are out of time, our dinner tonight before your departure notwithstanding. Let’s to our victuals and fellowship, and leave the matter of politics and souls alone for the rest of the night, shall we?

GFD Notes: And that was the end of that. Reks was right that I was out of time. I was to head out in the morning with a caravan headed through Cormyr, then find passage back to the Sword Coast. As it was, I held the caravan up from leaving until noon, and why they didn’t leave without my wine-drenched self is something I think Reks had a sly hand in. So, what remains at Charity is vague, though under control, and not worth the hassle to disrupt. By Reks’ accounting at any rate. If I had time, I’d ask Bishop Whitegate, and intend to do so some other time.
-GFD

DDC – Chapter Seven – Forword and Summary
Wherein the Current State of Daggerdale, Her Neighbours and Other Interested Parties are Inventoried

So you’ve gotten this far, Fair Reader! Far enough to begin reading about your own very chapter in the chronicle. It is but ¼ written, and I look forward to hearing about the deeds of heroes who will write the rest.

This ‘chapter’, such as it is, will be brief. It is a collection of seemingly dissociated works, notes and correspondences that provide as much of a first-hand account of the status of various people, groups and places that are likely to be involved later this chapter. You will learn more about each of them in the entries that follow, but here is a tidy summary of nouns that will serve you well to know;
xx




DDC – 1482 – 1: Current State of the White Cloaks
An inventory of licenses, team members and real estate held by the famous heroes of Daggerdale.
GFD Notes:
Even in Waterdeep, so far away from the Dales, I have heard tales of the White Cloaks sung in taverns by itinerant bards. Not that it happens every evening, mind you. But when it does, I take note. The efforts of these brave men and women are legendary, and continue to mount. The people of Daggerdale, as one curmudgeon once told me in a taproom in Shadowdale, “…never knew peace up there. Probably never will.” And so, heroes must grow their songs, or evil will prevail.

As I hope you’ve read so far, fair reader, evil has not prevailed, and in our times, we have the White Cloaks to sing of; descendants by some degree of earlier heroes, tied together with the bonds of bravery, victory and loss, their songs will grow as their enemies diminish.

Now I should say that the account below was given to me mostly by Administrator Reks, with some modifications that were required by my hand. I feel it is fairly accurate, wanting only for intelligence on selected members, for whom many others also desire closure.
Perhaps the next generation of heroes will provide this for us…
-GFD

Charters
The White Cloaks have operated under Charter of the Castle since 1479. This has allowed them to hold property in Castle Radiance (White Cloak Tower), and to pursue bounties as ‘Preferred Agents’ (they get their pick, along with the Redjacks and some other smaller groups).

In Elesias of 1482, Daggerdale underwent formal reorganization during a major summit called the Governors’ Assembly (c.f. DDC – 1482 – 10). The Assembly is dealt with in greater detail later in this chronicle, but here it is important to note that the White Cloaks were granted a Charter Militant, recognizing them as a formal part of the defense of the dale, and granting them a seat on the General Assembly.

Active Duty Teams
Mountain Team – Made up mostly of the more senior (and durable) members, this team is based out of White Cloak Tower at Castle Radiance, and is usually ranging in the mountains, foothills and plains of Netheril

1. Iolus Warburton - Captain – Soldier of Amaunator – candidate for the Order of the Lambent Shield, which he regularly turns down
2. Corran Altair - Sergeant – Paladin of Torm, Order of the Golden Lion
3. Drake Sterling – Accomplished soldier from outside the dale
4. Artorias Brave – From the Watchtower Order – accomplished shield specialist and devil hunter

Tethyamar Team – As the name suggests, stationed in Yarl Orgen’s Hall in Tethyamar. Made up of all the members of the team suited to subterranean adventure.
5. Vanion Creed – Sergeant – Accomplished soldier from outside the dale
6. Mr. Bollinger – Human, male, Artificer
7. Durandal – Human, male, strange fighter
8. Guggenheim Thorbardson – Dwarven male - Subterranean beast master


Heartland Team – Formerly ‘Bravo Team’ and made up of the more versatile members of the White Cloaks, this team will respond to threats anywhere in the heartland and is the busiest of the teams.
9. Hennigan Paros - Sergeant – An accomplished soldier from Luruar
10. Ganolen Thendolain – Accomplished soldier from within the dale
11. Imogen Mystral – Accomplished soldier from Foothills Farm
12. Bastian Swift – A cousin to Tuugan and accomplished soldier of the dale.


Other Members
13. Alen Reks – ‘Administrator’ – Also, Lord of Loedegan Close
14. Troia Trustar – Sergeant – Leads diplomatic and fact-finding missions around the dale and recently, further abroad. (Invoker of Sune)

15. Alystair Dretch - Sergeant – Usually acts independently, but often accompanies Troia on her diplomatic missions

Inactive Members
16. Lumina Whitegate - Retired - Residing in Liberty Hill.
17. Tuugan Swift – Retired – Residing at Crossed Blades Farm (can be coerced out of retirement from time-to-time)
18. Magistrate Banitt Harbaugh - Retired – Magistrate of Liberty Hill
19. Rhuun of Thunder – Absent Without Leave
20. Sorashana – Banished from Daggerdale by Zenith Lord Argent Whitegate – Current whereabouts unknown

21. Nathan Gale – Gunslinger from the Sword Coast, member of Order of the Tome – Missing and presumed dead (c.f. DDC – 1481 – 17: Report from Sgt. Paros)

22. Shea the Avenger – Zealous warrior of Amaunator, local girl from Gribbons’ Farm – Missing and presumed dead

23. Abigail Dran Quilan – Rashemi Witch – Missing and presumed dead (possibly related to Maevri Dran Quilan – c.f. DDC – 1372 -1)


Real Holdings

Loedegan Close (Daggerfalls)
This is one of the ancestral homes of the Whitegate Family and was gifted to the White Cloaks by Luminous Whitegate, for their efforts in ending the Dark Garden threat in 1481. ‘The Close’, as it is called, is a stately home in Daggerfalls, and is the de facto headquarters of the White Cloaks, now that there are three teams operating in different arenas.

The Close serves as an orphanage, there usually being 10-20 children of various ages living and learning there. The Close is currently presided over by Lady Hasting Blackmane, Steward of the Close. She educates the children and overseas the general operation of the estate.

It should be noted that the estate previous to the Dark Garden and the escalation of the war with Netheril in 1480/81 was quite opulent. However, in order to pay for the mercenaries needed to fight Netheril, the Whitegate family sold off nearly everything of value in the house. While still a large and stately home, it is austere inside, usually dark and cold.

The Heartland Team calls the Close ‘home’ and can sometimes be found here. Administrator Reks lives in the Close and is rumoured to never leave the gates of the estate. Despite the austerity of the place, it is rumoured that a great store of treasures and magic, accumulated by the White Cloaks, is hidden deep within the estate somewhere.

The estate is made up of three buildings; the main house, a fine brick stables, and a large servants’ house. These three buildings, along with one brick wall form a courtyard. Most of the White Cloaks keep a room in the guest building, while only the Administrator stays in the main house (which functions as the orphanage and school). The main house has a fine tower at the top of which is an aviary for messenger doves.
White Cloak Tower (Castle Radiance)

This is one of the main defensive structures of Castle Radiance, being on the Western Bailey exterior wall, facing west towards the plains of Netheril. It is a squat tower of 4 stories, thick-walled and serviceable. The White Cloaks have had a lease on the tower since receiving their Charter of the Castle in 1479.

This tower is the home of the Mountain Team, and is where the captain of the White Cloaks can be found when not ranging in the mountains and plains.

The first floor serves as a hostel and public kitchen. Newcomers to the Castle can stay and eat here for free, though donations are accepted. This space has functioned as a recruiting centre for the teams as well, with many notable members starting their career as a White Cloak here. Troia can often be found cooking and serving food here when she is at the Castle.

The second and third floors are the quarters for the teams, which (I am told) include a training room, a small library, a small workshop, and several bedrooms.

The fourth floor is a mainly defensive structure that can also be accessed by the battlements on either side of it, as well as an aviary for messenger doves.

The steward of the tower is a young lady named Lesia Goering, the daughter of the former mayor of Liberty Hill. Her mother was one of the main conspirators with the Dark Garden, herself a daughter of Belladonna. Lesia appears to be free of the taint of Shar but is happy to be cloistered up on the Castle, away from her ancestral home. Undoubtedly, Luminous is happy to have her close and under observation.
Arwencroft (Charity Hills Farm)
This is a stately row-home in Charity. It was gifted to the White Cloaks even before their arrival at Charity by Basil Muloch, who registered it as being ‘Assigned for the usage of the White Cloaks as they see fit, until such times as they deem their efforts in Charity are no longer needed, even if that be to the end of days’.

The home itself is in the style of Charity, which mimics that of Westgate; it is narrow, deep and tall, and finely appointed with leaded glass, light fixtures, wrought iron and fine millwork. The ground floor on the street-side has a small office in which their steward, Flora Scarlett (a local woman in her early 20’s) can usually be found. Flora does triple-duty as the steward of the estate, the land-lord for some renters, and a gatherer of intelligence for the White Cloaks.

This property comes with a tax liability that is accounted for by 4 small apartments on the first floor that are rented out to Freemen of the town. The 2nd and 3rd floors are kept by the White Cloaks, but are usually empty. It is rumoured that they keep emergency supplies there. There are no teams headquartered at Arwencroft, but there is room for a dozen people if needed.
Yarl Orgen’s Hall (Tethyamar)
A good-size hall adjacent to Thorbardson’s Hall, this space has been granted to the White Cloaks by the Silver Council of Tethyamar at the Governor’s Assembly, as a reward for the efforts of the team in the depths. Though I have not seen it myself, I have seen a map that Reks keeps posted on the wall of his study (he seems somewhat obsessed with the place, but tells me he’s never been). It is about 200’ long,

and is much like a street with rooms and mezzanines on both sides. It looks as though you could accommodate a small army in the space. It has been granted completely free of encumbrances by the Silver Council in perpetuity.

This of course is the headquarters for the Tethyamar Team, currently lead by Sgt. Creed. It is widely rumoured that a great store of treasure is hidden in Yarl Orgen’s Hall, the legal spoils of exploration and re-conquest of the lower halls. When asked about this, Reks replied ‘I don’t know that I’d use the word ‘great’ to describe the treasure’.
DDC – 1482 – 10: Excerpts from The Daggerdale Concordat, 1482 DR.
The decree crafted and agreed upon at the Governors’ Assembly of Elesias, 1482, wherein the current political entity of Daggerdale was established.
GFD Notes:
This document is quite easy to find, but I include a copy of it herein for posterity, in the event that it is not easy to find in subsequent ages. This is a legal document that lays out the relationship between the various settlements in Daggerdale, entrenches religious pluralism, and defines the common defence strategy and obligations of the signatories.

If anyone wants my opinion on the matter, and you are reading it, after all, this was driven by the church of Amaunator, who desired more than anything else, a strategy for the common defense, and a budget which they didn’t carry the lion’s share of.

Their Sunblades and the Order of the Lambent Shield had protected the dale at their own cost for nearly 80 years, but the war with Netheril and others had been costly, and they now required partners to share that cost.

I was fortunate to have been invited to the Tower to watch the proceedings from the Gallery, and for the most part, this Governors’ Assembly went smoothly. There were some raised concerns and voices over the shared cost of the troops and their command structure, and some small boundary disputes, but relative to similar proceedings in other regions, there seemed to be something near to consensus on almost all issues.

I suppose this amiable governance is the result of having so many determined enemies for so long, and there being little prospect for true peace in the near future, though I do wish it for them.
-GFD


Preamble & Superseding Rights
In any matters addressed by and prescribed for in this Concordat, The Concordat shall be held to be the governing document, superseding any provision in other agreements of any variety, on those specific matters. The Concordat is not a prescription for how the Signatories and their people are to carry out

their daily lives, but rather, what obligations and limit to obligations they owe to each other. In all respects save Religious Pluralism, the Concordat neither prescribes nor proscribes specific behaviours.
Signatories – As of 15 Elesias, 1482 DR.
There being two classifications of Signatory to the Concordat, namely;
Voting Signatories, which shall have the right to attend the Governors’ Assembly and vote upon matters brought before it, which now includes;
• The Mayor of Dagger Falls
• The Governors of Dwimmerholm Farm, Gribbons’ Farm, Mystral Grove Farm, Crossed Blades Farm, Liberty Hill Farm, Lostead Farm, Foothills Farm, Tesh Valley Farm & Daggerford Farm

• The Ambassador of the Council of Silver in Tethyamar, until such time as a King is declared for the dwarves, and that king shall appoint his or her member to this body

• The Ambassador of Charity, or other such representative, as prescribed by their Royal Assembly from time-to-time

• The Ambassador from Myth Drannor, or other such representative, as prescribed by that Nation from time-to-time

• The Ambassador from Cormanthor, or other such representative, as prescribed by that Nation from time-to-time

• The Lord of Castle Radiance, who reserves the right to have his interests represented by and his vote cast by proxy by,
• The Bishop (Amaunator) of Dagger Falls
• The High Cultivar of Chauntea, or other such representative, as prescribed by that Faith from time-to-time

• Other such governors or ambassadors for new settlements or proximal allies, that shall be voted in by a majority of four-fifths from time-to-time
GFD Notes:
The Ambassador for Myth Drannor is usually absent, but does correspond by messenger, and sometimes sends a proxy for meetings, but for the most part has been an observer with relatively little input.

The “Ambassador from Cormanthor” is a customary position of old in the Dale. There is no longer a unified organization of the Green Elves of Cormanthor since the 14th Century, post Spell-Plague.
-GFD


Non Voting Signatories, which shall have the right to attend the General Assembly and vote upon matters brought before it, which will, if passed by the General Assembly, be brought to the Governors’ Assembly for ratification, which now includes;
• The General of the Sunblades
• The Lord Commander of the Order of the Lambent Shield

• Three Magistrates from the Church of Amaunator, as chosen by that Faith
• Three Cultivars from the Church of Chauntea, as chosen by that Faith
• The Captain of the White Cloaks
• The Captain of the Redjacks
• The Captain of the Free Defense League
• The Ambassador from Candlekeep Emissaries
• The Ambassador from the Cormyrean Embassy
• The Master of the Merchant’s League in Dagger Falls
• The Master of the Labourers League in Dagger Falls
• The Nuncio of the All Faiths League in Dagger Falls
• Other such members as the Voting Signatories vote in by four-fifths majority from time-to-time
Consul of the Governors’ Assembly
The Voting Signatories will elect a Consul of the Governors’ Assembly at the beginning of this agreement, and every Shieldmeet thereafter. The Consul shall be chosen from any citizen of the dale, but shall not be a Voting Signatory or Non Voting Signatory to the Concordat. The Consul shall call the Assembly and maintain order during proceedings and act as the head of the Sun Blades.

The first Consul of the Governors’ Assembly, elected by unanimous agreement by all Voting Signatories, shall be Cpt. Kesh Oakdale (ret.) late of the 16th Company Sunblades, of Dwimmerholme Farm, whose first term shall commence on 15 Elesias, 1482 DR, and end on Shieldmeet, 1484 DR.

For his service as Consul, Cpt. Oakdale will be provided with apartments in Governor’s Hall (Dagger Falls), a yearly salary of 300 gp, 100 gp in discretionary administrative funds each year, and one aide to be paid 182 gp 5 sp per year, of his choosing.
Provisions for the Common Defense – The Sunblades
All settlements, nations and other organizations represented by the Voting Signatories agree that the defense of their holdings and people is primarily their responsibility, and further, that a common defense strategy with a Standing Army deployed strategically throughout the dale will be to the mutual benefit of all. Therefore, the Voting Signatories now support the reorganization of the Sun Blades along the following framework;
Chain of Command
1. Consul of the Governors’ Assembly
2. General
3. Captains
4. Lieutenants
5. Sergeants
Captains and Lieutenants can be assigned to answer to Governors in such circumstances that warrant this arrangement. This does not supersede any orders by the General, but is an arrangement of convenience for seeing to the local needs of specific settlements.

Standard Order of the Sunblades

• General (18 companies, 54 platoons, 1296 soldiers plus officers)
o Staff: Quartermasters, Intelligence, Attendants (9)
o Captain of the Castle (4 companies, 12 platoons, 288 soldiers)
• 4 Lieutenants with 1 company each (4 companies)
• 3 Sergeants with 1 platoon each (12 platoons)
o Each Platoon is 24 soldiers (288 soldiers)
o Captain of the Town (4 companies, 12 platoons, 288 soldiers)
• 4 Lieutenants with 1 company each (4 companies)
• 3 Sergeants with 1 platoon each (12 platoons)
o Each Platoon is 24 soldiers (288 soldiers)
o Captain of the Rides (2 companies, 6 platoons, 144 mounted soldiers)
• 2 Lieutenants with 1 company each (2 companies)
• 3 Sergeants with 1 platoon each (6 platoons)
o Each Platoon is 24 soldiers (144 soldiers)
o Captain of the Recruits (4 companies, 12 platoons, 288 soldiers – all in training)
• 4 Lieutenants with 1 company each (4 companies)
• 3 Sergeants with 1 platoon each (12 platoons)
o Each Platoon is 24 soldiers (288 soldiers – all in training)
o Captain of the South Settlements (1 company, 3 platoons, 72 soldiers)
• 1 Lieutenant with 1 company (1 company)
• 3 Sergeants with 1 platoon each (3 platoons)
o Each Platoon is 24 soldiers (72 soldiers)
o Captain of the Near Settlements (1 company, 3 platoons, 72 soldiers)
• 1 Lieutenant with 1 company (1 company)
• 3 Sergeants with 1 platoon each (3 platoons)
o Each Platoon is 24 soldiers (72 soldiers)
o Captain of the West Settlements (1 company, 3 platoons, 72 soldiers)
• 1 Lieutenant with 1 company (1 company)
• 3 Sergeants with 1 platoon each (3 platoons)
o Each Platoon is 24 soldiers (72 soldiers)
o Captain of the Reserve (1 company, 3 platoons, 72 soldiers)
• 1 Lieutenant with 1 company (1 company)
• 3 Sergeants with 1 platoon each (3 platoons)
o Each Platoon is 24 soldiers (72 soldiers)

Costs and Contributions
The costs of one soldier are;
182 gp/year in wages (at a rate of 5 sp/day in wages paid to that soldier every tenday)

24 gp/year in rations (payable in-kind by the settlement that solder is stationed at, if possible) 36 gp/year in lodging (payable in-kind by the settlement that soldier is stationed at, if possible)

8 gp/year in stabling for his or her mount-share (with one mount for every other soldier, payable in-kind by the settlement that solider is stationed at, if possible)

12 gp/year in feed for his or her mount-share (with one mount for every other soldier, payable in-kind by the settlement that solider is stationed at, if possible)
8 gp/year for armour, weapons and supplies
The total cost for one year for one soldier being 270 gp, 80 gp of which can be paid in-kind.
The costs of one platoon are:
24 soldiers at 270 gp each, totalling 6,480 gp, 1,920 gp of which can be paid in-kind

1 sergeant, with costs the same as a soldier, but with a rate of 6 sp/day in wages, or 307 gp/year, 80 gp of which can be paid in-kind
25 gp/year in administrative costs
The total cost for one year for one platoon being 6,812 gp, 2,000 gp of which are payable in- kind.
The costs of one company are:
3 platoons at 6,812 gp each, totalling 20,436 gp, 6,000 of which can be paid in-kind

1 lieutenant, with costs the same as a solider, but with a rate of 7 sp/day in wages, or 343.5 gp, 80 gp of which are payable in-kind.
100 gp/year in administrative costs
The total cost for one year for one companying being 20,879.5 gp, 6,080 gp of which are payable in-kind.

Each settlement at which a company is deployed will pay the price in coin or kind for those companies. As well, each settlement will pay the price in coin of the common companies, those being 2 companies of Rides, 4 companies of Recruits, and 1 company of Reserve (7 companies in total), according to the following shares;
Castle Radiance – 4 shares Dagger Falls – 4 shares
Each Farm – 1 share each for a total of 9 shares Charity – 1 share
Kingdom of Tethyamar – 1 share Kingdom of Cormyr – 1 share
For a total of 20 shares. The total cost for 7 companies being 146,156.5 gp/year, each share is 7,308 gp/year payable in coin.

Provisions for the Common Defense – Order of the Lambent Shield & Other Holy Orders For the greatest clarity, the holy orders of knights, paladins, and other warriors, priests and staff will be paid for entirely by their Churches, and will extract no mandatory payments from the people of Daggerdale. Holy orders may be granted a Charter Militant by four-fifths majority vote in the Governors’ Assembly as needed from time-to-time. The following Holy Orders are hereby granted a Charter Militant at the outset of the Concordat:
The Order of the Lambent Shield (Amaunator) The Order of the Golden Lion (Torm)
The Order of the Lambent Rose (Ilmater) The Knights of Justice (Tyr)
Provisions for the Common Defense – The Charters Militant
For the greatest clarity, the companies of independent soldiers, scholars, adventurers, and others who would commit themselves to the defense of the dale, at their own expense and peril, will extract no mandatory payments from the people of Daggerdale. However, they shall be granted by four-fifths majority vote of the Governors’ Assembly, their Charter Militant, which provides them with the following rights and privileges, so long as they keep their Charter Militant in good order:

To recruit, arm and train individuals whom the Governors’ Assembly finds to be of suitable character and fibre, for the purposes of defending the dale and of making a living and a profit

To hold such properties needed to conduct their business as the Governors Assembly finds suitable, and declares the specifics of such properties in the Charter Militant
To hold a seat on the General Assembly
Each Charter Militant will be reviewed in advance of each Shieldmeet, whereupon it shall require approval by three-fifths majority of the Governors’ Assembly for the next 4 years, until the next Shieldmeet.
Provisions for the Common Defense – The Militia
It being in the best interest of all Signatories to the Concordat that every Signatory provides defense in adequate measure to avoid becoming a liability to the Common Defense, all Signatories agree that:

All fighting-aged and capable people of their settlements are trained in their defense, with drills and training and other such suitable preparations to be conducted at least 4 times per year for 2 full days, and further that,

Each farm will conscript or have volunteers to form a Militia that will be composed of fighting- aged and capable people with the following considerations;

That one-fifth of all fighting-aged and capable people will be enrolled into the Militia at any one time for a period of not less than 4 years per person

That members of the Militia drill and train for at least 2 hours per tenday either under local martial leaders or alongside the Sunblades

That the militia may engage in their vocational duties with a minimum of disruption caused by their martial duties

That at least one full-time Captain of Militia is chosen to lead the Militia, whose duties are exclusively martial rather than vocational, and paid for by the settlement

The signatories of Daggerfalls, Castle Radiance, Charity, and all ally-nations (those currently being Tethyamar, Cormyr, Myth Drannor and Cormanthor) agree to maintain such suitable defenses, standing armies and militia required for their own defense, and for the provision of mutual-defense of the dale

An attack on one Signatory is to be considered an attack on all Signatories, with due consequences, which may include the deployment of Milia to neighbouring Signatories to aid in the Common Defense


Religious Pluralism
The Signatories of the Concordat acknowledge that the worship of many gods in Daggerdale is acceptable, and that the list of acceptable gods may change from time-to-time. To that end, the Signatories will maintain two lists of gods, namely;

Approbia Dei, being the gods that all citizens of the dale are entitled to worship free of restraint, which shall be edited from time-to-time by the Voting Signatories with four-fifths majority, and which at the outset of the Concordat includes;

All such elven deities as approved by the Ambassador from Myth Drannor All such dwarven deities as approved by the Ambassador from Tethyamar The gods of men and their exarchs including:

Amaunator, who shall only be removed from the Approbia Dei by unanimous vote of the Voting Signatories

Chauntea, who shall only be removed from the Approbia Dei by unanimous vote of the Voting Signatories
Torm Ilmater Mielikki Waukeen Selune Sune

Tymora Oghma Gond Tempus
Approbium Dei, being the gods that are forbidden from worship in the dale, which shall be edited from time-to-time by the Voting Signatories with four-fifths majority, and which at the outset of the Concordat includes;

All such elven deities as disapproved by the Ambassador from Myth Drannor All such dwarven deities as disapproved by the Ambassador from Tethyamar The gods of men and their exarchs including:

Shar, who shall only be removed from the Approbium Dei by unanimous vote of the Voting Signatories
Bane Lolth
Ghaunadaur Asmodeus Cyric Gruumsh
In respect to all other gods and exarchs, the Voting Signatories give the ecumenical authorities of the dale to right to bring forth such other gods and exarchs for consideration for the Approbia Dei or Approbium Dei, from time-to-time.

DDC – 1482 – 3: Daggerdale Gazetteer
Being the only such document about the dale from Our Century. GFD Notes:
We come now to a primary source completely of my own making. Compiled in the style of Volothamp Geddarm’s famous encyclopedic accounts of other remote places, I was inspired to put together as tidy a summary as I could summon. A great deal of the information below is from the Yellow Abbey Booke of Surveys and Measures, 1481 edition (the 1482 edition was not published before I left), but the rest is all from my first-hand experience in the dale.

I have done my best to remain unbiased in my accounting below, but before you furl your brow and proceed to read askance on account of the very mention of bias, let me say that the people, the forest, the mountains, the farms, the rivers, lakes and the very air of the place were such a delight to the senses, that I think I may be guilty only of a pastoral bias. The numbers, names and themes from the dale have had a hard accounting, and I am sure you’ll profit by them.

I will begin, if you don’t mind, by sharing a ballad I heard about the dales while I was a young man. It stuck with me, and now I wonder if there isn’t a bit of old Jonstan the Rover in me.
-GFD



Clippety-cloppety, bold Jonstan the Rover Rides misty-eyed down to the Dales again Into forests and fields, rare beauty all over, Land of his true loves – Aldee, Imthra, and Luthane,
Elda and Myrta, Chalantha and Araine

Will he find yet another? Or be welcomed back? Long lasses aplenty catch his winking eye.

Is it kisses he’ll taste soon? Or scorn everlasting? Love and laughter and soon away Jonstan will fly-
Gone again over threshold and under dawn sky.

Far across Faerûn, a rover adventures free ‘Till the Dales call his heart home again To Jhaele, Sharune, Aleese and Rythree-
Warm arms and hearth and a roof ‘gainst rain

‘Till his wandering feet bear him away again.

Climbing far mountains, riding in high clover To Waterdeep and the shores of the Shining Sea-

“Hark! Comes now bold Jonstan the Rover? Will he, oh will he ever come back to me?” The Dales call back the man wedded but free.

Clipppety-cloppety, bold Jonstan the Rover Comes riding down into the Dales again. Their forests and fields, rare beauty all over,

His true love more than all the maidens in pain. My man is riding mist-eyed to the Dales again.

-Jaladha Tshamryl, Minstrel of Battledale, “Jonstan the Rover”

Geography
As Volothamp wrote in 1367:
“If the gods were more disposed to smile on the Dales, this pretty wooded Dale (once known as Merrydale before a tragic infestation of vampires changed its people’s character) could well be the most popular destination for hunters in all the Dragon Reach. Its rolling hills are only lightly settled and teem with game of all sorts. Streams and unspoiled ponds are everywhere , and one can see in this pleasant land many ferny bowers, caverns, and picturesque ruined cottages.”

Although much has changed in the last 100 or so years, that description still holds, with now some exceptions for large settlements, and the great forest of Cormanthor doing its best to hedge them in.

Daggerdale is nestled deep within Cormanthor, a forest which is now rumoured to be full of Feywild Passages, which unwary travelers may not realize they have traversed. The forest is mostly composed of Cormanthor Oak, a thick-trunked leggy tree that often grows to over 60’ in height and diameter. In many parts of the forest, the trees grow at about five-times the rate one would expect, which means a very rich supply of lumber for the area, but also a constant struggle to keep fields and roads cleared.

Deep Cormanthor

To the west of the dale are the Desertsmouth Mountains, unchanged in

name even though the desert of Anuaroch has now been transformed into the emerald fields of Netheril. It is the will of those in Daggerdale that Netheril return to the Shadowfell, and perhaps they are keeping the name of the mountains in hope of their victory over a much greater foe. The mountains could be described as medium-sized, with many high enough to be snow-covered throughout the year, but without the glaciers and other extreme elevation features seen in larger ranges to the north.

Much of Daggerdale has been settled in the Tesh Valley, a rich-soiled valley that cradles the great river that comes down from the mountains to the west, and eventually finds its way to the Moonsea far to the east.

To the south and east of Daggerdale are the Dagger Hills; a maze-like network of hills and small limestone cliffs and caves that has been swallowing up explorers for centuries. In the current era, Cormanthor has swallowed up the hills as well, adding to the confusion and danger of travel there. The hills are rich in ores, and in bygone eras men and dwarves attempted to mine these riches, but today the hills are home only to goblins (as far as intelligent beings go), and scores of different types of monsters. Owlbears, large spiders, stirges, wolves and dire wolves are but a small sampling of the dangers (or exciting hunting opportunities, depending on your vocation) to be found there.

Politics
In our era, the settlements of Daggerdale are nearly entirely large walled villages the locals call ‘farms’, though they are more like fortresses, complete with a standing army (more on that below). Surrounded by large well-kept fields, the ‘farms’ typically command a hilltop from which they can see anyone approaching for nearly a mile. Of course, this is made possible only by a constant effort to cut back the encroaching forest, but the prevalence of the church of Chauntea in the region makes this task a bit easier.

The people of Daggerdale have always been described as dour, but I find that generalization to be either outdated or perhaps unfair. Although they take their security seriously (getting into Dagger Falls involves answering a lot of questions from ‘magistrates’ that feel more like inquisitors to me), the people are friendly, if a little aloof. Travelers to the region can expect friendly nods from the locals, but little in the way of conversation unless pressed. There are exceptions, of course, and many of the inns would be considered comfortable and well-appointed anywhere I’ve been, and the company friendly if not lively.

As of 1482, Daggerdale is governed by a Governors’ Assembly, which is composed of members from each farm, the prominent churches, and significant allies (more on those, below). This Assembly is the closest thing to a regional government in the dales and is largely the result of the strength of the Church of Amaunator in the area, and their desire to organize a common defense and the payment thereof.

Each individual settlement elects a Governor by its own custom, and these governors meet semi- regularly in Dagger Falls to discuss the defense of the dale. This is a new organization, but it is made up of very successful organizations that preceded it.

Beneath the Governor’s Assembly is the General Assembly, which is made up of many different groups, religious, business, labour, and adventuring companies, and it meets regularly to propose rules and actions for the Governors’ Assembly. Overall, the dale is run very well, and has been for over 50 years.

The day-to-day governance of Dagger Falls is headed by the office of Mayor. It is worth noting that this office never had a formal election process, clearly defined duties, compensation or clearly written authority. Until the Daggerdale Concordat, this position was something of a ceremonial honorarium, as the town’s defence and other matters were handled by various other organizations. However, the Concordat clearly defines all of these things, and formally acknowledged Lilly Cassimar as the current Mayor. Mayor Cassimar is a friendly woman of means, who enjoys hosting large dinners at her family home in the centre of the town. She is a dedicated Sunite and is known for her stunning appearance but even more stunning manners, patience and kindness.
Prominent Religions
There are two main religions which essentially run the dale; the Church of Amaunator, and the Church of Chauntea.

The Church of Amaunator is headed by a Zenith Lord, currently Argent Whitegate, currently residing in Castle Radiance in the mountains. The Zenith Lord is primarily concerned with countering the evil of Netheril, and as such is located as close as safely possible to Netheril. The church is effectively run by the Bishop of Dagger Falls, currently Blaze Whitegate (grand-nephew to Argent), who resides in the Cathedral. Beneath the Bishop are the magistrates of the dale, who have a complicated hierarchy and disparate duties. The term ‘magistrate’ could mean anything from a country church priest to a

dangerous inquisitor. The Church has an impressive institute of learning called the Yellow Abbey, which is adjacent to the Cathedral of Dagger Falls. This is a seminary for new priests and magistrates, as well as a grammar school for children as old as 18. The Yellow Abbey has a library called the Historic Wing, which is a repository of secret and semi-secret writings that is difficult to gain entry to.

The Church of Amaunator had two military branches, until 1482; the Order of the Lambent Shield (an order of Paladins and other holy warriors), and the Sunblades. After the Daggerdale Concordat (Elesias, 1482 DR), the administration and cost of the Sunblades was passed onto the Governors’ Assembly, but the ranks are still filled with many worshipers of the Sun God, including most

of the officers. The Sun Blades can be seen on every settlement and road in the dale, and are usually friendly, though some are accompanied by zealous inquisitors who will ask many uncomfortable questions of new travelers. The Lambent Shield is usually deployed from Castle Radiance, postured against the military might of Netheril.

It should be said that most people in the dale speak well of the prosperity that Amaunator has brought, especially as delivered by the Whitegate Family, who grew the religion and the defense of the dale for decades. Though the

family is nearly extinct now, after a terrible battle with a villainous group of druids known as the Dark Garden, some of the highest-ranking positions in the dale are still held by the few remaining old men of the family.

The Church of Chauntea is something you will find in every dale, and Daggerdale is no exception. Every farm has a large flock of worshipers, and the Church’s position in the dale is enshrined in the new Concordat that ensures it a voting seat in the Governors’ Assembly.

Though not as well organized or hierarchic as the Amaunatori of the dale, the Chaunteans do have a functioning network that allows them to share information and work together

with their neighbours. The head of the church is chosen every year after the Greengrass Festival, which is one of the highlights of the year for all members of

Symbol of Chauntea in
Daggerdale

the dale (it is quite lively and oftentimes licentious) and carries the title of High Cultivar. The rest of the clergy are simply called ‘Cultivars’, which could represent a neophyte priestess, or an accomplished arch-priestess. The clergy are mostly female, but the body of the church itself is evenly split between males and females.

The current High Cultivar is Madeleine Oakdale, of Crossed Blades farm. ‘Maddy’ as she prefers to be called spends only a tenday per month in Daggerfalls (the third tenday is when the Governors’ Assembly sits), but is otherwise found on her farm where she remains the head of her faith.

Many other gods are worshiped publicly or privately in the dale, and an approved list of these gods can be found posted in Dagger Falls, and in many of the border-settlements of the dale. The Approbia Dei as it is known, is also publicly posted along with outlawed gods on a list known as the Approbium Dei.
Military
As mentioned in the section on Religion, the Sunblades can be found just about everywhere in the dale. This organization is made up of platoons of 24 soldiers lead by a sergeant. Three platoons make up a Company, lead by a lieutenant. Divisions are composed of 1 to 4 companies and are lead by captains.

The captains in turn are lead by General Dauntless Thunderstorm, who is the head of all 18 Companies of Sunblades, or roughly 1200 soldiers plus officers.

At every farm and other settlement you will find a platoon or more of Sunblades. They are typically dressed in chain shirts, trained to fight well with swords and axes, and every other man bears a heavy shield and is trained in the defense of the men adjacent to him. These platoons are the elite core of the defense of the dale and are actively involved in the training of the Militia, which is many times the size of the Sunblades.

In every settlement, you will find that a high proportion of men and women of able body are trained in their defense, with arms nearby to address sudden threats. Though not considered a ‘regular standing army’, many an invader to the dale has learned the hard way that these men and women are far from green conscripts. The young women of the dale are infamously dangerous with short bows, which they use for sport and entertainment as well as defense, and the men are all deadly with axes, both swung and thrown.

The Amaunatori Knights known as the Order of the Lambent Shield, lead by High Commander Luminous Whitegate, are rarely seen in the heartland of the dale. They are stationed in Castle Radiance and are typically deployed on the front with Netheril. This is one of the most battle-hardened fighting forces in Faerun in Our Time, by many estimations, with even the lowest ranking men and women being veterans of scores of major battles. Typically found dressed in half plate armour and wielding magical longswords, these men and women also display a high degree of individualism in their gear and tactics.
Allies & Enemies
Daggerdale’s first and most reliable allies are its neighbours. Shadowdale is the only dale with what could be considered a shared border with Daggerdale, and although in bygone centuries relations were tepid at best between them, these two dales conduct a great deal of trade between themselves and will quickly jump to defend each other when needed.

The Kingdom of Tethyamar, which is undergoing rediscovery and reorganization is a very strong ally and trading partner, and indeed holds a seat on the Governors’ Assembly. At the time of writing this, a little over 1,000 dwarves have come to the area to reclaim the halls of their ancestral home, but more than half have chosen to stay living above ground, in some of the settlements of the Dalesmen.

The elves of Myth Drannor are a true ally, although their operating timeframe makes them seem aloof to the common folk of the dale. Holding a seat on the Governors’ Assembly as well, they are rarely in attendance, as they are busy with their own struggle against their enemies both ancient and new. They have not made a notable military contribution to Daggerdale in the last 10 years or so, their absence from the escalating war with Netheril and the Dark Garden noticed and commented upon by many who bled at those battles. What is not fully understood by any but the most well-informed diplomats of the dale is that the efforts of the elves of Myth Drannor make a tangible contribution to the war with Netheril, and are likely responsible for that great enemy not having the strength to overrun Daggerdale on a whim.

The Kingdom of Cormyr has long been involved in the politics of Daggerdale. In the 14th century, the Cormaeril family had a claim to the rulership of the dale, though that was short lived (dying with William Cormaeril in the late 1390’s). Today, Cormyr is an ally of necessity, as they both share a devious and

determined enemy in Netheril. Cormyr essentially provides a bulwark against Netheril for the south- western portion of the dales, and similar to Myth Drannor, siphons off enough of Netheril’s might to keep them from overrunning smaller enemies. An embassy from Cormyr Drannor used to be located at Castle Radiance until the Concordat of ’82, at which time it was moved to Dagger Falls. A small garrison of Purple Dragons can be found at the Embassy in town, and a larger force of 12 Knights and 120 regulars are stationed at the Castle, sharing the defense against Netheril.

The primary foe of the dale is Netheril, and specifically one of the Twelve Princes of Shade, Melagaunt. Melagaunt has been tasked with taking command of Daggerdale but has been unable to do so. While he has many agents, chief among them is his ‘Curator’, Loki Mouvranesh. Mouvranesh is an accomplished spy and sorcerer and has been the author of many devious plots against the Dalesmen. In recent years, she supported the Dark Garden coven in their plot to overthrow the dale, as well as the brutal cult known as the Sons of Bel. While the Dark Garden was defeated utterly in 1480, many of the instigators from the Sons of Bel escaped justice and remain at-large, whether within the dale or without, none I’ve met can say.

Like many nearby polities, Daggerdale has constant low-intensity conflict with organized and semi- organized groups of demihumans, such as the orcs that issue from the Desertsmouth Mountains, tribes of goblins from the Daggerhills, and Hobgoblins from the northern reaches of Cormanthor.

Of old, the chief enemy of the dale were the Zhentarim. The events of the late 14th century put an end to the Black Network’s hold over the dale, and especially over Dagger Falls (which it held fast for many years), but we again hear of trading costers coming out of places like Voonlar, Hillsfar, Yulash and Teshwave. Although merchants from these costers claim that they are a peaceful lot that have simply been identified as ‘Zhentish’ due to their “Moonsea-ish looks and bearing”, some names from the past have re-emerged; one such coster is Company Drurginz, which recently annexed the ancient and storied Shield Trading Company in Voonlar. Now operating as Company Drurginz, it has reconnected routes from Sembia to Waterdeep for the first time more than a century.

Many local adventuring companies could also be considered ‘allies’, though some more appropriately could be labelled ‘mercenaries’. The Free Defense League, lead by Captain Bargle Battlemaster, is headquartered at Castle Radiance, and has nearly 40 members who take ‘bounties’ posted at the castle (these are often related to orcs and Netherese scouting parties that the Lambent Shield doesn’t have the time to deal with).

Another, the Redjacks, is lead by the prickly Hastle Redwater, a veteran of dozens of campaigns. His Redjacks number more than 60, and are very capable, if somewhat self-interested, soldiers and adventurers. The Redjacks have a tower at Castle Radiance where they also take bounties, and now have a new lodge in Dagger Falls, from where they hope to grow their footprint in the dale.

Finally, the famous White Cloaks round out the largest of the private companies. This is the youngest of the three organizations but is the fastest-growing and has had the most spectacular successes (and failures too, though those tend to not make any songs). Their victories against the Dark Garden and the Sons of Bel have cemented a place for them in the hearts and lore of the dale. Ostensibly allied with the Church of Amaunator, they permit members of all faiths on the Approbia Dei. I give a full accounting of their holdings and roster in the Dagger Dale Chronicle (c.f. DDC – 1481 – 1), but it is worth repeating here that they are lead by Captain Iolus Warburton, a paladin of Amaunator and native of a now-

abandoned farm to the north of the Falls. The White Cloaks hold many properties, including estates in Dagger Falls (Loedegan Close), Charity (Arwencroft), Tethyamar (Jarl Orgen’s Hall) and Castle Radiance (White Cloak Tower).

Demographics
In most of other parts of Faerun in Our Time, it is impossible to say how many people live in one place or another. This is not so in Daggerdale, as the Yellow Abbey conducts a census every year in every major settlement. The following table has been reproduced from the Yellow Abbeye Booke of Surveys and Measures, 1481 DR.
